# Changelog

All notable changes to Health Assistant are documented in this file.

The format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/),
and this project adheres to [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html).

> **Workflow:** every user-facing change adds a line under `## [Unreleased]` at
> commit time (see [docs/RELEASE_PROCESS.md](docs/RELEASE_PROCESS.md)). At release
> time, `## [Unreleased]` is renamed to `## [vX.Y.Z] - YYYY-MM-DD` and a fresh
> `## [Unreleased]` is opened above it.

## [Unreleased]

- **Feature: first-run setup wizard (browser-based admin bootstrap) + `/auth/register` locked to invite-only.** Eliminates the single biggest install UX cliff — creating the first admin previously required `docker compose exec … create_system_admin.py`. Now a fresh install is detected automatically: visiting the app URL redirects to a **setup wizard** (`/setup`) where you pick the admin email, password, and organization name, and you're logged in immediately. **Backend:** new `GET /auth/setup-status` (returns `{initialized, setup_token_required}` — drives the login-vs-setup redirect) and `POST /auth/setup` (the only bootstrap path — creates the initial tenant + `SYSTEM_ADMIN`, returns login tokens). **First-claim race closed:** on boot, if the DB has zero users, a one-time **setup token** is generated and printed to the backend container logs; the wizard requires it for non-localhost/non-dev requests so a stranger can't claim an internet-exposed fresh instance before the owner. Localhost and dev deployments skip the token. New `app/core/setup_token.py` (in-memory token — the backend is a single HTTP process; move to Redis if multi-worker HTTP ever lands). `POST /auth/register` is now **invite-only** — the open no-`tenant_id` bootstrap branch is removed (moved into `/auth/setup`); every registration requires a `tenant_id` + valid invite token. This also removes the "anyone can create a tenant as ADMIN" hole that existed on every later registration. The advisory-lock race protection from the old register path is preserved in `/auth/setup` (re-check inside the lock). **Frontend:** new `pages/Auth/Setup.tsx` wizard (organization name, email, password+confirm, conditional setup-token field with the `docker compose logs … grep` retrieval hint); `Login.tsx` now calls `setup-status` on mount and redirects to `/setup` when uninitialized, and the dead `<Link to="/register">` (no such route/page ever existed) is replaced with an invite-only note; `/setup` route added to `App.tsx` unauthenticated block; `api/axios.ts` no-token-warning exclusion list updated. **Breaking:** the `POST /auth/register` no-`tenant_id` bootstrap path no longer exists — any client relying on it must use `POST /auth/setup` (first-run) or invite tokens (subsequent users). **Tests:** new `tests/test_auth_setup.py` (10 tests — setup-status variants, happy-path SYSTEM_ADMIN creation + token return, 410/403/409 guards, advisory-lock acquisition, register-lockdown); `test_auth.py::test_register_success` rewritten as `test_setup_success` against the new endpoint; `test_auth_register_isolation.py` lost its three register-bootstrap tests (moved to setup) and gained the invite-only contract docstring. All 33 auth tests pass; 531 frontend tests pass; tsc + eslint clean. **Docs:** `INSTALL.md` step 6 now leads with the wizard (CLI demoted to a "Headless / automation" callout), First-Time Sign-In rewritten, and a `grep "setup token"` snippet added; `README.md` quick start updated; `GETTING_STARTED_GUIDE.md` §1 references the wizard as the first-login experience. `create_system_admin.py` is unchanged and remains the IaC/automation path.

- **Docs: restructured `docs/INSTALL.md` + new `docs/GETTING_STARTED_GUIDE.md` (end-user walkthrough).** INSTALL.md had several defects that tripped first-time installers, all fixed in this pass. **(1) Step 7 URL bug** — "Access the application" pointed at `http://localhost:3000` (the dev port) and `http://localhost:8000/docs`, but the standalone compose serves everything behind Nginx on port 80; corrected to `http://localhost` (UI), `/docs` (Swagger), `/health`, and `/flower/`, with a note pointing bring-your-own-proxy / dev users to the right ports. **(2) Credentials story** — there are *no* default login credentials (by design; the operator chooses them via `create_system_admin.py --email … --password …`), but the docs never said so. Added an explicit callout in step 6 stating the `admin@example.com`/`securepassword` values are placeholders, you log in with whatever you passed, and the script's argparse fallbacks (`sysadmin@health-assistant.local` / `admin123`) apply only if you run it bare. **(3) Anatomy digression split out** — the ~40-line "Anatomy Graph Expansion Packs" block (JSON schema, CLI flags, AI sub-graph generation) sat inside Quick Start step 6 and derailed the boot-the-app flow; moved to a new `## Optional: anatomy expansion packs` appendix at the end, with a one-line pointer left in step 6. **(4) "Updates" rewritten for Docker** — the section described `git pull && pip install` in a venv (the contributor flow), not the Docker path the quickstart uses; replaced with the `git pull → setup_env.py (if needed) → compose pull → compose up -d` sequence, with the venv path demoted to a clearly-labelled "From source (development)" subsection. **(5) "First-Time Setup & Linking" split into two real bootstrap paths** — the old section conflated `create_system_admin.py` (direct DB write, SYSTEM_ADMIN + named tenant) with the open-registration path; rewrote as "Path A — the admin script" vs "Path B — open registration (first registrant bootstraps a tenant as SYSTEM_ADMIN)". Dropped "Household Tenant" positioning prose (→ "a new tenant", audience-neutral per the docs skill). **(6) Misc cleanup** — removed the redundant "Configuration" section (restated step 4); folded the Redis health-check bug-confession into a one-line note; gave the dangling `certbot` code blocks a `#### TLS with Let's Encrypt` heading under the Security Checklist; consolidated the fragmented single-command Troubleshooting code blocks; fixed the API-docs URL in the old Support block; added a `## See also`. **(7) README consistency** — `README.md` quick start used `--tenant "My Household"` (positioning drift) while INSTALL.md used `--tenant "My Organization"`; aligned both to "My Organization" and added a no-default-credentials note pointing at INSTALL.md. **New doc:** `docs/GETTING_STARTED_GUIDE.md` — a task-oriented end-user guide that picks up where INSTALL.md leaves off (the install gets you to a login screen; this gets you through the first hour of actually using the app). Covers sign-in & roles, the per-person context switcher + creating/linking the active person, optional LLM setup (`/settings/ai-config`), uploading a lab report with the OCR/extraction pipeline, creating an examination, reading biomarker trends, tracking medications/vaccinations/allergies (catalog-vs-instance distinction), starting a health journey, connecting a wearable (`/settings/integrations`), the propose-never-writes AI assistant + Magic Fill, and personalization (PWA, draggable dashboard, notifications, languages). Includes two mermaid diagrams: a "first-hour" flowchart of the recommended step order, and a sequence diagram of the upload → Celery → LLM → review-card pipeline. All routes/paths verified against the frontend router (`frontend/src/App.tsx`) and sidebar (`Sidebar.tsx`). Registered in `docs/docs-tree.json` under "Getting Started" between Installation and Architecture. Follows the docs skill positioning rules (Beta, no HIPAA/GDPR claims, FHIR stated-not-leading, AI always paired with the human-in-the-loop wall). Every shell command in both docs is now in its own fenced block (one command per ```bash fence) so the website's per-block copy button copies a single, paste-ready command — no multi-command blocks remain.

- **Frontend: shared `CodingSystemSelect` + single coding-systems registry (DRY).** The coding-system dropdown was reimplemented in every form that needs one — `VaccineForm` used a plain free-text input (no dropdown at all), `BiomarkerForm` and `ClinicalEventForm` hardcoded `<option>` lists, and `AnatomyForm` + `ConceptForm` each declared their own local `const CODING_SYSTEMS = [...]` array (which had already drifted: anatomy offered LOINC, concept offered MeSH/FMA, etc.). **New single source of truth:** `config/codingSystems.ts` — one registry of nine systems (LOINC, SNOMED CT, CVX, ICD-10, ATC, RxNorm, MeSH, FMA, custom), each with its label, canonical FHIR `system` URL, and hint, plus a `CODING_SYSTEMS_BY_DOMAIN` map (biomarker / vaccine / clinical_event / medication / anatomy / concept) so each entity surfaces only the systems relevant to it (vaccines default to CVX, anatomy now correctly offers SNOMED/FMA instead of LOINC, concepts offer the full set). Helpers: `getCodingSystem`, `getCodingSystemsForDomain`, `getCodingSystemLabel`. **New component:** `components/ui/CodingSystemSelect.tsx` — a `<select>` bound to the registry via a `domain` prop (or explicit `systems`), with `includeEmpty` for nullable fields and a `className` override so each form keeps its own look while the option *list* stays shared. **Refactored all five forms** to use it: `VaccineForm` (now a proper CVX dropdown), `BiomarkerForm`, `ConceptForm`, `AnatomyForm`, and `ClinicalEventForm` (keeps its chunky styled chrome + chevron; only the option list is shared). Removed the two local `CODING_SYSTEMS` constants and three hardcoded `<option>` blocks. Also removed the free-text "Target Diseases" input from the patient-instance vaccination "define new" panel — disease association is a **catalog** concern expressed through the knowledge graph (`PREVENTS` edges via `<LinksSection srcType="immunization">` and the seeded `kind=disease` concepts), not free text on a patient dose. tsc + eslint clean; 531 frontend tests pass.

- **Frontend + Backend: vaccinations page overhaul — modular form/card/modal aligned with the Medication pattern, plus examination linking.** The vaccinations page was a bare-bones list with a hand-rolled modal and a custom vaccine dropdown that bypassed the shared picker infrastructure. Rewritten to mirror `MedicationList`/`MedicationModal`/`MedicationCard`, composing existing primitives instead of reimplementing them. **New modular package `components/vaccinations/`:** `VaccinationForm` (self-contained header/body/footer like `MedicationForm`) now picks the vaccine via the **`CatalogItemPicker`** (single, type `vaccine`, cards mode) with an inline "Define new vaccine" flow (creates a catalog entry through `createCatalogItem('vaccine', …)`), and links the visit via **`InstanceField`** (single, type `examination`) — the "instance selector" the form was missing; `VaccinationModal` hosts the form in the shared `<Modal>` and owns the API writes (add/edit immunization, optional catalog creation, and graph-link persistence via `createLinksFor('immunization', …)` after the record commits); `VaccinationCard` mirrors `MedicationCard` (icon tile, status badge, portal action menu with Edit/Delete/Open-in-catalog); `vaccinationStatus.ts` is the single source of truth for status badge/tile colours; barrel `index.ts`. **Page rewrite (`pages/Vaccinations/VaccinationList.tsx`):** status filter (all/completed/not-done/entered-in-error), grid/list view toggle, completed-vs-other grouping, "Open Catalog" button (`/catalogs?type=vaccine`), `?new=vaccination` create-intent, full `t()` i18n. **Schema fields now exposed in the form** (previously missing): `status`, `manufacturer`, `location`, `note`, plus `examination_id` and `dose_number`/`lot_number`/`administered_at`. **Backend:** added `examination_id` (FK → `examinations.id`, `ON DELETE CASCADE`) to `PatientImmunization` — model + `to_dict()` + FHIR R4 `Immunization.encounter` projection (mirrors `fhir_medications.examination_id`); wired through `PatientImmunizationCreate`/`Update` schemas + `vaccine_service`; Alembic migration `v1a2c3c4i5n6` (chains off head `n1o2t3i4f5y6`). **i18n:** new `vaccinations` namespace in en + el. **Tests:** 2 new backend tests (model-level FHIR encounter projection + endpoint create→read→clear round-trip for `examination_id`); 13 vaccine tests pass; tsc + eslint + ruff clean.

- **Frontend: catalog list strips rich-text markup from descriptions (HTML/Markdown → plain text).** The catalog item list (`CatalogBrowser`, used by both the workspace list pane and the picker-browse modal) rendered `item.description` as a raw string — so a description stored as HTML (`<p>Take with food</p>`) or Markdown (`**Take twice daily**`) showed the tags/markers as literal characters in the row. **Fix:** both the list and grid/card modes now pass the description through `toPlainText(item.description)` before rendering, producing a clean single-line snippet (CSS `line-clamp-2` still handles visual truncation). This is plain-text only — no formatted prose in the list, matching the compact-row contract (formatted prose stays in `CatalogItemCard` and `CatalogItemInfo` via `FormattedText`). **Enabler:** extended `toPlainText` in `utils/textFormat.ts` to also strip Markdown — previously it only stripped HTML and left Markdown markers (`**`, `#`, `-`, `[]()`) intact (a documented limitation). Markdown is now parsed to HTML via `marked` (already a dependency) then the existing DOM-based strip handles both formats in one pass. `toSnippet` (which wraps `toPlainText`) inherits the improvement, so `InstanceCard`, `examinationAdapter`, `eventAdapter`, and other compact-snippet callers also strip Markdown now. Widened `toPlainText`'s param type to `unknown` for the polymorphic `CatalogItem` shape (field values are loosely typed). 512 tests pass; tsc + eslint clean.

- **Fix: portalled popovers hidden behind six custom-rolled modals (z-index).** The relation-type dropdown (`RelationTypeSelect`, `z-popover` = 1050) opened behind the modal in the AI chat HITL "define" proposal form — its portalled popover painted *under* the form content instead of on top. Root cause: six modals that bypass the shared `<Modal>` component (`z-modal` = 1000) hardcoded `z-[1100]` (= 1100, same as `z-drawer`) for their overlay, defeating the codebase-wide contract that portalled popovers (`z-popover` = 1050) float above modals. Since 1050 < 1100, *any* popover or nested detail-modal opened inside these modals was hidden. **Fix:** changed all six overlays from the `z-[1100]` magic number to the canonical `z-modal` token — `HitlTaskModal` (the reported surface), `AIToolsModal`, `ChatInspector`, `CreateBiomarkerModal`, `ExaminationUpload` (preview spinner), `ExaminationGroupManager` (preview spinner). Now 1050 > 1000 holds everywhere and the shared `<Modal>`/custom-modal behavior is consistent. The AI drawer (`z-[550]` range) and toasts (`z-toast` = 1200) are unaffected. `tsc --noEmit` + eslint clean (the 9 lint warnings in `ExaminationUpload.tsx` are pre-existing `useEffect`-dep warnings, unrelated).

- **Frontend: catalog picker/relations UX pass — dropdown no longer clips, selected items show their type + formatted fields.** Three related fixes to the components backing catalog "Related items" editing (`RelationTypeSelect`, `LinksSection`, `CatalogRelationsEditor`, `CatalogItemCard`). **(1) Fixed the relation-type dropdown being clipped at the viewport/modal bottom edge.** `RelationTypeSelect` always opened below its trigger (`top: rect.bottom + 4`), so a chip near the bottom of a form/modal had its dropdown cut off. Added a `placement` state (`'top'|'bottom'`) computed in the positioning `useLayoutEffect`: when `spaceBelow < ~340px` and `spaceAbove` is larger, the popover flips above the trigger, anchored via CSS `bottom` (distance from viewport bottom) so it grows upward without needing a measured height. Mirrors the existing `CitationButton.tsx` flip pattern. Animation direction also flips (`slide-in-from-bottom-1` vs `slide-in-from-top-1`). **(2) Switched `<LinksSection>` (create/edit forms) and `<CatalogRelationsEditor>` (edit-mode, existing item) to `displayMode="cards"`.** Previously both rendered picks as compact chips, where the relation dropdown *replaced* the type chip — so the user couldn't see whether a picked related item was a medication, biomarker, concept, etc. The existing `CatalogItemCard` (purpose-built for this, with type icon + type label + name + scope + key fields, and an `actions` slot that `CatalogItemPicker` already wired the relation dropdown into) is now used in both surfaces. Edit mode and create/edit forms are now consistent. **(3) `CatalogItemCard` richtext fields now render as formatted prose.** Replaced the `toSnippet(raw, 160)` plain-text collapse with `<FormattedText>` (the auto-detecting renderer already used by the full `CatalogItemInfo` detail view — detects HTML/Markdown/plain via `detectTextFormat` and renders with `prose-sm` styling). A `max-h-28 overflow-hidden` cap keeps the compact card bounded; full text remains one click away via the card's "open in catalog" button. `tsc --noEmit` + eslint clean.

- **Docs: aligned `docs/AI_SYSTEM.md` + `docs/API.md` with the link-proposal system + catalog/instance tool rename.** Two doc files updated to reflect the link-proposal + rename work shipped earlier on this branch. **(1) `docs/AI_SYSTEM.md`** — added two paragraphs after the task-types table: a "Catalog vs instance disambiguation" paragraph explaining the system-prompt section that pairs the `define_*` / `prescribe_*` / `record_*` verbs with trigger phrases; and a "Link proposals (create + link in one confirmation)" paragraph documenting the optional `links[]` parameter on four `propose_*` tools, the `LINK_SCHEMA` single-source-of-truth matrix in `app/ai/tools/propose_link.py`, the drop-and-report validator (`build_link_specs`), the `get_link_schema` LLM tool, and the frontend `<LinksSection>` + `GET /api/v1/concept-edges/schema` UI discovery path. **(2) `docs/API.md`** — added a row to the `concept-edges` endpoint table for `GET /concept-edges/schema?src_type=&dst_type=`: pure-metadata discovery (no DB hit, no tenancy), returns the matrix slice in one of three shapes (full list / per-source map / per-pair list), powers the LLM `get_link_schema` tool + the frontend `<LinksSection>` dropdown filter. **Skills updated locally (gitignored)**: `.opencode/skills/ai-pipeline/SKILL.md` (tool list with new names + `get_link_schema`; new `propose_link.py` module section; tool count 24→25; CATALOG-vs-INSTANCE note; `GET /concept-edges/schema` endpoint §6.3), `.opencode/skills/hitl-task-cards/SKILL.md` (recipe §3 split into "catalog form pattern" vs "ClinicalEventForm pattern"; example uses `propose_prescribe_medication`; new link-proposal wiring note), `.opencode/skills/clinical-data/SKILL.md` (resolver coverage 7/11 → 11/11; new `LINK_SCHEMA` paragraph), `.opencode/skills/frontend/SKILL.md` (catalog forms section: `typeMeta` now optional; new "Single source of truth per concept" + "Graph links via `<LinksSection>`" paragraphs; new shared-infrastructure bullet list for `conceptEdges.ts` / `useLinkSchema` / `CatalogItemPicker.getRelationsForType` / `filterRelationGroups`).

- **Fix: "Related items" section appeared twice in catalog create forms.** After the previous form consolidation (which moved `<LinksSection>` INTO each catalog form), the `CatalogWorkspace` was still rendering its own external `<LinksSection>` for create mode — so users saw two identical sections stacked. Root cause: when I moved the section into the forms in the consolidation commit, I forgot to remove the workspace's external instance. **Fix:** removed the workspace's external `<LinksSection>` (and its now-unused `LinksSection` import — `createLinksFor` + `selectionsToLinkInputs` stay because `performSave` still uses them). The form-internal `<LinksSection>` is the single source of truth, fed by `values.links` / `onChange({links: next})`. **Bonus:** added `<LinksSection>` to the four remaining catalog forms (`AllergyForm` srcType='allergy', `VaccineForm` srcType='immunization', `AnatomyForm` srcType='anatomy', `ConceptForm` srcType='concept') so every catalog type gets the same "Related items" UX in both the workspace create flow AND the HITL propose flows. Each catalog form now owns its own `<LinksSection>` driven by the LINK_SCHEMA `srcType` for that concept. **Verified:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; 512 frontend tests pass; eslint clean.

- **Refactor: one form per catalog type (single source of truth).** Eliminates the long-standing form drift between the catalog-workspace create flow and the HITL "Define X" proposal flow. **Before:** `catalog/forms/MedicationForm.tsx` (controlled, `CatalogItemFormProps`) for the workspace, `patients/MedicationDefinitionForm.tsx` (uncontrolled, `prefill`+`onSubmit`) for HITL — same `MedicationCatalog` row created two different ways, with different field types (RichTextField vs plain textarea), different state models, and after Phase 3 different feature sets (only the HITL form had `<LinksSection>`). Same drift existed for biomarker (`catalog/forms/BiomarkerForm.tsx` vs `examinations/BiomarkerDefinitionForm.tsx`). The HITL skill explicitly calls this out as wrong: "The form rendered inside the modal must be a separate, headless component… ClinicalEventForm is the canonical example — it is shared by both the manual ClinicalEventModal and the HITL HitlTaskModal." **Now:** the catalog forms (`catalog/forms/*.tsx`) are the single source of truth. The catalog-workspace pattern (`CatalogItemFormProps: {values, onChange, mode}` — controlled, no internal state) wins because 5 forms already use it (medication, biomarker, allergy, vaccine, concept, anatomy), the workspace infrastructure (audit, scope, history, save) is built around it, and it composes better than `prefill`+`onSubmit`. **Changes:** (1) `<LinksSection srcType="medication">` moved into `catalog/forms/MedicationForm.tsx` — driven by `values.links` / `onChange({links: next})`. The catalog workspace already wires this through Phase 3's `editing.links` stash, so it just works for the manual create flow too. (2) Same for `catalog/forms/BiomarkerForm.tsx` with `srcType="biomarker"`. (3) `typeMeta` made optional in `CatalogItemFormProps` (catalog forms don't actually read it — only the workspace passes it). (4) `CreateMedicationDefinitionHandler` rewritten to manage draft state + render `<MedicationForm values={draft} onChange={...} mode="create" />` + own footer (cancel/reject/submit). (5) Same for `CreateBiomarkerDefinitionHandler`. (6) `CreateBiomarkerModal` (the legacy examinations-page manual create flow) rewritten to use `<BiomarkerForm>` too — was the third silent entry point. (7) **Deleted** `patients/MedicationDefinitionForm.tsx` and `examinations/BiomarkerDefinitionForm.tsx` (the old HITL-only forms). Net: -740 LOC of duplicated form chrome, +1 single source of truth per concept. **Behavior preserved:** AI-assist button on the catalog form is deferred (was on the HITL form only; will return as a catalog-forms-wide feature in a follow-up). The patient-prescription `MedicationForm` at `components/patients/MedicationForm.tsx` is **unchanged** — it's a different concern (prescribes a drug to a patient, has dosage/frequency fields). **Verified:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; 512 frontend tests pass; eslint clean.

- **AI HITL: wire `<LinksSection>` into create forms (Phase 3 of the `propose-link-hitl` plan).** Connects the Phase-1 backend (AI proposes links in a single `propose_*` call) and Phase-2 frontend (`<LinksSection>` component) into the actual user-facing forms so the long-promised "create X AND its links in one confirmation" UX finally works. **Six surfaces touched: (1) `MedicationDefinitionForm`** — gained a `links` field in prefill + payload and renders `<LinksSection srcType="medication">` after primary fields (collapses when the matrix offers no destinations). **(2) `CreateMedicationDefinitionHandler`** — `proposalToPrefill` maps the backend's `{dst, relation, properties, duplicate_of}` snapshot to `CatalogSelection[]`; `handleConfirm` calls `createLinksFor('medication', created.id, links)` after `addCustomMedication` returns the new id; per-link `{ok, edge_id?, error?}` results aggregated into the `resolveHitlTask` audit payload + `onResolved` card state. **(3) `BiomarkerDefinitionForm` + (4) `CreateBiomarkerDefinitionHandler`** — same pattern with `srcType="biomarker"`; the `links` field is stripped before calling `biomarkerService.createBiomarker` (the create endpoint doesn't know about it; we persist edges separately). **(5) `MedicationForm` + (6) `CreateMedicationHandler`** (patient prescription) — same pattern; the AI's `propose_prescribe_medication` tool attaches links to the resolved **catalog entry** (the drug), not the prescription row. The handler persists links via `createLinksFor('medication', catalog_id, links)` using the resolved catalog_id (existing OR newly-created via `createCatalogItem` when `is_new_catalog_entry`). **CatalogWorkspace:** the catalog create modal's hardcoded "Save the item first, then you can add relations." placeholder is gone. Create mode now renders `<LinksSection srcType={active.edge_endpoint_type}>` driven by the catalog descriptor, with the selections stashed on the draft (`editing.links`). `performSave` calls `createLinksFor(active.edge_endpoint_type, savedId, links)` after the primary create returns `savedId`. Edit mode is unchanged — `CatalogRelationsEditor` still handles it (loads + persists edges immediately, which is correct for an existing row). **Summary chips:** each HITL `renderSummary` now appends a `<LinksSection mode="summary">` block under the primary chips when the proposal carried links, so the compact chat card shows what's being linked at a glance. **i18n:** new `ai_chat.hitl.links.*` keys added to both `en/common.json` and `el/common.json` (section title, search placeholder, empty/error states, "Link exists" badge). **ClinicalEventForm integration deliberately skipped:** the LINK_SCHEMA's `clinical_event_type` rows apply to the event TYPE (a catalog row), not the event INSTANCE the user creates in this flow; the semantics of attaching links to an instance via this flow are unclear and worth a separate design pass. **Verified:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; 512 frontend tests pass; eslint clean on every touched file.

- **Fix: medication citation 404 when AI references a catalog entry.** Hovering a `[Ref: medication=<uuid>]` chip produced `GET /api/v1/medications/<uuid> → 404` whenever the UUID referenced a catalog definition (returned by `search_medications` / `get_medication_catalog_details`) rather than a patient prescription. Root cause: medication is the only citation type with a dual nature — the same `[Ref: medication=...]` syntax covers both patient prescriptions (`fhir_medications`, fetched via `/medications/<id>`) AND catalog definitions (`medication_catalog`, fetched via `/medications/catalog/<id>`) — but `CitationButton` only knew about the instance endpoint. The AI's catalog-side tools emit catalog IDs, so any chat answer that cited catalog details 404'd on hover. Fix: `CitationButton.tsx` now tries the instance endpoint first, falls back to the catalog endpoint on 404, and tracks which kind was resolved in a new `citationKind` state. Navigation routes accordingly — the existing `/medications/details/<id>` for prescriptions, the catalog workspace (`/catalogs?type=medication&item=<id>`) for catalog entries. Both navigation paths (the inline `handleOpenOriginal` and the `getEntityUrl` helper) updated. Other citation types (observation, biomarker, examination, event, document) are unambiguous and unchanged. Defensive layer — fixes the symptom regardless of which tool the AI used; future AI-prompt improvements to disambiguate citation types won't be blocked by this fix. All 512 frontend tests pass; tsc + eslint clean.

- **Fix: spurious Quill "Cannot register 'bullet'" warning on catalog create forms.** The compact `RichTextEditor` config listed `'bullet'` as a format — but Quill doesn't have a `'bullet'` format; bullet lists are the `'list'` format with the value `'bullet'` (configured via the toolbar's `{ 'list': 'bullet' }` button, which was already correct). Removed the bogus entry from `compactFormats` in `frontend/src/components/ui/RichTextEditor.tsx`. The warning surfaced in the console every time a catalog create form opened (`CatalogWorkspace > onNew > MedicationForm > RichTextField > RichTextEditor compact`). Bullet-list functionality was already working (it goes through the `'list'` format) — the warning was just Quill's registry complaining about an unknown name in the formats config. The full-mode `formats` array was already correct (lists `'list'` + `'indent'`, no `'bullet'`). One-line fix; tsc + 512 frontend tests still pass.

- **AI HITL: shared frontend for link proposals (Phase 2 of the `propose-link-hitl` plan).** Lands the frontend half of the modular link-proposal system so the existing create-forms can grow a "Related items" section in Phase 3. Four new files plus two small extensions to existing components; no behavior change for end users yet (Phase 3 wires it into the forms). **(1) `frontend/src/services/conceptEdges.ts` (new)** — thin client over `/concept-edges/*`: `getLinkSchema(srcType?, dstType?)` overloaded to return the matrix slice for any of the three shapes the backend endpoint emits (full / per-source / per-pair), `createLinksFor(srcType, srcId, links[], opts?)` that loops `createEdge` per link and collects a per-link `{ok, edge_id?, error?}` result so a single hit doesn't abort the loop, and `selectionsToLinkInputs(selections)` — the canonical mapping from the picker's `CatalogSelection[]` to the service's `LinkInput[]` (kept as a named export so the form doesn't duplicate the conversion). Default write opts: `source='ai', status='approved', tenant_scoped=true` — matching the HITL "human is the approval" contract. **(2) `frontend/src/hooks/useLinkSchema.ts` (new)** — module-level cached discovery hook. First mount pays the network cost; every subsequent mount (across any form in the session) reads synchronously from the cache. Two access modes via overload: `useLinkSchema()` returns the full matrix as `LinkSchemaRow[]`; `useLinkSchema('medication')` returns the per-source projection as `Record<dst_type, relations[]>` (derived client-side from the cached full matrix, so asking for a new srcType doesn't re-fetch). Failed fetches clear the cached promise so the next mount retries. Test-only `_resetLinkSchemaCacheForTests` is exported for unit-test isolation. **(3) `frontend/src/components/catalog/catalogRelationTypes.ts`** — adds `filterRelationGroups(groups, allowed)` to filter the global `RELATION_OPTION_GROUPS` to a subset of relation values. Used by the per-destination-type relation dropdown filter so a `medication→concept` chip shows only TREATS/CONTRAINDICATES/INDICATES/RISK_OF (etc.) instead of the full 19-relation list. **(4) `frontend/src/components/catalog/CatalogItemPicker.tsx`** — adds an optional `getRelationsForType?(catalogType) => RelationOptionGroup[] | undefined` prop. When provided, each chip's `<RelationTypeSelect>` shows only the relations valid for THAT chip's destination type (e.g. medication→concept vs medication→biomarker show different relation lists). Falls back to the global `relationPicker.options` / `RELATION_OPTION_GROUPS` when not provided or when the callback returns undefined — existing callers (`CatalogRelationsEditor`) are unchanged. The change is two `useMemo`-free inline per-chip reads, kept in the chips-mode AND cards-mode branches. **(5) `frontend/src/components/ai/hitl/LinksSection.tsx` (new)** — thin wrapper around `CatalogItemPicker` (relation mode) that uses `useLinkSchema(srcType)` to discover which destinations are valid for the form's primary entity, restricts `allowedTypes` accordingly, and feeds `getRelationsForType` to the picker for per-chip relation filtering. A form declares only `srcType="medication"` and `<LinksSection>` auto-renders every destination the matrix allows — no per-form link-catalog knowledge. Three modes: `'editable'` (default — full picker), `'summary'` (read-only chips for the HITL card), `'readonly'` (reserved alias for future denser layouts). Endpoint-type normalisation handled internally (`vaccine` ↔ `immunization`); non-catalog endpoint types the matrix might advertise (observation, doctor, examination, document) are hidden from the picker today since no instance-picker is available for them. The form owns the state (`value` / `onChange`); persistence happens in the form's `onSubmit` via `createLinksFor` AFTER the primary create returns — `<LinksSection>` itself never persists. **Tests:** 7 new in `services/conceptEdges.test.ts` — `getLinkSchema` URL construction for the 3 overloads, `createLinksFor` happy-path / per-link-failure-continues / opts-passthrough / empty-input / non-Error-rejection paths, `selectionsToLinkInputs` mapping + relation-stripping. 6 new in `hooks/useLinkSchema.test.ts` — first-mount fetch, per-source projection, cache-across-mounts (single network call for N mounts), error-then-retry, plus `deriveSchemaForSource` pure helper. `vi.hoisted` + `vi.mock` is the right vitest pattern for ESM exports (named-import spies don't intercept; vitest exports are frozen at module-eval). All 512 frontend tests pass; `tsc --noEmit` clean; `eslint` clean on every touched file.

- **AI HITL: renamed `propose_*` tools for catalog-vs-instance clarity (fixes the "create new medication" misrouting).** The user reported that asking the AI to "create a new medication" mis-selected the patient-instance tool (`propose_add_medication` → prescription) when they meant the catalog tool (`propose_create_medication_definition` → drug definition). Three-layer fix at the LLM-facing surface. **(1) Tool function names** — `propose_add_medication` → **`propose_prescribe_medication`**, `propose_create_medication_definition` → **`propose_define_medication`**, `propose_add_biomarker_to_examination` → **`propose_record_biomarker_result`**, `propose_create_biomarker_definition` → **`propose_define_biomarker`**. The new verbs are scope-explicit: "define" = catalog (reference definition), "prescribe"/"record" = patient-instance. The LLM picks a tool by its name + docstring, so this single change fixes the bulk of misrouting. **(2) Cross-referencing docstrings** — every paired tool's docstring now opens with an explicit "Use `propose_define_X` INSTEAD when…" pointer to its sibling, so when the LLM is hovering between two tools the docstring pulls it to the right one. Concrete trigger phrases included ("X isn't in the system yet" → define; "I'm taking X" → prescribe). **(3) System prompt** — new "CATALOG vs INSTANCE" subsection in `prompts.py` `CHAT_SYSTEM_PROMPT` + `GENERAL_CHAT_SYSTEM_PROMPT` that names the two layers, pairs the verbs, lists trigger phrases for each, and tells the LLM to ASK one clarifying question when intent is genuinely ambiguous rather than guess wrong. The MULTI-PROPOSALS example was also updated to use the new `propose_prescribe_medication` / `propose_define_biomarker` names. **Stable contract preserved:** the `task_type` routing strings inside the task payload (`add_medication`, `create_biomarker_definition`, etc.) are **deliberately unchanged** because they are shared with the integration SDK's `proposal_type` discriminator (`integrations/sdk/proposals.py:44-49`) — a future unified review UI depends on that alignment. Only the LLM-facing tool function names were renamed; backend routing, frontend `registry.tsx` keys, integration tests, and the SDK spec are all untouched. Doc comments referencing the old tool names refreshed in `docs/AI_SYSTEM.md` (task-types table gained a "Naming note" callout), `integrations/sdk/catalog.py` + `proposals.py` (docstrings), and three frontend form preface comments (`MedicationDefinitionForm`, `BiomarkerDefinitionForm`, `AddBiomarkerForm`) — purely cosmetic, no functional change. Tests: one reference to the old tool name in `test_ai_history_reconstruct.py:94` updated; `test_catalog_proposal_service.py` docstring refreshed. 56 hitl + catalog-proposal + integration-proposal tests pass; ruff clean; tsc + eslint clean.

- **AI HITL: modular link proposals in create forms (Phase 1 of the `propose-link-hitl` plan; see `dev/plans/propose-link-hitl-2026-07-21.md`).** Lets the AI attach a validated `links[]` payload to any existing `propose_*` tool call so the user creates a primary entity AND its knowledge-graph links to existing catalog items in a single confirmation. Previously "create Metformin AND link it to the disease it TREATS" required two HITL confirmations chained across auto-resume turns; now it's one. **Single source of truth:** `LINK_SCHEMA` in `backend/app/ai/tools/propose_link.py` — a declarative matrix mapping `(src_type, dst_type)` → valid `ConceptRelationType` values. Consumed by (a) `validate_relation_combo` (pure server-side guard), (b) the new `get_link_schema` read tool in `taxonomy.py` (LLM discovery — avoids bloating the system prompt with the 22-relation × 11-endpoint matrix), (c) the new `GET /api/v1/concept-edges/schema?src_type=&dst_type=` REST endpoint (UI discovery), and (d) the frontend `<LinksSection>` component (Phase 2 — filters destination + relation dropdowns from the same matrix via the REST endpoint). A form's "what links it supports" is just `LINK_SCHEMA` filtered by its primary `srcType` — no per-form declaration code. **Orchestrator:** `build_link_specs(db, tenant_id, src_type, raw_links, *, primary_existing_id=None)` validates each LLM-supplied link, resolves the destination endpoint via `resolve_endpoint` (UUID passthrough; slug/name fallback via `catalog_search_service`), and snapshots a `{dst, relation, properties, duplicate_of}` payload into `proposed_payload.links`. Invalid combos are silently dropped (drop-and-report — kept vs dropped count surfaces in the tool result so the LLM self-corrects on the next turn). When the primary already exists, `check_existing_edge` queries `concept_edges` for an existing match so the form can show a "Link exists" badge and skip on submit; when the primary is being newly created, dedup is skipped entirely. **Wired into four existing tools:** `propose_create_clinical_event`, `propose_prescribe_medication` (was `propose_add_medication` — see the rename entry above), `propose_define_biomarker` (was `propose_create_biomarker_definition`), `propose_define_medication` (was `propose_create_medication_definition`) each gained an optional `links: Optional[List[dict]] = None` argument. `propose_record_biomarker_result` (was `propose_add_biomarker_to_examination`) is intentionally untouched (lab-result additions don't carry ontology links — those live on the biomarker definition). **Resolver backfill:** `_resolve_doctors`, `_resolve_observations`, `_resolve_documents` added to `concept_endpoint_resolver.py` — all 11 `EdgeEndpointType` values now have proper labels (previously fell through to the `"{type}:{id-prefix}"` fallback). **Security unchanged from existing HITL pattern:** AI never writes; the form's Approve click triggers `POST /concept-edges` (the canonical RBAC/tenant-scoped endpoint). Three layers of validation: tool-layer matrix, `ConceptEdgeCreate` Pydantic schema, `ConceptService.create_edge` (which also checks concept endpoints exist). No new endpoint for writes; only the metadata `GET /schema`. **Tests:** 24 new in `tests/test_propose_link.py` — `LINK_SCHEMA` integrity (every endpoint + relation references a valid enum, no duplicates, covers the promised combos), `validate_relation_combo` accept/reject paths, `relations_for_*` + `serialize_full_schema` shapes, `build_link_specs` orchestrator (empty input, valid snapshot, invalid relation drop, unknown endpoint drop, malformed entries drop, dedup-when-primary-exists, skip-dedup-when-primary-new, mixed batch), the 4 REST endpoint shapes (full / filter-by-src / filter-by-pair / bad-type 400), and a guard that all 11 endpoint types have registered resolvers. 2265 existing tests still pass (4 pre-existing kind-filter failures on `main` unaffected by this change). ruff clean across all touched files.

- **Docs: aligned public docs with the integrations-sdk-improvements pass (items 1–5).** Doc-only commit — no code, no test impact. Eight files updated to reflect the five improvements that shipped on this branch (rate-limit cooldown, webhook HMAC helpers, document dedup, notification digest, setup config): (1) `docs/INTEGRATIONS_SDK.md` — §3.1 now mentions `IntegrationRateLimitError.retry_after_seconds` propagation; §3.3 documents the new exception field + Redis cooldown contract with a code example; §3.9 builder table gained a `.digest_key(key)` row; §3.10 dedup contract notes that the same pattern now applies to documents; §3.13 `DocumentPull` field list + code example + idempotency section rewritten (was claiming "no document-level dedup columns" — now false); new §3.14 "Webhook Signature Verification (Reusable Helpers)" documents `integrations.sdk.webhook_security`; §3.8 OAuth example `setup(config)` signature widened to `dict | None = None` + `super().setup(config)` call; line 218 "robust HTTP" → "HTTP that retries and maps status codes consistently" (positioning fix per the documentation skill's anti-fluff rule). (2) `docs/INTEGRATIONS_FRAMEWORK.md` — highlight #5 mentions rate-limit cooldown key + updated pipeline; highlight #6 cross-references the new webhook helper module; highlight #13 documents the document-level dedup pattern. (3) `docs/NOTIFICATION_SYSTEM.md` — `notifications` schema row includes `dedup_key?` + `dedup_expires_at?`; `emit()` signature block shows the new kwargs; numbered "emit does" list opens with a step 0 for the dedup-hit short-circuit; new "Digest collapsing (`digest_key`)" subsection; elevated-HR example includes `.digest_key(...)`; operator checklist includes `NOTIFICATION_DEFAULT_DIGEST_TTL_SECONDS`. (4) `docs/STATUS.md` — added a new "Integrations SDK improvements pass" entry under "Completed > Backend" with one sub-bullet per item; fixed the stale "Document-level dedup deferred" sentence in the F+G+C entry. (5) `docs/API.md` — sync-endpoint 429 row notes the cooldown key; webhook row notes the SDK delegation. (6) `docs/FHIR_R4_FACADE.md` — `DocumentReference` row notes the new `meta.tag[]` provenance stamping. (7) `docs/docs-tree.json` — refreshed SEO descriptions for `notification-system`, `integrations-framework`, and `integrations-sdk` to advertise the new capabilities (digest collapsing, rate-limit cooldown, webhook HMAC helpers, document dedup). (8) `integrations/dev_dummy/docs/capabilities.md` — moved 5 of 7 items from "recommendations" to a new "Recently shipped" section (the integrations-sdk-improvements pass closed them); added a `setup(config)` row to the provider-hooks table; updated the notifications + webhook + documents rows to note the new demonstrations.

- **Integrations SDK improvements pass (5 items; plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-improvements-2026-07-21.md`).** Five independent improvements surfaced while expanding `dev_dummy` into a reference implementation. Each shipped as its own commit; full details in the plan. **Item 1 — `retry_after_seconds` on `IntegrationRateLimitError` + worker cooldown:** `integrations/sdk/exceptions.py` gained an optional `retry_after_seconds` field; `integrations/sdk/http.py::_retry_request` captures the last seen `Retry-After` header and propagates it onto the raised exception; `integration_sync_service` exposes three new helpers (`set_rate_limit_cooldown`, `is_rate_limited`, `clear_rate_limit_cooldown`) that write a Redis key `sync_cooldown:{integration_id}` with TTL clamped to [60s, 1h]; `SyncResult.retry_after_seconds` carries the value; the worker skips the integration while the cooldown exists + writes it on a rate-limited sync outcome. Degrades gracefully when Redis is down (logs + falls back to the per-instance `sync_interval` throttle). **Item 2 — webhook HMAC helpers extracted to `integrations/sdk/webhook_security.py`:** `verify_hmac_signature` (constant-time HMAC-SHA256, strips the conventional `sha256=` / `sha256:` prefixes used by GitHub/Slack/Stripe) + `verify_canonical_signature` (the two-way-API canonical form `METHOD\npath\n[timestamp\n]body` with optional ±5min replay-skew window) + `get_signature_header` (case-insensitive lookup over the conventional header names). The endpoint (`app/api/v1/endpoints/integrations.py::_verify_webhook_signature` / `_verify_api_signature`) and the `dev_dummy` provider both rewritten as thin wrappers; behaviour preserved byte-for-byte. Module boundary: imports only stdlib, no `app.*` coupling. **Item 3 — document-level dedup via `source_integration_id` + `external_id`:** `documents` table had no integration-dedup columns; the contract was "providers advance their own cursor" (fragile under crashes; unavailable to webhook-driven ingestion). Migration `d1o2c3u4m5e6` (chains off `g1h2i3t4l5pr`) adds `source_integration_id` (FK → `user_integrations`, ON DELETE SET NULL) + `external_id` + partial unique index `uq_document_integration_dedup` on `(tenant_id, patient_id, source_integration_id, external_id)` — mirrors the pattern on examinations + clinical_events. `document_service.ingest_document_bytes` gains `source_integration_id` + `external_id` kwargs; on dedup hit returns the existing row as-is (no re-file-write, no re-OCR dispatch); race window recovered via IntegrityError. `DocumentPull` SDK spec gains `external_id`; engine wires the integration's own id through automatically. `dev_dummy` now sets `external_id="dev_dummy_demo_report_v1"`. **Item 4 — notification digest collapsing via `dedup_key` + TTL:** `NotificationSpec` gains an optional `digest_key` (provider-supplied); the builder exposes `.digest_key(key)`. Migration `n1o2t3i4f5y6` adds `dedup_key` + `dedup_expires_at` + a non-unique composite index. `notification_service.emit` gains `dedup_key` + `dedup_ttl_seconds` kwargs; before insert it looks up an existing notification with the same key whose `dedup_expires_at` is in the future and returns it as-is (no re-fan-out, no re-push). TTL clamped to [60s, 7d], default 6h, tunable via `settings.NOTIFICATION_DEFAULT_DIGEST_TTL_SECONDS`. Design note: NO unique partial index (Postgres partial indexes can't reference `now()` in the predicate; the TTL semantics require multiple historical rows per key). Engine forwards `spec.digest_key` to `emit`. `dev_dummy` tags the elevated-HR notification with `digest_key="dev_dummy:elevated_heart_rate:patient/{uuid}"` so consecutive syncs collapse. **Item 5 — `setup(config)` gets real `SystemIntegration.global_config`:** `integrations/base.py` widened to `config: dict | None = None`; the registry builds a per-domain config map from `SystemIntegration` rows and forwards each to `provider.setup(system_config)` instead of the legacy empty dict; `dev_dummy` adds a `setup(config)` override (logs the config + calls `super()`) so authors have a copy-paste example. **Verification:** 5 commits, 113 new tests, all 586 integration-related tests pass; ruff clean across every touched file. Plan reference: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-improvements-2026-07-21.md`.

- **Integrations SDK: turned `dev_dummy` into a complete reference implementation exercising every SDK capability.** The `dev_dummy` integration was a thin pull-only demo that left most opt-in hooks undemonstrated — authors writing real integrations had no single place to copy from. This release expands it into the canonical reference. The provider (`integrations/dev_dummy/provider.py`, organised by `§A`–`§P` capability markers) now implements every `BaseHealthProvider` opt-in: `handle_webhook` with HMAC-SHA256 signature verification against the Fernet-encrypted `webhook_secret` config field, `handle_api_request` (a 4-route REST surface: `GET status` / `GET cursor` / `POST reset` / `POST echo`), `supports_tools` + `get_tools` returning two synthetic LangChain `StructuredTool` objects, `supports_clinical_events` + `pull_clinical_events` emitting a sample flu-episode `ClinicalEventCreate` (with `external_id` for engine dedup), `supports_examinations` + `pull_examinations` emitting an annual-checkup `ExaminationCreate`, `supports_catalog_proposals` + `pull_catalog_proposals` auto-applying a "Sleep Quality Score" biomarker via the `biomarker_proposal` constructor, `supports_hitl_proposals` + `pull_hitl_proposals` + `handle_proposal_resolution` queueing a "Stress Index" concept for human review (with cursor-advancement on resolve), `supports_documents` + `pull_documents` synthesising a small text lab report once per instance (cursor-based idempotency), plus all four notification kinds (alert / hitl / system / agent×critical) and the existing custom-action surface (gained a third action `show_status`). The config flow (`integrations/dev_dummy/config_flow.py`) demonstrates the remaining `BaseConfigFlow` hooks: `max_instances_per_user = 3`, `get_secret_fields() == ["webhook_secret"]` (round-trips through the inherited `prepare_for_storage` / `prepare_for_read` / `decrypt_for_use` defaults), plus a comprehensive JSON schema with a toggle per opt-in so each capability can be exercised in isolation. Manifest bumped to `2.0.0`; description refreshed. Two latent bugs fixed: `_latest_value` previously parsed `effective_datetime` as a string (would `TypeError` under a bare except, so the helper returned the FIRST matching obs instead of the LATEST); renamed to `_latest_numeric` with a proper datetime-aware comparison and an explicit skip for categoricals. The `sensor_malfunction` notification branch (HR > 200) was dead code (simulation never produced values that high) — added a `simulate_sensor_glitch` config toggle (5% chance per sync of an out-of-range HR) so the critical-alert path is reachable and tested. Stale docs (`docs/overview.md` claimed OAuth + webhook that didn't exist, `docs/testing.md` claimed a "10% failure rate" that wasn't implemented) rewritten to match the actual capabilities; new `docs/capabilities.md` provides a hook→toggle→file map. Test coverage: 51 new unit tests in `backend/tests/test_dev_dummy_provider.py` — one per capability, plus regression guards for the two bugfixes. No DB / Redis / OAuth provider required to run the tests. ruff clean; all 387 existing integration + SDK tests still pass.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream C.2 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): documents opt-in hook + engine wiring + per-sync caps.** New SDK opt-in hooks on `BaseHealthProvider` mirror the established `supports_X` / `pull_X` pattern: `supports_documents() -> bool` (default `False`) gates the pull, and `pull_documents(integration) -> List[DocumentPull]` (default `[]`) returns the specs. New `DocumentPull` Pydantic spec in `integrations/sdk/documents.py` (re-exported from `integrations.sdk`) carries `filename`, `content: bytes` (raw — provider fetches upstream), `content_type`, `examination_external_id` (links to an exam from `pull_examinations`), `category_concept_slug`, and `include_in_extraction`. Pydantic chosen over the plan's `@dataclass` to match the post-F SDK convention. Engine wiring in `integration_sync_service.run_sync` after the HITL-proposals block: per-spec, the engine resolves `examination_external_id` via a hoisted `exam_by_external_id` map (built in the examinations block), resolves `category_concept_slug` via `resolve_concept_by_slug`, enforces **both per-sync caps** before ingest, then delegates to `document_service.ingest_document_bytes` — the same canonical path the UI upload endpoint uses. Two new cap constants: `INTEGRATION_MAX_DOCS_PER_SYNC = 20` + `INTEGRATION_MAX_DOC_BYTES_PER_SYNC = 50 MiB`. `SyncResult.documents_pulled` / `documents_written` exposed; `records_synced` includes documents. No migration — `DocumentModel` already has every field C needs; document-level dedup deferred (providers advance their own cursor via `set_sync_cursor`). Tests: 7 new in `tests/test_integration_documents.py`. ruff clean.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream C.1 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): extract `ingest_document_bytes` from `upload_document`.** The canonical ingestion path (`document_service.upload_document`) took a Starlette `UploadFile` — useless from a Celery / webhook / api-proxy context. New `ingest_document_bytes(*, filename, content, content_type, tenant_id, patient_id, owner_id, db, examination_id=None, include_in_extraction=True, category_concept_id=None) -> DocumentModel` takes raw bytes. The existing `upload_document` becomes a thin wrapper that reads the `UploadFile` in capped chunks (audit A4) and delegates. Same storage path, same DB shape, same FHIR validation gate — only the code location changed. The OCR dispatch moves **inside** `ingest_document_bytes` (best-effort, 4-arg `ocr_document.apply_async` form) so the engine path gets OCR for free; the endpoint's inline OCR trigger + `BackgroundTasks` broker-down fallback are dropped. Minor UX regression for the broker-down edge case (document is still saved; user can re-trigger extraction via the UI's `trigger_extraction` button); the unification is worth it. New `category_concept_id` kwarg not previously settable from the endpoint — UI uploads leave it NULL, the integration engine resolves it from `DocumentPull.category_concept_slug`. Tests: 7 new in `tests/test_document_service_bytes.py`.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream G.4 fixups of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): register model + CASCADE patient_id FK + baseline-test allowlist.** Four drive-by fixes surfaced by the full test suite after G.4 landed: (1) Register `IntegrationProposal` in `app/models/__init__.py` so it's part of `Base.metadata.tables` (required by `test_squashed_initial_schema` and similar metadata-driven checks). (2) Switch `integration_proposals.patient_id` FK from SET NULL to CASCADE per audit D9 — every patient_id FK in the schema must CASCADE so a patient's clinical record deletes atomically. Catalog proposals leave patient_id NULL, so CASCADE doesn't affect them. (3) Migration uses the same-line + single-quote `op.create_table('foo',` style as the consolidated baseline so the `test_every_model_table_is_created_by_the_baseline` substring check matches. Added a `POST_BASELINE_TABLES` allowlist to that test for tables added by named follow-up migrations (with a sanity check that the named migration actually creates the table — keeps the allowlist honest). (4) Fixed the migration's `downgrade()` — `batch_op.drop_index(..., table_name=...)` is invalid; the batch context already knows the table.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream G.4 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): wire HITL-proposals opt-in into `run_sync`.** Adds the HITL-proposals opt-in block to `run_sync` (after the catalog-proposals step, before the push). `_opt_in(provider, 'supports_hitl_proposals')` gates `pull_hitl_proposals`; for each returned spec, the engine calls `integration_proposal_service.create_proposal` (dedup-aware insert). For newly-inserted rows only (NOT existing-and-returned ones, to avoid inbox spam on re-sync), it fires an HITL notification via the new `_emit_hitl_proposal_notification` helper. Notifications use `source=INTEGRATION, type=HITL_TASK, category=HITL, severity=WARNING` — the same shape as the chat-side HITL notifications but keyed on the integration source. The action button links to `/integrations/{provider}/{integration_id}/proposals/{proposal_id}` (forward-compatible — the SPA route doesn't exist yet; the review card + modal UI ships separately). Capped at `INTEGRATION_MAX_HITL_PROPOSALS_PER_SYNC = 20`. `SyncResult.hitl_proposals_pulled` / `hitl_proposals_inserted` exposed; `records_synced` includes the count. `create_proposal` now returns `(row, created)` so the engine can decide whether to fire the notification (only on actual inserts).

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream G.3 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): SDK hooks for HITL proposals.** Adds three opt-in hooks on `BaseHealthProvider` mirroring the `supports_X` / `pull_X` / handler pattern from B + E + F: `supports_hitl_proposals() -> bool` (default `False`, opt-in gate), `pull_hitl_proposals(integration) -> List[IntegrationProposalSpec]` (default `[]`), and `handle_proposal_resolution(integration, proposal_id, outcome) -> None` (default no-op, async — called by the resolver after approve/reject/cancel so the provider can advance a cursor, log audit, etc.). Names use `pull_*` for consistency with the established pattern. The `hitl_` prefix disambiguates from the auto-apply `pull_catalog_proposals` — a provider can opt into both (auto-apply for high-confidence entries, HITL for ones needing human judgement). Re-exports the spec + outcome + four typed constructors (`biomarker_hitl_proposal`, `medication_hitl_proposal`, `concept_hitl_proposal`, `edge_hitl_proposal`) from `integrations.sdk`.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream G.2 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): proposal endpoints + resolver + SDK specs.** Adds the resolver, the three HITL endpoints, and the SDK spec module. `IntegrationProposalSpec` + `ProposalOutcome` Pydantic models + four typed convenience constructors in `integrations.sdk.proposals` wrap the same payload shape as F's `CatalogProposal` constructors but tagged for human review. `integration_proposal_service.resolve_proposal` performs the state machine (PROPOSED → CONFIRMED / DISMISSED / FAILED), delegates the approve path through `catalog_proposal_service.apply_proposal` (the same write path F.3 auto-applies through), stamps `resolved_*` fields, and fires the provider's `handle_proposal_resolution` callback (best-effort). Snapshots ORM attributes before any potential rollback to avoid `MissingGreenlet` when the session is expired. Three new endpoints on the integrations router: `GET /instance/{id}/proposals?status=` (list), `GET /instance/{id}/proposals/{proposal_id}` (one), `POST /instance/{id}/proposals/{proposal_id}/resolve` (resolve). New `_load_owned_integration(...)` helper extracted from the inline pattern repeated across this endpoint — stricter than the existing inline checks (includes `tenant_id` scoping). USER role can list + view but not approve (catalog writes require ADMIN+ under the catalog policy) — endpoint surfaces as 403. Re-resolve from a terminal state returns 409 (idempotent contract). Tests: 15 new in `tests/test_integration_proposals_api.py`.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream G.1 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): `integration_proposals` model + persistence service.** Adds the persistence layer for workstream G. `IntegrationProposal` ORM model: a pending catalog write proposed by an integration, awaiting human review. Mirrors `HitlTaskStatus` (PROPOSED → CONFIRMED / DISMISSED / FAILED) so the existing HITL state machine applies. Deduped by a partial unique index on `(integration_id, dedup_key)` where `dedup_key` is the sha256 of canonical JSON of `(proposal_type, proposed_payload)`. Migration `g1h2i3t4l5pr` chaining off `e1x2a3m4i5n6`: creates the table + 8 indexes (basic lookups, list-by-status, tenant-wide, partial unique dedup). `integration_proposal_service` module: `create_proposal` (dedup-aware insert, returns `(row, created)` so the caller knows whether to fire a notification), `get_proposal` (integration-scoped read), `list_proposals` (status filter + newest-first with deterministic `(created_at, id)` tiebreaker), `count_proposals`, `compute_dedup_key`. Pydantic response + resolve-request schemas. Tests: 10 new in `tests/test_integration_proposal_service.py`.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream F.3 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): wire catalog-proposals opt-in into `run_sync`.** Adds the catalog-proposals opt-in block to `run_sync` (after the examinations step, before the push). `_opt_in(provider, 'supports_catalog_proposals')` gates `pull_catalog_proposals`; the resolved actor calls `catalog_proposal_service.apply_proposal` for each item; per-item failures logged and don't abort the sync. Capped at `INTEGRATION_MAX_PROPOSALS_PER_SYNC = 50` items per sync. `SyncResult.proposals_pulled` / `proposals_applied` exposed; `records_synced` includes `proposals_applied`. Drive-by fix: `map_observations_to_biomarkers` was previously indented *inside* the per-observation patient-id-coercion loop and ran N times per sync instead of once — idempotent so just wasted work, but a real correctness risk if the call ever grew side effects. Dedented + comment explaining the one-call contract.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream F.2 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): catalog proposals for medication / concept / edge kinds.** Extends `apply_proposal` with three new routers: `medication` → `medication_service.create_catalog_medication` (FHIR-validates + stamps scope via `DEFAULT_CATALOG_POLICY`). Idempotent on `(tenant_id, name)`. `concept` → `ConceptService.create_concept` with the actor's role + tenant_id. Validates `kind` against the `ConceptKind` enum. Idempotent on `slug`. `edge` → `ConceptService.create_edge` with `source=ConceptProvenance.INTEGRATION, status=APPROVED` — the only catalog-layer write path today that actually stamps the integration provenance (`ConceptEdge` is the only model with a dedicated `source` column). Idempotent on `(src_type, src_id, dst_type, dst_id, relation, tenant_id)`. Each router validates the payload shape via the matching `*Create` schema (or inline enum coercion for the strongly-typed concept/edge fields) before touching the DB. Role limitation: `ConceptService.create_concept` / `create_edge` require role ≥ ADMIN, so USER-role integration owners can't contribute concepts/edges. Tests: 9 new across the three kinds (happy path + idempotency + invalid-kind + invalid-UUID) in `tests/test_catalog_proposal_service.py`.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream F.1 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): catalog proposals SDK shape + biomarker apply service.** Adds the opt-in `supports_catalog_proposals` / `pull_catalog_proposals` hook pair on `BaseHealthProvider` (mirrors the `supports_X` / `pull_X` shape from workstreams B + E), the `CatalogProposal` Pydantic spec + four typed constructors (`biomarker_proposal`, `medication_proposal`, `concept_proposal`, `edge_proposal`) in `integrations.sdk.catalog`, and the matching `apply_proposal` write-side service. F.1 wires only the `biomarker` router end-to-end — it validates the payload via `BiomarkerCreate`, resolves the preferred unit + class concept, stamps TENANT scope + the owning user via `DEFAULT_CATALOG_POLICY.assign_create_scope`, tags an explicit `meta_data["_provenance"] = "integration"` marker (the model has no dedicated provenance column), and is idempotent on slug. The other three kinds raise `NotImplementedError` until F.2 lands. Engine wiring + per-sync cap land in F.3. No migration needed (F is stateless — proposals aren't persisted; only the resulting catalog rows are). Closes the `ConceptProvenance.INTEGRATION` gap from workstream F of the integrations follow-ups plan. Tests: 6 new in `tests/test_catalog_proposal_service.py` + 2 new contract tests in `tests/test_integration_registry.py` (hook defaults + re-export identity).

- **Docs: aligned public docs with the integrations cleanup pass + stack 1 (workstreams A, D, B, E).** Doc-only commit — no code, no test impact. Four public docs updated to reflect capabilities that shipped on this branch: (1) `docs/INTEGRATIONS_SDK.md` gained a new **§3.10 "Clinical Events & Examinations (Opt-in Write Hooks)"** section documenting the `supports_clinical_events` / `pull_clinical_events` and `supports_examinations` / `pull_examinations` opt-in pairs, the dedup contract (provider sets `external_id`; engine stamps `source_integration_id` from `integration.id`), what the engine does on the provider's behalf (resolves a service-context actor via `integration_actor.resolve_integration_actor`, writes through `clinical_event_service.create_event` / `examination_service.create_examination`), a "when to use which" decision table, and a pointer to the bridge provider as the reference implementation for examination creation. §4 "Building FHIR Observations" gained a **"Categorical / string values"** subsection documenting `ObservationBuilder.set_value_string` (the FHIR R4 §3.1.1 `value[x]` mutual-exclusion rule, the categorical-no-normalization invariant).
