(2) `docs/INTEGRATIONS_FRAMEWORK.md` gained a new **highlight #10 "Integration-Driven Write Hooks (Clinical Events & Examinations)"** alongside the existing Tool Exposure (#7), Notification Exposure (#8), and Secret Encryption (#9) contracts. (3) `docs/STATUS.md` "Completed" section gained a new **"Integrations SDK follow-ups pass"** entry summarizing the four workstreams (A: SDK robustness / shared `_retry_request` / full-jitter backoff / `fetch_json` removal; D: `resolve_integration_actor` service helper; B: clinical-events opt-in hook + migration `b1l2i3n4t5ev`; E: `examination_service.create_examination` chokepoint + migration `e1x2a3m4i5n6` + bridge migration that fixes the `category_id` silent-drop bug). (4) `docs/API.md` `examinations` and `clinical-events` sections gained notes that the write paths delegate to the canonical services and that responses now expose optional `source_integration_id` / `external_id` fields populated only on integration-sourced rows; the `POST` rows' dedup semantics are clarified (UI heuristic vs integration-key). The broader **H (Docs restructure)** workstream — API-ref table for the SDK, reserved config keys section, notifications-module section — is intentionally deferred to a batch pass at the end of the follow-ups plan; this commit only addresses stale-correctness.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream E.3 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): examinations opt-in hook + engine wiring.** Completes workstream E (the largest capability addition in stack 1). New SDK opt-in hooks on `BaseHealthProvider` (`integrations/sdk/base.py`) mirror the `supports_clinical_events` pattern shipped in B.2: `supports_examinations() -> bool` (default `False`) gates the pull, and `pull_examinations(integration) -> List[ExaminationCreate]` (default `[]`) returns the exams. `ExaminationCreate` is re-exported from `integrations.sdk` so providers can build payloads without reaching into `app.schemas`. Providers set `external_id` on the payload (the upstream system's stable encounter id); `source_integration_id` is supplied by the engine (= the integration's own id), not by the provider. Engine wiring in `integration_sync_service.run_sync`: after the clinical-events step, the engine probes `_opt_in(provider, "supports_examinations")`, and if True, calls `pull_examinations`, resolves a service-context actor via `integration_actor.resolve_integration_actor(db, integration)` (workstream D), and writes each exam via `examination_service.create_examination(db, actor, payload, source_integration_id=integration.id, external_id=payload.external_id)` (workstream E.1's dedup-aware write path that the bridge provider was migrated to in E.2). Per-exam failures are logged but don't abort the sync — mirrors the clinical-events and push hook resilience pattern. `records_synced` in the sync log now also counts exams written. Tests: 3 new — `test_run_sync_wires_examinations_opt_in_hook` (source-level guard that run_sync references the hook + the create_examination call), `test_sdk_base_declares_examinations_opt_in_hook_with_safe_defaults` (contract test for the False/[] defaults), `test_examination_create_is_reexported_from_sdk` (the SDK re-export aliases the schema, not duplicates it). 283 integration + SDK + bridge + examination-service + clinical-event + actor tests green; ruff reports zero new errors on touched files.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream E.2 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): bridge provider migrates to the canonical `examination_service.create_examination` (fixes a latent category-silent-drop bug).** The bridge's `_process_and_save_sync_data` (`integrations/health_assistant_bridge/provider.py`) inlined ~80 LOC of dedup + ORM construction for examinations. That code had gone stale in three ways: (1) it set `category_id=` — a column that **no longer exists** on the live `ExaminationModel` (renamed to `category_concept_id` when categories moved into the unified taxonomy), so the bridge silently dropped the category on every exam it created; (2) it referenced the deleted `ExaminationCategory` model (categories are now `Concept` rows with the `examination_category` kind tag); (3) it pre-generated UUIDs with `uuid.uuid4()` instead of letting the model's `gen_random_uuid()` server default do its job. E.2 replaces the entire exam-processing block with a call to `examination_service.create_examination(db, actor, payload, source_integration_id=integration.id, external_id=client_exam.id)`. The bridge now resolves a service-context actor via workstream D's `resolve_integration_actor`, builds an `ExaminationCreate` payload (with `category` as text so the service can run `MedicalProcessingService.resolve_category` — the modern concept-resolution path), and passes the integration provenance through. The returned exam's id is then used when parsing the nested records. Org-name → organization resolution stays provider-side (the service doesn't manage organizations). Bonus refinement to `examination_service.create_examination`: the heuristic UI dedup path now fires **only for pure UI callers** (defined as "no integration provenance at all" — both `source_integration_id` and `external_id` unset). An integration-sourced exam, even one missing `external_id` because the upstream system exposes no stable ids, no longer risks accidentally matching an unrelated UI row that happens to share date + category + notes. Tests: 1 new in `tests/test_health_assistant_bridge.py` — `test_bridge_routes_examinations_through_canonical_service` is a source-level guard that the bridge calls `create_examination`, references `resolve_integration_actor`, and does NOT construct `ExaminationModel` directly, reference `ExaminationCategory`, or set the stale `category_id=` field (uses a negative-lookbehind regex so the live `category_concept_id=` doesn't trip the check). 132 bridge + examination-service + c2-layering tests green; ruff reports zero new errors on touched files (4 pre-existing in the bridge untouched).

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream E.1 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): new `examination_service.create_examination` chokepoint + integration-key dedup.** The `POST /examinations` write path was inlined entirely in the route handler at `backend/app/api/v1/endpoints/examinations.py:46-128` — patient validation, category resolution, dedup, ORM construction, doctor linking, commit, and relationship reload all lived in the endpoint. That left integrations (the bridge provider, the future `supports_examinations` SDK hook from E.3) no clean call site, so the bridge bypassed dedup entirely with its own direct-ORM write — and its code is **stale** (uses `category_id` instead of the live `category_concept_id`). New `backend/app/services/examination_service.py` exposes a single function, `create_examination(db, current_user, payload, *, source_integration_id=None, external_id=None)`, that owns the full pipeline. The endpoint becomes a thin HTTP adapter (4 lines of handler body) that maps `NotFoundError` → 404. The service preserves **both** dedup paths from the original endpoint: (1) the **integration-key dedup** (precise, opt-in via kwargs) — when both `source_integration_id` and `external_id` are supplied, the service looks up by `(tenant_id, patient_id, source_integration_id, external_id)` and returns the existing row as-is; (2) the **heuristic UI dedup** (fuzzy, default-on) — when `auto_extract_metadata` is False, the service looks up by `(tenant_id, patient_id, examination_date, category_concept_id, notes)` to catch accidental re-submissions; bulk-placeholder uploads (`auto_extract_metadata=True`) bypass the heuristic check, preserving the original endpoint's batch-create semantics. **Bonus latent-bug fix:** the `source_integration_id` and `external_id` fields exist on `ExaminationCreate` (and have for a while), but the old endpoint never forwarded them to the ORM constructor — UI callers that set them were silently ignored. The service now honors them, with the explicit kwarg winning over the payload field when both are present. New migration `e1x2a3m4i5n6` adds the matching **partial unique index** `uq_examination_integration_dedup` on `(tenant_id, patient_id, source_integration_id, external_id)` — fires only when all four columns are non-NULL, so UI rows bypass it and integration-sourced rows are deduped at the DB layer. Same pattern B.1 shipped on `clinical_events`; catches the race window between the SELECT and INSERT. The `MedicalProcessingService` import is **lazy** inside the function body to avoid a circular import (`app.ai.pipeline.service` → `app.workers.task_logger` → `app.workers.ai_tasks` → back); a comment explains why the endpoint module can get away with a top-level import (route modules load later) but a service module can't. Tests: 9 new in `tests/test_examination_service.py` — integration dedup hit (no new row queued), integration-key SELECT filters on all four fields (compiles to SQL and asserts each predicate present), integration dedup miss creates with provenance populated (asserts `source_integration_id`/`external_id`/`tenant_id`/`created_by` on the ORM instance), UI-only path skips the integration-key lookup (asserts no `source_integration_id =` predicate in any query), heuristic dedup returns existing when `auto_extract_metadata=False`, `auto_extract_metadata=True` bypasses heuristic dedup (guards the bulk-placeholder upload flow), missing patient raises `NotFoundError`, source-level guard that the model declares both columns, and a source-level guard that the endpoint delegates to the service (no direct `ExaminationModel(...)` construction or inline `resolve_category` in the route handler). 250 tests green (conftest applies the new migration cleanly); ruff reports zero new errors on touched files (2 pre-existing E402 in `examinations.py` untouched).

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream B.2 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): clinical-events opt-in hook + engine wiring.** The smallest of the new capability hooks — providers can now pull longitudinal clinical events (hospital admissions, chronic conditions, pregnancies, ...) alongside observations, and the engine writes them through the existing `clinical_event_service.create_event` (which gained dedup in B.1). New SDK opt-in hooks on `BaseHealthProvider` (`integrations/sdk/base.py`) mirror the `supports_notifications` / `supports_tools` pattern: `supports_clinical_events() -> bool` (default `False`) gates the pull, and `pull_clinical_events(integration) -> List[ClinicalEventCreate]` (default `[]`) returns the events. `ClinicalEventCreate` is re-exported from `integrations.sdk` so providers can build payloads without reaching into `app.schemas`. New optional `external_id` field on `ClinicalEventCreate` — providers set it to the upstream system's stable encounter/episode id; the engine reads it off the payload and passes it through to `create_event`'s dedup-aware kwarg path. `source_integration_id` is **not** on the schema — the engine always supplies it (= the integration's own id), so providers can't fake their provenance. Engine wiring in `integration_sync_service.run_sync`: after `apply_telemetry_split`, the engine probes `_opt_in(provider, "supports_clinical_events")`, and if True, calls `pull_clinical_events`, resolves a service-context actor via `integration_actor.resolve_integration_actor(db, integration)`, and writes each event via `clinical_event_service.create_event(db, actor, ev, source_integration_id=integration.id, external_id=ev.external_id)`. Per-event failures are logged but don't abort the sync (mirrors the push hook's resilience). The new generic `_opt_in(provider, hook_name)` helper centralizes the `getattr` / callable-check / exception-swallowing dance so the engine can grow future opt-in hooks (`supports_examinations`, `supports_documents`, ...) without each call site re-implementing it. `clinical_event_service.create_event` also got a small refactor: `external_id` is now read via `external_id or payload.external_id` (so the dedup key set by the provider on the payload is honored even when the engine forgets to forward it explicitly), and `event_data = payload.model_dump(exclude={..., "external_id"})` (since the field now exists on the schema, it must be excluded from the dump to avoid passing it twice to the ORM constructor). Tests: 5 new — `test_run_sync_wires_clinical_events_opt_in_hook` (source-level guard that run_sync references the hook + the create_event call with `source_integration_id=integration.id`), `test_opt_in_helper_handles_missing_method`, `test_opt_in_helper_swallows_exceptions_from_capability_probe`, `test_sdk_base_declares_clinical_events_opt_in_hook_with_safe_defaults` (contract test for the False/[] defaults + bodies), `test_clinical_event_create_is_reexported_from_sdk` (the SDK re-export aliases the schema, not duplicates it). 246 integration + SDK + clinical-event + bridge tests green; ruff reports zero new errors on touched files.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream B.1 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): clinical-event integration-provenance columns + dedup in `create_event`.** Lays the DB + service foundation for workstream B.2 (the SDK opt-in hook that lets integrations pull clinical events). Without these columns, every sync would create duplicate events for the same upstream encounter. New alembic migration `b1l2i3n4t5ev` adds two nullable columns to `clinical_events`: `source_integration_id` (FK → `user_integrations.id`, `ON DELETE SET NULL`) and `external_id` (free-text — the upstream system's encounter id). Plus a **partial unique index** `uq_clinical_event_integration_dedup` on `(tenant_id, patient_id, source_integration_id, external_id)` that only fires when all four columns are non-NULL — UI-created events (both fields NULL) bypass it, integration-sourced events are deduped automatically at the DB layer. Mirrors the existing pattern on `examinations` (`examination_model.py:53-59`). The `ClinicalEvent` model declares the columns + `to_dict()` serializes them. `clinical_event_service.create_event` gained two new optional kwargs — `source_integration_id` and `external_id` — that trigger dedup when **both** are supplied: a new `_find_integration_event` helper runs a SELECT keyed on all four fields, and if a row exists it's returned as-is (no duplicate insert, no notification re-fire). UI callers leave both as `None` and get the original create-always behavior — the kwargs are not part of `ClinicalEventCreate`, so the wire schema is unchanged and interactive callers can't accidentally set them. The partial unique index also catches the race window between SELECT and INSERT at the DB layer (a concurrent sync attempt that wins the INSERT raises `IntegrityError` instead of double-inserting). Tests: 6 new in `tests/test_clinical_event_integration_dedup.py` — dedup hit returns existing row (asserts no new row queued), dedup SELECT filters on all four fields (compiles the query to SQL and asserts each predicate is present, catching a regression that drops one), dedup miss creates with provenance populated (asserts `source_integration_id`/`external_id`/`tenant_id`/`created_by` on the queued ORM instance), UI-caller path with only `external_id` set skips the lookup entirely (asserts zero execute calls), symmetric path with only `source_integration_id` set also skips lookup, and a source-level guard that the ORM model still declares both columns. 177 tests green (conftest applies the new migration cleanly); ruff clean on touched files.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream D of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): service-context actor resolver.** New `app/services/integration_actor.py` with one function: `resolve_integration_actor(db, integration) -> TokenData`. The clean service-layer functions an integration will want to call (`clinical_event_service.create_event`, the future `examination_service.create_examination`, etc.) all take `current_user: TokenData` — for RBAC (the `check_*_access` helpers compare against `current_user.tenant_id` / `current_user.role`) and for audit provenance (`AuditMixin.created_by` / `updated_by` populate from `current_user.user_id`). There's no interactive user when a Celery worker runs `sync_active_integrations`, when a webhook fires, or when a two-way API proxy handler runs. Today's escape hatch is the bridge provider bypassing the service layer entirely and writing ORM rows directly — losing dedup, category resolution, doctor linking, audit provenance, and tenant scoping (and its code is also stale: uses `category_id` instead of `category_concept_id`). `resolve_integration_actor` fixes this generically: it derives a `TokenData` from the `UserIntegration`'s owning user (`user_id` + `tenant_id` + `role` + `email`), so service-layer writes from integration contexts go through the exact same code path as interactive UI writes — same RBAC, same audit, same tenant scoping. The role is **re-fetched from `UserModel` on every call** so role changes (e.g. an ADMIN demoted to USER after the integration was connected) take effect on the next sync without re-issuing tokens. The tenant_id comes from the user row, not the integration row, defending against the owner having been moved to a new tenant after connecting the integration. **No service-account-style "integration user" is created** — the integration acts as its owner, with whatever role the owner has. Raises `NotFoundError` if the owner row is gone (hard delete / FK cascade) so the caller can surface it as an integration ERROR state rather than silently writing under a NULL identity. Foundational for workstreams B (Clinical Events hook), C (Documents hook), and E (Examinations hook) — all three need this helper to call their respective services from non-interactive contexts. 5 new tests in `tests/test_integration_actor.py`: happy-path field population (id/tenant/role/email/is_service_account), role re-fetch + user-tenant-wins-over-integration-tenant invariant, `NotFoundError` on owner deletion, defensive `NotFoundError` on malformed `user_id=None` integration row (and confirms no DB query is issued in that case), and a sanity check that the produced `TokenData` is shaped for `check_patient_access`. C2 layering suite (115 tests) green — the new service module imports only from `app.core.errors`, `app.models.*`, `app.schemas.*`, and `sqlalchemy` (no endpoint imports); ruff clean.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream A.3 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): vestigial `fetch_json` removed from the SDK base.** `BaseHealthProvider.fetch_json(integration, url, headers=None, params=None, max_retries=3)` was a pre-`http_request` GET helper at `integrations/sdk/base.py:283-338` that inlined its own retry loop — different backoff base (`2 ** attempt`) from the canonical `http_request` (`1.0 * 2**n`), no jitter, and a misleading final exception (`raise IntegrationRateLimitError` on **all** exhaustion paths, including non-429 ones). It had **zero provider overrides or call sites** across `integrations/` and `backend/` (verified via `rg "fetch_json" integrations/ backend/` → only the declaration hit). After A.1 + A.2 extracted the shared `_retry_request` primitive, `fetch_json` was the only SDK HTTP surface not routing through it. **Removed outright** (greenfield — no compatibility shim needed). Providers that need a robust GET now call `await http_request(self._http_client, "GET", url, ...)` from `integrations.sdk`, getting full-jitter backoff, `Retry-After` honoring, and the correct exception type per status code. The `asyncio` and `.exceptions` imports that were only used by `fetch_json` are dropped too. Documentation: `docs/INTEGRATIONS_SDK.md` §3.1 + §3.3 rewritten to reference the shared helpers (`http_request` / `fhir_search` / `fhir_create` / `fhir_conditional_update`) and the full-jitter retry policy; the local integrations skill's codebase map, SDK-base description, pull-data example, §5.1 method table, §5.4 exception table, §9 checklist, §10 robustness note, and §13.1 debugging row all updated (8 `fetch_json` references → 0; verified via `rg`). Tests: 2 new in `tests/test_integration_registry.py` — `test_sdk_base_no_longer_declares_fetch_json` (asserts the method is gone from `BaseHealthProvider`) and `test_sdk_base_no_longer_imports_asyncio_or_legacy_exceptions` (source-level guard that the now-unused imports stay gone, catching a partial revert that leaves them dangling). 109 SDK + integration tests green; ruff clean on touched files.

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream A.2 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): shared retry helper for all SDK HTTP calls.** Extracted a single `_retry_request(do_request, *, url, method, max_retries)` primitive in `integrations/sdk/http.py` that owns the SDK's entire retry/backoff/jitter/status-mapping contract (network errors → retry then `IntegrationDataError`; 429 → retry honoring `Retry-After` then `IntegrationRateLimitError`; 5xx → retry then `IntegrationDataError`; 401/403 → immediate `IntegrationAuthError`; everything else returned to the caller). The three helpers that previously inlined their own copies of this loop — `http_request` (`integrations/sdk/http.py`), `fhir_create` + `fhir_conditional_update` (`integrations/sdk/fhir.py`), and the OAuth/DCR/token-refresh `_request_json` (`integrations/sdk/auth.py`) — now all delegate to it. Consequences: (1) **`_request_json` is retry-aware for the first time** — pre-refactor, OAuth discovery / Dynamic Client Registration / token exchange / token refresh were all single-shot, so a transient 429 or 503 on a hospital IdP's load balancer surfaced as an immediate `IntegrationDataError`/`IntegrationRateLimitError`; now those calls get the same full-jitter backoff as every other SDK HTTP call. (2) **All four helpers now share one jitter implementation** (the `_backoff_delay` introduced in A.1) — pre-refactor `fhir_create` and `fhir_conditional_update` carried their own copies of the no-jitter `backoff = 1.0; backoff *= 2` loop and had already diverged subtly (`fhir_create` had no logger warnings, `fhir_conditional_update` did). (3) **`fhir_conditional_update`'s 412 path is preserved** — the helper returns the final response and the caller still decides what to do with non-retryable non-2xx; 412 remains a tuple return, not a raise. Cleaned up unused imports left in the wake of the refactor (`asyncio`, `IntegrationAuthError`, `IntegrationRateLimitError` from `fhir.py`; `IntegrationRateLimitError` from `auth.py`). Tests: 5 new — `tests/test_sdk_auth.py` (`test_discover_smart_retries_5xx_via_shared_handler` proves the prior single-shot path now retries; `test_discover_smart_429_retries_then_raises_rate_limit` proves the same for 429 → `IntegrationRateLimitError`); `tests/test_sdk_fhir.py` (`test_fhir_helpers_route_through_shared_retry_request` is a source-level guard that re-inlining the retry loop in either helper would trip; `test_fhir_create_retries_5xx_then_raises_data_error` confirms the post-refactor retry count matches `max_retries`; `test_fhir_conditional_update_412_still_returns_tuple` pins the 412 tuple-return contract). 95 SDK + integration tests green; ruff reports zero new errors on touched files (2 pre-existing errors in `base.py` / `secrets.py` untouched).

- **Integrations SDK (Workstream A.1 of follow-ups pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-followups-2026-07-21.md`): full-jitter retry backoff + bounded default `max_pages`.** Two defects in the SDK's HTTP/FHIR layer, both with thundering-herd failure modes. (1) **No jitter anywhere.** Every retry wait was a deterministic `base * 2**attempt` — when a backend recovers from a transient outage, all integration instances retry on the exact same tick, restressing the server. Added `_backoff_delay(attempt, base=1.0)` in `integrations/sdk/http.py` using the **full-jitter** scheme (AWS Architecture Blog, "Exponential Backoff and Jitter"): `uniform(0, min(base * 2**attempt, 60.0))`. Each client now picks an independent random wait in its theoretical cap, so a retry wave spreads out instead of stampeding. The 60-second ceiling bounds the worst-case wait at high attempt counts. `http_request` now calls `_backoff_delay` on every retry path (network error, 5xx); the 429 path still prefers a server-provided `Retry-After` when present (the server knows its own load better than our heuristic). (2) **`paginate_bundle` and `fhir_search` defaulted to `max_pages=None` (unbounded).** An integration that forgot the argument could walk a multi-million-entry FHIR Bundle indefinitely. Both now default to `DEFAULT_MAX_PAGES = 100` (exported from `integrations.sdk.http`); callers can still pass `max_pages=None` for an explicit opt-out when genuinely unbounded iteration is needed. Tests: 7 new in `tests/test_sdk_http.py` — `_backoff_delay` returns values in `[0, base * 2**attempt]` (sampled 50× per attempt across 8 attempts), the 60s ceiling kicks in at high attempts, `base` scales the range, `http_request`'s retry sleeps are jittered (captured via `monkeypatch` on `asyncio.sleep`), `Retry-After` overrides jitter when present, the default `max_pages=100` cap actually halts self-linking Bundle iteration, and `max_pages=None` is still a working escape hatch. 40 SDK HTTP + FHIR tests green; ruff clean on touched files.

- **Agent skills + cross-skill drift cleanup (Phase 4 of integrations-SDK cleanup pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-cleanup-2026-07-21.md`).** Three local agent skills — the canonical reference for any agent working in the codebase — had drifted against the actual codebase. (1) `.opencode/skills/integrations/SKILL.md` §1 listed `health_connect/` as "empty placeholder — scaffold only" but that directory was removed long ago; §1 also omitted `sdk/notifications.py` (12 KB, exporting `NotificationSpec` / `NotificationSpecBuilder` / `NotificationAction` / `NotificationTypeSpec`); §1 documentation table and §10 gotcha #13 both referenced `docs/USER_INTEGRATIONS_PLAN.md` as "OUTDATED" but the file was deleted in commit `0b9951c` (2026-07-20); §8.3 route table was missing the three notification routes (`GET /notification-types`, `PUT /{domain}/notification-types/{type_id}`, `POST /{domain}/notification-action/{integration_id}/{action_id}`) that exist in the actual code at `backend/app/api/v1/endpoints/integrations.py:828,892,963`; §10 gotcha #12 mis-stated that `ObservationBuilder.build()` "strips tzinfo (naive UTC) for asyncpg" — the opposite of what the code does (the tz-fix regression test at `tests/test_sdk_observation_builder_tz.py:30` pins that the builder must keep tzinfo; the rationale is now corrected). (2) `.opencode/skills/project-overview/SKILL.md` carried the same two stale items (`health_connect/` directory listing + `USER_INTEGRATIONS_PLAN.md` doc row); fixed in place, also added the missing `fhir_server/` to the integration list. (3) `.opencode/skills/documentation/SKILL.md` listed the deleted `USER_INTEGRATIONS_PLAN.md` in its docs-categorization table; row removed. Verified `rg "USER_INTEGRATIONS_PLAN|health_connect" .opencode/ docs/` now returns zero matches. Doc-only commit — no test impact; all changes are inside `.opencode/skills/`.

- **Integrations SDK: legacy OAuth stubs removed from the core base (Phase 3 of cleanup pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-cleanup-2026-07-21.md`).** The minimal core base at `integrations/base.py` (the abstract class the registry discovers providers through) declared a legacy OAuth trio — `get_auth_url` / `exchange_token` / `refresh_access_token` — that predates the SDK's `begin_oauth` / `complete_oauth` pair and the `SmartOAuth` helper (`integrations/sdk/auth.py`). No engine path called them; they returned `""` / `{}` / `{}` silently, which invited new integrations to override the wrong shape (the SDK base at `integrations/sdk/base.py` formally declares the new pair as `raise NotImplementedError` defaults, but the core base's silent trio was a footgun for anyone reading the core abstract class directly). **Breaking change, by design** — greenfield codebase, no users, no out-of-tree overrides to preserve: all three methods are **removed outright** (not deprecated). Providers that need OAuth subclass the SDK base and use `SmartOAuth` for the SMART-on-FHIR round-trip. The `import warnings` that a more conservative earlier version of this change had added is also dropped. 2 new tests in `tests/test_integration_registry.py` (`test_core_base_no_longer_declares_legacy_oauth_stubs` asserts none of the three names exist on `BaseHealthProvider`; `test_core_base_does_not_import_warnings_module` guards against a partial revert leaving a dangling import). 5 registry tests green; ruff clean on the changed lines (3 pre-existing ruff errors untouched).

- **Integrations: webhook sync path now routes through the shared telemetry/FHIR split helper (Phase 2 of cleanup pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-cleanup-2026-07-21.md`).** The webhook handler at `POST /api/v1/integrations/{domain}/webhook/{integration_id}` (`backend/app/api/v1/endpoints/integrations.py`) used to inline its own copy of the telemetry-vs-FHIR routing loop that `apply_telemetry_split` (`backend/app/services/integration_sync_service.py`) already encapsulated. Two consequences: (1) the two copies had already **diverged subtly** (the webhook copy matched `"8867-4" in slug OR "heart-rate" in slug`; the canonical helper also matches `slug == "heart_rate"` and treats the slug-detection chain as `elif`, so a future policy change had to be made in two places); (2) the webhook path **never stamped `performer[0].reference`** with the integration id (the inlined performer block was missing the `"reference": "Integration/{id}"` field that the manual + background paths set), so observations ingested via webhook didn't link back to their owning instance in the details-endpoint UI (`integrations.py:503-506,545-548`); (3) `post_sync_notifications` was always called with `telemetry_persisted=0, fhir_persisted=count` because the webhook path didn't track the split — acknowledged in an inline comment. The webhook handler now delegates to `apply_telemetry_split` (the same helper `run_sync` uses for manual + background sync, audit A4), the inlined copy and the redundant `b_defs_map` fetch (the helper does its own) are removed, and `post_sync_notifications` now receives the **real** per-channel counts. Net effect: all three sync entry points (manual, background, webhook) now produce identical observation pipelines, telemetry-class webhook data (heart rate, steps, etc.) lands in the TimescaleDB hypertable instead of bloating `fhir_observations`, and webhook-driven integration notifications report correct per-channel counts. 3 new source-level parity tests in `tests/test_integration_sync_telemetry_split.py` guard against a revert: `test_webhook_endpoint_uses_apply_telemetry_split` (handler delegates to the helper), `test_webhook_endpoint_no_longer_inlines_telemetry_loop` (the `"calories" in slug` literal and the `TelemetryDataModel(` constructor must not reappear in the handler), and `test_webhook_endpoint_passes_real_per_channel_counts_to_notifications` (`fhir_persisted=len(fhir_records)` and `telemetry_persisted=len(telemetry_records)` literals must survive). 18 telemetry-split + integration tests green; ruff reports zero new errors on touched files (8 pre-existing errors in `integrations.py` untouched).

- **Integrations SDK (Phase 1 of cleanup pass, plan: `dev/plans/integrations-sdk-cleanup-2026-07-21.md`): categorical-observation fix + API-surface gaps.** Three small independent defects, each capable of silently dropping data or steering integration authors at the wrong pattern. (1) **Fix (silent data drop): `ObservationBuilder` now supports categorical / string values.** `set_value(value: float, ...)` was the only value-setter on the SDK builder (`integrations/sdk/observation_builder.py`), and `build()` always emitted a `valueQuantity` — never a `valueString` — so any integration that needed categorical data (lab PCR results, sleep stages, subjective pain scores, questionnaire answers) had no SDK path. The reference bridge integration worked around this by poking `obs_builder._data["value_string"] = ...` as a private attribute (`integrations/health_assistant_bridge/provider.py`), but `build()` never read `_data["value_string"]`, so the categorical value was **silently discarded** before reaching the FHIR validator — the bridge's "SARS-CoV-2 PCR: POSITIVE" records never landed. Added a public `set_value_string(value: str)` chainable method that mirrors FHIR R4 §3.1.1's `value[x]` mutual-exclusion rule (last setter wins; calling `set_value` after `set_value_string` clears the string slot, and vice versa), and updated `build()` to emit `value_string` (omitting `value_quantity`) when set. `raw_value` / `normalized_value` / `relative_score` are left unset for categoricals — they're numeric concepts and downstream analytics must not try to plot a string on a numeric axis. The bridge provider now uses the public method (the private-attribute poke is gone). New test file `tests/test_sdk_observation_builder_categorical.py` (7 tests) covers the basic shape, mutual-exclusion contract in both directions, the no-numeric-normalization invariant, a FHIR R4 round-trip through `assert_valid_fhir`, and a regression test that reproduces the old buggy bridge pattern to prove it would have lost data. (2) **Surface gap: `fhir_create` is now re-exported from `integrations.sdk`.** The helper (`integrations/sdk/fhir.py`) — FHIR `POST /{Resource}` with the same retry/auth/rate-limit contract as `fhir_conditional_update` — was implemented but absent from `integrations/sdk/__init__.py`'s imports and `__all__`, so provider authors reading its docstring naturally tried `from integrations.sdk import fhir_create` and hit `ImportError`. Added to both lists; new re-export smoke test plus three behavioral tests (201 returns the resource, 401 → `IntegrationAuthError`, Bearer header sent when `access_token=` passed) appended to `tests/test_sdk_fhir.py`. (3) **Dead code: `NotificationSpec.source_ref` no longer carries a dead `if False` branch.** The field was declared `field(default_factory=list) if False else field(default_factory=dict)` (`integrations/sdk/notifications.py`) — the list branch was unreachable, so the field was effectively `default_factory=dict`, but the construct read like a typo and invited a future "fix" that would revert to a list. New `tests/test_sdk_notifications.py` (4 tests) pins the `NotificationSpec` defaults (incl. the `source_ref == {}` contract), the `to_payload` action/block serialization, the fluent `NotificationSpecBuilder`, and the `NotificationTypeSpec` defaults/`to_dict`. 39 new + 74 existing integration tests green; ruff clean on all touched files (4 pre-existing ruff errors in `health_assistant_bridge/provider.py` untouched).

- **Docs: full rewrite of `docs/API.md` to match the actual backend (audit `dev/audits/AUDIT-API-2026-07-20.md`).** The public REST API reference documented only **~127 of 298** endpoint handlers (~43% coverage) and several documented routes were wrong. - **Docs: kept `TASK_DEBUGGING.md` as a re-scoped internal reference, deleted `USER_INTEGRATIONS_PLAN.md`, rewrote `TASK_DEBUGGING_GUIDE.md` as a clean reference.** (1) `docs/USER_INTEGRATIONS_PLAN.md` — **deleted** (had been temporarily restored, then dropped on re-evaluation). The doc was actively misleading as a reference: the `UserIntegration` class definition used `provider` (actual column is `domain`), still said `OAuth Credentials (Should be encrypted in a production environment)` (they ARE encrypted via Fernet now — audit B1), the `BaseHealthProvider` interface showed methods that don't match the real SDK in [INTEGRATIONS_SDK.md](docs/INTEGRATIONS_SDK.md), and the 5 API endpoints it listed (`/integrations/{provider}/auth-url`, `POST /wearable/data`, etc.) propagated the **exact same path drifts** the rest of this CHANGELOG entry fixes in `API.md`. The valuable bits (Health Connect / HealthKit on-device push pattern, cloud-vs-device strategy) are already covered in [MOBILE_SYNC_APP.md](docs/MOBILE_SYNC_APP.md) and [INTEGRATIONS_FRAMEWORK.md](docs/INTEGRATIONS_FRAMEWORK.md). Unlike the integrations plan, its content (TaskLogger / TaskProgressTracker / TaskTimeoutMonitor class internals, structured-log JSON schema, error categories, monitoring metrics + alert thresholds) accurately matches the current `backend/app/workers/task_logger.py`. Now opens with a clear "Scope of this doc / Status" header marking it internal (not in docs-tree.json) and pointing at [TASK_DEBUGGING_GUIDE.md](docs/TASK_DEBUGGING_GUIDE.md) as the canonical operator-facing troubleshooting workflow. (3) Rewrote `docs/TASK_DEBUGGING_GUIDE.md` from a postmortem-style narrative (opened with a specific incident: "3 documents stuck for 632 minutes", named filenames) into a clean 6-step reference: background on the task lifecycle + the 10-min/15-min/20-min thresholds, verify worker is alive, verify AI config, read structured logs, retry via API/UI, direct DB inspection; plus a symptom→cause→fix table and a prevention checklist. Two renderable **Mermaid** diagrams replace ASCII art and prose: a `stateDiagram-v2` of the document/examination status machine (uploaded → processing → aggregating → analyzing_text → completed, with failed/retry transitions) and a `flowchart TD` triage decision-tree that routes a stuck task from symptom to the right step (config / file / provider-outage / timeout / unknown → retry or DB-inspect), matching the same Mermaid-first convention already applied to CI_CD_SETUP, NOTIFICATION_SYSTEM, and TELEMETRY_AND_AGGREGATION. Audit `dev/audits/AUDIT-API-2026-07-20.md` items F1/F2/F3 updated accordingly.

- **Docs: replaced ASCII flow diagrams with renderable Mermaid.** The three prose flow diagrams that still used box-drawing characters in code fences — the CI/CD 4-stage pipeline (`docs/CI_CD_SETUP.md`), the notification fan-out model (`docs/NOTIFICATION_SYSTEM.md`: `emit` → `Notification` → `NotificationRecipient` / `NotificationDelivery` → Redis/Celery), and the telemetry→FHIR patient attribution chain (`docs/TELEMETRY_AND_AGGREGATION.md`: `TelemetryDataModel.device_id` → `UserIntegration` → `Patient.user_id`) — are now ` ```mermaid ` flowcharts so they render natively on GitHub and the docs site instead of depending on monospace alignment. File-tree listings (PROJECT_STRUCTURE, EXPORT_IMPORT, FHIR_R4_FACADE) and the UI mockup in TASK_PROGRESS_INDICATOR are intentionally left as plain code blocks — Mermaid has no faithful tree/mockup primitive.

- **Docs: new `CLINICAL_EVENTS.md` reference for the clinical-events type blueprint + seed format.** Previously the `clinical_event_types` seed schema was only documented across scattered mentions in ARCHITECTURE.md, SEEDING_AND_DEMOS.md, and API.md — never as a single canonical reference. The new `docs/CLINICAL_EVENTS.md` covers: the two-layer model (type blueprint vs. instance), the seed JSON envelope with a worked example, every top-level field (slug / name / category_slug / description / icon / color / schedule_kind / metadata_schema + the journey-template fields), the four `schedule_kind` values (`state` / `range` / `recurring` / `point`) and how each renders on the calendar, the `metadata_schema` field-type reference (`text` / `number` / `date` / `boolean` / `catalog-select`) including the validation rules for catalog-select fields (`CatalogType` / `CatalogRelationType` / `concept_kind` constraint), the category system (`event_category` concepts, the always-present system `general-event` fallback), the journey-template analytics fields (`default_duration_days` / `phases` / `milestones` / `severity_scale`), the frontend localization pattern (`events.type.{slug}.*` / `events.category.{slug}.*` i18n keys with backend-string fallback), the bilingual search behavior (English source + current locale), a table of all 9 shipped types, and a step-by-step "add a new type" checklist. Registered in `docs-tree.json` under "Core Systems" with SEO metadata; cross-linked from ARCHITECTURE.md (clinical_event_types + episodes/occurrences lines), SEEDING_AND_DEMOS.md (stage 2 row), API.md (Clinical Events section header), and TAXONOMY.md (the `event_category` ConceptKind row).

- **Fix (documents): PDF / image preview no longer blocked by `X-Frame-Options: DENY`.** The document preview (`AuthenticatedPdf` / `PdfViewer`, rendered as a same-origin `<iframe src="/api/v1/documents/{id}/download?token=...">`) was rejected by the browser because `security_headers_middleware` (`app/main.py`) stamped `X-Frame-Options: DENY` on **every** response unconditionally, including the inline download the preview embeds. The middleware now uses `setdefault` so the `DENY` baseline is preserved for all routes while a route that legitimately needs to be framed can opt out. The document download endpoint (`GET /api/v1/documents/{id}/download`) sets `X-Frame-Options: SAMEORIGIN` **only when serving a file inline** (`should_serve_inline` is `True` — PDFs, images, text; active-content types like svg/html/xml/js stay DENY and are forced to `attachment` anyway, so no clickjacking surface is opened). New regression test asserts the middleware honors an explicit per-route override without dropping the other baseline headers. Audit A7 test still green (the `DENY` default is intact on a normal route).

- **Frontend: PWA-safe in-app detail overlays for picker cards, reusing each entity's source-of-truth view.** The "open" affordance on `InstanceCard` / `CatalogItemCard` (the compact peek cards under `InstancePicker` / `CatalogItemPicker` in `displayMode="cards"`) no longer navigates away — it opens an **in-app overlay** so the form/modal behind it is never interrupted and the standalone PWA never exits to a browser tab (the prior new-tab approach broke the PWA shell on iOS and re-bootstrapped the whole SPA for an internal route). The overlay renders the entity's **existing rich component**, not a stripped variant: a new per-type **detail registry** (`detailViewRegistry`, the overlay counterpart of the browse `viewRegistry`) lets `InstanceCard` dispatch by type — examinations reuse `ExaminationPreview` (full biomarkers/notes/impressions/diagnoses/documents); observations resolve to their biomarker definition and render the same tabs the BiomarkerDetail page uses (`BiomarkerTrendTab` chart + `BiomarkerInfoTab` + `BiomarkerHistoryTab`) plus the extracted `BiomarkerKpiStrip` (Latest Result / Clinical Reference / Avg / Total Records); clinical events reuse `ClinicalEventCard`. Catalog cards already used `CatalogItemInfo`. Unmapped observations fall back to the shared `BiomarkerResultCard`. **Stack-safe `Modal`**: the cards live inside form modals (e.g. `MedicationForm` in `MedicationModal`), so opening an overlay stacks two Modals — Escape now closes only the topmost (resolved by live DOM order of `[data-modal]` panels, robust against React's child-before-parent effect timing) and the focus-trap no-ops when focus is in a child modal; single-modal behavior is unchanged. **DRY extractions**: `BiomarkerResultCard` and `BiomarkerKpiStrip` lifted out of `ObservationView` / `BiomarkerDetail` (both now consume them), and a `useBiomarkerDetailData` hook encapsulates the biomarker+trend load. **Bug fix**: `computeStatus` (`biomarkerUtils`) and the `useBiomarkers` observations path now coerce the FHIR `interpretation` CodeableConcept to a string (`codeableText`) — `getObservation(id)` returns an object where the list endpoint returned a string, which crashed `.toLowerCase()` when opening an observation overlay. Tests: stack-safe `Modal` (single/nested Escape), `InstanceCard` registry-dispatch, and the existing biomarker suites; tsc + eslint clean.

- **Frontend: open-in-detail links on picker cards now open in a new tab (forms aren't interrupted).** `InstanceCard` and `CatalogItemCard` — the compact peek cards rendered under `InstancePicker` / `CatalogItemPicker` in `displayMode="cards"` — already exposed an "open in domain" / "open in catalog" button (the `ExternalLink` affordance), but it navigated **same-tab**, so clicking it from inside a form/modal/detail-editor abandoned the in-progress edit. Both cards now default to opening that link in a **new tab** (`target="_blank"` + `rel="noopener noreferrer"` to prevent tab-nabbing), via a new `openInNewTab?: boolean` prop (default `true`). The prop is threaded through `InstancePicker` and `CatalogItemPicker` and auto-forwarded by `InstanceField` (it spreads `...pickerProps`), so every layer is overridable while the default flows to all callers. This covers every form/edit surface that renders these cards with zero per-form edits: the Record New Medication form (selected medication + linked examination), `MedicationDetail` + `DocumentDetail` (editable examination links), `ExaminationEventModal` (associated events), and `ClinicalEventForm` (related examinations + biomarkers). The existing `InstanceCard` test was strengthened to assert the new-tab default (`target` + `rel`) plus a same-tab opt-out case. Frontend tsc + eslint clean; 151 instance/catalog tests green.

- **Frontend: rich info card for a selected catalog definition (`CatalogItemPicker.displayMode="cards"`).** `CatalogItemPicker` (the search-and-select for catalog items — medication / biomarker / allergy / vaccine / concept / anatomy definitions) previously rendered a picked item only as a compact chip (label + remove). It now mirrors `InstancePicker`'s `displayMode: 'chips' | 'cards'` (+ a `renderCardFooter` slot): in `cards` mode each selection renders a new **`CatalogItemCard`** — the catalog counterpart of `InstanceCard` — that fetches the definition via `/catalogs/{type}/{id}`, caches it by `type:id` for the session, and shows a compact card (type icon + type chip + name + scope badge + open-in-catalog link + remove) whose body is **metadata-driven** via the existing `useFieldDescriptors` / `TYPE_FIELDS` registry, so it auto-adapts to every catalog type: a picked medication surfaces indications / dosage / contraindications / side effects, an allergy shows description / typical reactions, etc. (richtext → one-line snippet, chips → semantic `ChipList`, with a `maxFields` cap; loading skeleton + unavailable-state fallback; `invalidateCatalogItemCard` for cache busting). The Record New Medication form now uses `displayMode="cards"` so the selected medication's info is visible at a glance instead of a bare chip — matching the per-record `InstanceCard` already shown for the form's linked-examination field. The catalog-type → icon map was extracted to a shared `catalogTypeIcons.ts` module (single source of truth) so the new card and the `CatalogItemInfo` pane never drift. Default stays `chips`, so no other `CatalogItemPicker` caller is affected. Frontend tsc + eslint clean.

- **Records: unified instance browser/picker + cross-record linking.** A reusable, registry-driven system for searching and selecting **patient-scoped record instances** (examinations, medications, observations, documents, clinical events, allergies, vaccines) — the patient-records counterpart of the catalog `CatalogItemPicker`. Plan: `dev/plans/instance-browser-unified-picker-2026-07-16.md`. **Backend:** a registry-driven dispatcher `GET /api/v1/instances/search?q=&types=&patient_id=&limit=` (`app/instances/` + `app/services/instance_search_service.py`) fans an `ILIKE` query out across the requested entity types, each search function tenant- + patient-scoped. Security is enforced **centrally in the endpoint** (never per-entity): tenant isolation on every query; `check_patient_access` when `patient_id` is given (404 cross-tenant, 403 for an unlinked `USER`); tenant-wide browse (no `patient_id`) is **ADMIN/SYSTEM_ADMIN only** — `USER` gets 403 (the picker always binds the current patient context, so this is defense-in-depth against enumeration). 14 backend tests incl. the mandatory security cases (USER tenant-wide 403, USER other-patient 403, cross-tenant 404, `q`<2→422, tenant isolation, patient + type filters). **Frontend:** generic, domain-agnostic primitives in `components/instances/` — `InstanceBrowser` (presentational list/grid over a uniform `InstanceRow` projection, sort/search-highlight/picker-mode/Load-more/keyboard-nav), `InstancePicker` (controlled input: debounced type-ahead + Browse button, single/multi, relation binding via the catalog `RelationTypeSelect` reused verbatim), `InstanceBrowseModal` (wraps the existing `useFilterState`/`FilterBar` filter engine + a patient-guard; uses the existing `MasterDetailLayout` shell with a preview pane — list left, generic `InstancePreview` right, rich text via `FormattedText`), `InstanceField`, and a runtime `instanceRegistry`. Seven per-entity adapters (`features/instances/adapters/`) supply fetch (service list + client `q`/patient normalization, since most instance services lack a search param), search (the unified dispatcher scoped to type), facets, and row/selection/route projection; `services/instanceSearchService.ts` wraps the endpoint. **Per-type browse views** (`features/instances/views/` + a `viewRegistry`) let each entity reuse its purpose-built UI instead of the generic list: examinations render the robust `ExaminationCard` list + `ExaminationPreview` master-detail; observations render a biomarker card grid (via `useBiomarkers` + `biomarkerUtils`, trends-style); other types fall back to the generic `InstanceBrowser` + `InstancePreview`. Views are decoupled from the data adapters (registered at app entry) to avoid import cycles. Built entirely on existing primitives — no new filter/modal logic reinvented. **Consolidation:** retired the two genuinely-duplicated bespoke selector modals (`ExaminationSelectorModal` + `ObservationSelectorModal`, each one caller, near-identical) by routing the clinical-event form through `InstanceBrowseModal` (−325 lines); the write-back `ExaminationEventModal` now uses it for selection too (keeping its diff-and-save + per-event reason inputs). **New linking affordances** (where the data model supports it): `DocumentDetail`'s examination link is now editable (link/change/clear via `PATCH /documents/{id}`, was read-only); `MedicationDetail` gained a per-record editable examination link (was set only implicitly at creation); `MedicationForm` gained an optional linked-examination at create/edit. Allergy/vaccine→event linking is deferred — the model has no such link table (events link only to exams/observations/anatomy), and the plan forbids speculative link tables. 38 frontend tests + the 14 backend tests; tsc + eslint + vite build green; ruff clean.

- **AI chat: voice input (speech-to-text) + capability-based model features.** Two coupled changes that rework how models declare what they can do and add hands-free chat input. **(1) Capability-based models:** replaced the implicit "every model is a chat model" assumption with an explicit capability set. A new `AIModelCapability` enum (`text` / `vision` / `audio_input`) is stored as a JSONB `capabilities` array on `AIModel` (migration `s1t2m3o4d5e6`, default `["text"]` so existing models keep their meaning). A single source-of-truth mapping (`app/ai/providers/capabilities.py` `required_capabilities_for_task`) declares what each task needs — `chat`→text, `ocr`→vision, `transcription`→audio_input, every other text-generation task→text — so the AI-config Models UI now shows **feature toggles** (Text is always on; Vision / Audio Input are opt-in chips with icons + colored badges on the list row). A model can be multimodal (e.g. `gpt-4o` = text+vision) or purpose-built (`whisper-1` = audio_input). The `transcription` task type was added to `TaskType`, surfaced in the config summary (`AIConfigSummary.transcription`) + a new `voice_input` workflow, so admins can create a `transcription` task assignment pointing at an `audio_input` model. **(2) Voice input:** a new `POST /ai-assistance/transcribe` endpoint accepts a compressed audio upload, resolves the `transcription` assignment via a new `AIProviderService.get_stt_target` (validates the resolved model advertises `audio_input`; rejects a misconfigured chat-only assignment with a clear guard message), and POSTs it to the provider's `/audio/transcriptions` (OpenAI-compatible) returning `{text}`. Audio is **ephemeral** — never persisted (it may contain PHI); the resulting text is prompt-guard-scanned for audit correlation and then placed in the chat input box for the user to review/edit before sending (it then flows through the normal chat pipeline). Size (20 MiB) + MIME guards at the trust boundary; backend `app/ai/assistance/stt.py` (`STTTarget`, `TranscriptionError`, `transcribe_audio`) + new config (`AI_STT_MAX_AUDIO_BYTES`, `AI_STT_TIMEOUT_SECONDS`, `OPENAI_STT_MODEL`). **Frontend:** `useVoiceRecorder` hook records Opus/16 kHz mono/24 kbps via `MediaRecorder` (~90 KB / 30s — tiny uploads) with a 60s hard cap; `ChatVoiceButton` is a **single unified control** handling both interaction models by gesture — tap (down→up < 250 ms) = toggle (tap to start, tap to stop), press & hold = push-to-talk — with a live elapsed timer and a clear "unsupported/permission-denied" path. Transcribed text appends into the editable input box (preserves typed draft + focuses for review). i18n added (en + el). 12 backend tests (`test_stt_capabilities.py`) cover the capability mapping, baseline inclusion, and STT-target resolution/enforcement; the squash-schema test was relaxed to allow a baseline + incremental follow-ups. Frontend tsc + eslint + build green.

- **AI chat: multimodal image support — ask questions with images.** The agentic chatbot (both the side-panel drawer and the full-screen `/ai-assistant` page) now accepts image attachments so users can ask about lab-report scans, photos, charts, or medication labels. **Backend:** a new modular `app/ai/assistance/attachments.py` is the single source of truth for image handling — an `AllowedImageMime` enum (JPEG/PNG/WEBP/GIF; SVG deliberately excluded as a script vector), `validate_image_data_url` / `validate_chat_images` (MIME whitelist + per-image `AI_CHAT_MAX_IMAGE_BYTES` 8 MiB + per-request `AI_CHAT_MAX_IMAGES` 4 count enforcement at the trust boundary, fail-fast `ImageValidationError` subclassing `ValueError` so it surfaces as a localized guard SSE message with no SDK leak), `build_multimodal_content` (emits the OpenAI vision content-block schema — plain `str` when no images, `[{"type":"text"},{"type":"image_url"}]` otherwise), and `has_images`. `AIAssistanceRequest.images: List[str]` (RFC 2397 data URLs) flows through the `/assist` + `/stream` endpoints; `AIAssistanceService.assist` validates images for the `chat` task only and threads them through `_chat_stream` / `_general_chat`. User messages now persist `{"text", "images": [...]}` in the `ChatMessage.content` JSONB, and `reconstruct_history` rebuilds multimodal `HumanMessage`s for past turns so vision context survives across turns. The chat system prompt gained an "IMAGE & VISION INPUT" rule block (examine images, transcribe values, never fabricate illegible numbers, route "look at my uploaded document" to `get_document_content`). Image bytes bypass the text prompt-injection guard (the HITL wall remains the structural defence for clinical writes). **Frontend:** modular, reusable pieces — `types/ai.ts` gained `ChatImageAttachment` (data URL), a `ChatAttachmentStatus` enum + `PendingChatAttachment` interface for composer state, and `images?` on `Message`; a new `useChatAttachments` hook centralizes client-side validation (mirrors the backend limits so rejected files are never base64-encoded) + `FileReader` data-URL encoding for three input vectors (pick, drag-drop onto the input bar, clipboard paste); `ChatAttachmentPicker` (paperclip button + hidden `<input type=file multiple>`) and `ChatAttachmentPreviewRail` (thumbnail chips with remove + encoding spinner) compose into the modernized input bar; `ChatMessageImages` renders galleries inside bubbles with count-adaptive layouts (single large tile / side-by-side / 1+2 / 2×2 grid with "+N" overflow) and a keyboard-navigable full-screen lightbox. The send button enables image-only sends ("what's this?"), and history reload maps persisted `images` back into the bubbles. 13 backend unit tests (`test_chat_attachments.py`); frontend tsc + eslint + vite build green.

- **Frontend: catalog list rows are now fully clickable + anatomy form unified with the Anatomy Explorer.** Three coupled UX/consistency improvements to the Catalogs workspace and the Anatomy page. (1) In `CatalogBrowser`, each list row and card was selectable only via the inner title/description button — the rest of the row (empty space, the badges column) did nothing. Selection moved to the whole `<li>`/card (cursor-pointer), while the inner interactive elements (class/scope badges, the external-domain link, the picker Add button) keep working independently via `stopPropagation`. (2) Catalogs > Anatomy's create/edit form previously fell back to the bare `GenericCatalogForm` (name + description only), unlike the Anatomy Explorer's `AnatomyStructureForm` (name, slug, category, SNOMED code, description). A new **`AnatomyForm`** is registered in the `CATALOG_FORMS` registry and is now the single shared field set used by **both** surfaces — `AnatomyStructureForm` was refactored to render it. It matches the patterns of the other catalog forms: the anatomy **class** is a `CatalogItemPicker` (`conceptKind="anatomy_class"`, single-select, bound to `class_concept_id`) instead of a legacy uppercase-enum dropdown, and **coding system + code** are two separate fields (`standard_system` select + `standard_code` text) like ConceptForm/BiomarkerForm. (3) Added an **"Open in catalog"** link from both the Anatomy detail card (`/catalogs?type=anatomy&item=<id>`) and the Explorer toolbar (`/catalogs?type=anatomy`) so a structure can be opened/edited in the full catalog workspace. Writes for anatomy now route through the `/anatomy` domain endpoint (not `/catalogs/anatomy`) via a new anatomy entry in the `writeTarget.ts` dispatcher (mirroring how `concept` writes go through `/concepts`), so the class concept is resolved + global-item RBAC enforced by the anatomy service; `buildWritePayload` gained an `anatomy` branch. Dropped the legacy `category` field from the `anatomyService` TS types (`AnatomyListParams`/`AnatomyStructureInput`/`AnatomyStructurePatch`) and the `list()` method — the modern field is `class_concept_id`/`class_concept_slug`; `AnatomySearchPopup` now converts its category filter to a class slug at the API boundary, and `bodyPartService` creates with `class_concept_slug: 'other'`. Frontend tsc + eslint clean.

- **Frontend: catalog Info tab modernized — registry-driven, type-aware structured detail.** The catalog workspace's Info tab (the preview of a selected biomarker/medication/allergy/anatomy/vaccine/concept) was a flat `Object.entries()` dump with mechanically-derived labels and `JSON.stringify` blobs for structured fields. It is now driven by a per-type discriminated-union field registry (`components/catalog/info/fieldRegistry.ts` + `useFieldDescriptors` hook) grouping each catalog type's fields into titled sections (Identity / Coding / Clinical / Safety / Reactions / Schedule / Targets / Presentation / …) rendered by a thin orchestrator. Specialized renderers replace the raw values: `CodeBadge` (LOINC/SNOMED/CVX/ATC/ICD-10/FMA code + system badge + external lookup + copy), `ChipList` (semantic pills for aliases/side-effects/reactions/targets/kinds), `BooleanPill` (flags), `EnumBadgeField` (allergy category, concept status with toned colors), `RefRangesField` (biomarker stratified ranges as a compact table **+ a number-line band**), `DoseScheduleField` (vaccine doses + interval chips), `ColorSwatchField` + `IconPreviewField` (concept color/icon, glyph tinted by the concept color). Six generic, app-wide-reusable primitives were lifted to `components/ui/` (CopyButton, ChipList, CodeBadge, BooleanPill, InfoSection, KeyValueGrid, RangeBar) so biomarker-detail / medication-detail / FHIR views can adopt them later. Interaction additions: a live in-preview **field filter**, a related-summary chip (jumps to the Relations tab), a "Needs attention" completeness badge (missing code/unit/category), Copy-JSON, keyboard shortcuts (`e` edit / `r` relations / `h` history / `Esc` clear, ignored while typing), and a type-icon empty state. i18n keys added to en + el (39). **Zero backend changes** — a Phase-0 payload check confirmed every field was already serialized by the `/catalogs` adapters (incl. expanded `preferred_unit_symbol` + `reference_ranges[]`). Also fixed a Rules-of-Hooks violation the filter introduced (hooks now run before the `if (!item)` early return; a regression test mounts null→item→null) and cleared the pre-existing `react-hooks/exhaustive-deps` warnings in `CatalogWorkspace`. `tsc` + eslint (0 errors) + 350 frontend tests green. Unit-system toggle deferred (payload lacks full Unit rows for client-side conversion); inline single-field edit deferred (the full Edit form + `e` shortcut already cover it). Plan: `dev/plans/catalog-info-preview-modernization-2026-07-16.md`.

- **Database: squashed the migration chain into a single consolidated baseline.** The `alembic/versions/` directory carried 40 incremental migrations (the prior `0001` squash + 39 follow-ups accumulated over ~3 months of refactoring), many create-then-modify-then-drop cycles on the same objects. These are now replaced by **one** deterministic baseline — `8ddb7ef7ca4d_consolidated_baseline.py` — that reproduces the full current schema from an empty database. It was generated via `alembic revision --autogenerate` against the ORM metadata, then hand-augmented with the pieces autogenerate cannot infer: `CREATE EXTENSION` for `pgcrypto`/`pg_trgm`/`timescaledb`; the trigram + FTS tsvector + JSONB GIN expression indexes powering catalog hybrid search; the per-tenant unique indexes on `slug`/`mrn` (`(col, COALESCE(tenant_id, <sentinel>))`), the `concept_edges` dedup unique, and the partial `users.is_service_account` index; the explicit `fk_*` constraint names; and the guarded TimescaleDB hypertable + compression/retention policies + hourly/daily continuous aggregates on `telemetry_data`. The 58 `create_table` blocks are topologically ordered and the `tenants↔users` FK cycle is broken by deferring `tenants.owner_id`; the downgrade is an order-independent `DROP TABLE ... CASCADE`. `UUIDMixin.id` now also declares `server_default=text("gen_random_uuid()")` so DB-level UUID defaults survive (autogenerate had dropped them because the model previously carried only a Python-side default). No in-place upgrade path — existing databases must be dropped and recreated (`alembic upgrade head`); acceptable since the project has no users yet. Verified by `pg_dump` schema diff (functionally equivalent; only cosmetic differences remain — enum value ordering, unique-constraint vs unique-index on one table), an upgrade→downgrade→upgrade round-trip, and the full suite (1975 passed). Tests that hardcoded the old `0001` path/revision (`test_squashed_initial_schema.py`, `test_softdelete_mixin_alignment.py`) were rewritten to validate the new baseline dynamically; `docs/TAXONOMY.md` updated.

- **Seeds (audit B9 / F3): default catalog ships reference ranges, incl. stratified examples.** `data/seeds/default_catalog.json` previously defined 10 biomarkers with **no ranges at all**. It now carries widely-published standard adult reference ranges (marked as illustrative defaults — method-/population-dependent, not clinically authoritative) for all 10, plus **stratified examples** that exercise the resolver: hemoglobin (♂ 135–175 / ♀ 120–155 g/L), HDL (♂ ≥1.0 / ♀ ≥1.2 mmol/L), creatinine (♂ 60–110 / ♀ 45–90 µmol/L), and TSH (pediatric 0–18y 0.7–5.7 vs adult 0.4–4.0 mIU/L). The import pipeline now supports them: `BiomarkerCreate` carries `reference_ranges`, and `CatalogImportService` upserts them **idempotently** by stratification key (sex/age-window/unit) — re-seeding updates bounds in place without duplicating, and deliberately does NOT delete user-added ranges (a clinician's custom rows survive re-seed). Verified end-to-end: a fresh seed produces the expected rows; the dev DB was re-seeded. 3 regression tests (`test_audit_b9_seed_reference_ranges.py`) cover seed validity, range creation, and idempotent upsert + user-range preservation.

- **Frontend (audit B9 / F3): reference ranges editable on create + clearer editor layout.** Two fixes to the stratified-range editor in the biomarker form: (1) it was hidden on first creation (ranges need a parent id, which doesn't exist until the biomarker is saved). The editor is now a **pure draft editor** (stores ranges in the form's draft via `onChange`, makes no API calls itself), so it works identically in create and edit mode; the catalog workspace reconciles the draft against the server after the biomarker is saved via a new `biomarkerService.syncReferenceRanges` helper (POST new / PUT changed / DELETE removed / skip unchanged). (2) The cramped 7-column grid with detached labels was unreadable — each range is now a labelled card (Sex / Age min / Age max / Low / High / Unit) with uppercase field labels and a remove control. Frontend tsc + eslint + 245 tests green.

- **Fix (frontend): typing in a form modal no longer loses focus.** Every entity form (biomarker, patient, doctor, hospital, etc.) lost input focus on each keystroke — after typing one character the caret jumped out of the field. Root cause: `Modal`'s focus-management effect depended on `onClose`, and parents pass an inline `onClose` (`() => setOpen(false)`) whose identity changes every render. Each keystroke re-rendered the parent → the effect tore down (its cleanup restores focus to the pre-modal element, yanking the caret out) and re-ran (re-focusing the first field). Fixed by reading `onClose` through a ref so the Escape handler stays current while the effect is gated on `isOpen` only — focus is now captured once on open and restored once on close. Frontend tsc + eslint + 245 tests green.

- **Frontend (audit B9 / F3): stratified reference-range editor in the biomarker form.** The catalog > biomarkers > create/edit form now supports multiple demographic-specific ranges. A new `ReferenceRangesEditor` (repeating rows: sex / age window / unit / low / high) is shown in **edit mode** and manages ranges via the nested CRUD endpoints (POST on add, PUT on blur, DELETE on remove) — the server stays the source of truth, complementing the draft-based core fields that save through the generic catalog endpoint. Create mode shows a "save the biomarker first" hint (ranges need a parent id). The existing single "Ref. min/max" stays as the resolver's default/fallback range. Backend: the `/catalogs/biomarker` adapter now serializes each item's `reference_ranges` so the form has them on open. New types (`BiomarkerReferenceRange`) + service methods (`list/create/update/deleteReferenceRange`). 1 new backend test for the adapter serialization; frontend `tsc` + eslint clean.

- **Data architecture (audit B9 / F3): reference-range CRUD API + DB-driven `/reference-ranges`.** Completes the stratified-ranges feature with the missing management surface: nested REST endpoints `GET/POST /biomarkers/{biomarker_id}/reference-ranges` and `PUT/DELETE /biomarkers/{biomarker_id}/reference-ranges/{range_id}` (Pydantic `BiomarkerReferenceRangeCreate/Update/Response` with `low ≤ high` + sane age-window validation). Access is **inherited from the parent biomarker** — reads require the parent to be visible (global+tenant), writes are gated by `DEFAULT_CATALOG_POLICY.check_modify` on the parent's scope/ownership (a USER cannot manage ranges for a system biomarker → 403). `BiomarkerResponse` now serializes each biomarker's `reference_ranges`. Retired the hardcoded `GET /analytics/reference-ranges` dict (a parallel source of truth that drifted from the catalog) — it now reads the caller-visible biomarker catalog, and the dead frontend `getReferenceRanges` wrapper (never imported anywhere) was deleted. 7 endpoint tests (`test_audit_b9_reference_ranges_api.py`) cover the CRUD cycle, 404s, validation, the inherited-access model, the response shape, and the DB-driven ranges endpoint.

- **Data architecture (audit B9 / F3): stratified biomarker reference ranges.** `BiomarkerDefinition` carried a single global `reference_range_min`/`max`, which made `relative_score` and the status badge unreliable for anyone outside the "default" demographic (a range normal for a 60-year-old female is not normal for a 25-year-old male). Added a child table **`biomarker_reference_ranges`** holding 0..* ranges each scoped by `sex` / `age_min`-`age_max` / `unit_id` (mirroring FHIR `Observation.referenceRange` with `appliesTo` + `age`), plus a specificity-ranked resolver in **`app/services/reference_ranges.py`** (`resolve_reference_range` / `pick_reference_range` / `resolve_for_patient`) that picks the most-specific applicable row for a patient and falls back to the legacy global range when none matches — so a row constraining a dimension only applies when the patient's value for that dimension is *known* (an unknown age/sex/unit can't be assumed to fall inside a stratified window). Migration `r8b9c0d1e2f3` creates the table (with `low ≤ high` + sane age-window `CHECK` constraints, `ON DELETE CASCADE` from the biomarker) and backfills one catch-all row per biomarker from its legacy bounds. Wired into `analytics_service.get_biomarker_trends` — the user-visible status/range source now resolves by the patient's sex/age instead of the single global range. A shared `compute_relative_score` helper dedupes the scoring math. The legacy columns are retained (display sites + resolver fallback). 15 regression tests (`test_audit_b9_reference_ranges.py`) cover the model/constraints, the resolver's specificity + fallback semantics, DB integration via `resolve_for_patient`, CHECK-constraint enforcement, and CASCADE on biomarker delete.

- **Backend structure (audit C2): fixed the service→router layer inversion.** `clinical_event_service` imported the `check_*_access` helpers from `app.api.v1.endpoints.utils`, coupling the service layer to the router (and to `HTTPException`) — so the service couldn't be reused from Celery, the importer, or the FHIR facade without dragging in Starlette. The seven canonical access helpers (`check_patient/examination/medication/immunization/event/allergy/observation_access`) were moved to **`app/services/access.py`** (they already raise domain exceptions `NotFoundError`/`AuthorizationError`/`ValidationError` post-C1, mapped to HTTP status by the global `DomainError` handler — so the same code is now callable from any layer). The router-layer `endpoints/utils.py` was **deleted**; all 13 importers (11 endpoint modules, the service, and 2 tests) now import from `app.services.access`. The 4 `patch()` targets in `test_examinations.py` were updated to the new module. A new parametrized hygiene suite (`test_audit_c2_layering.py`, 109 checks) forbids any module under `app/services`, `app/ai`, `app/workers`, or `app/facade` from importing `app.api.v1.endpoints`, and pins that `clinical_event_service` and the endpoint modules resolve the helpers from the access module. Suite green (1938; the single unrelated planner-stats test is pre-existing).

- **Data architecture (audit B4): dropped the dead `VersionedMixin.is_current` column.** The audit flagged `VersionedMixin` as "dead data," but on inspection the claim was only half-true: `version` is a *live* feature (the FHIR R4 facade bumps it on every update, reads it for `If-Match` optimistic locking → HTTP 412, and exposes it in the `ETag` header — `test_fhir_r4_versioning.py`), while `is_current` was genuinely never queried anywhere in the codebase. Migration `q7a8b9c0d1e2` drops `is_current` from all 18 tables that carried it (leaving `version` intact); `VersionedMixin` now declares only `version`. The now-unused `Boolean` import and the stale `CatalogItemInfo.tsx` / catalog-adapter readonly-field references were cleaned up. Breaking change is acceptable (no users). 8 new regression tests (`test_audit_b4_versioned_mixin.py`) pin that `is_current` stays gone while `version` survives.

- **Backend structure (audit C9): dropped the stale `_db` filename suffixes.** `documents_db.py` / `document_service_db.py` were named after a long-deleted non-DB predecessor, implying an alternative implementation that no longer exists. Renamed to `documents.py` / `document_service.py` (`git mv` to preserve history); all import paths in `app/` + `tests/` updated. No behaviour change. Suite green.

- **Docs: aligned documentation with the 2026-07-15 audit changes.** `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` documents the `fhir_observations` `patient_id` FK (`ON DELETE CASCADE`) and `document_id` UUID FK (`ON DELETE SET NULL`) (B2/B3). `docs/STATUS.md` gains a "Full-project audit (2026-07-15)" bullet. `docs/API.md`: the `/auth/refresh` response now shows the **rotated** `refresh_token` (A5) + new `POST /auth/logout` and `/auth/logout-all` endpoints; the `429` row is no longer "future" (A2 rate limiting is live); the auth endpoint summary updated. `docs/INSTALL.md` production checklist: rate limiting is built-in (A2) and baseline security headers are automatic (A7). `docs/AI_SYSTEM.md`: `INTEGRATION_SECRET_KEY` is fail-closed in prod (A11), not plaintext-with-warning. Agent skills (`.opencode/skills/`, local) corrected: `clinical-data` (Observation `patient_id` FK, B1 per-tenant unique pattern, B3 facade `?patient=` fix), `backend` (`core/errors.py` C1, `core/converters.py` C8), `project-overview` (D1 + SECRET_KEY gotchas).

- **Backend polish (audits C7 + C10 + B13; B12 verified resolved).** (C7) `SECRET_KEY` and `INTEGRATION_SECRET_KEY` are now proper Pydantic fields (`Optional[str] = None`) instead of `os.getenv(...)` baked in at class-definition time — the latter bypassed Pydantic and made the prod-guard validators untestable (the codebase's own comment flagged this exact pattern for VAPID). The existing dev-ephemeral/prod-refuse validators now work against a real field and accept test overrides. (C10) `process_document_sync` (the FastAPI `BackgroundTasks` OCR fallback when Celery/Redis is down) gained a docstring explaining why a synchronous direct-call path exists and that the name is intentional. (B13) Migration `o6f7a8b9c0d1` adds the `(session_id, created_at)` composite index on `chat_messages` (the chat-session load path is always `WHERE session_id = ? ORDER BY created_at`); the `AuditMixin.created_by`/`updated_by` columns were evaluated as **not worth indexing** (provenance columns, never a `WHERE` predicate → a ~20-table index migration would add write cost with no query benefit). (B12) the `medicationintent` enum case-mismatch is already resolved — the model's `values_callable` emits lowercase labels matching the DB type, confirmed via `alembic check` (no drift); the historical migration's uppercase column declaration is immutable history. Suite green (1822).

- **Backend structure (audit C8): de-duplicated `_uuid()`/`_now()`/`_parse_dt()`.** These three conversion helpers were re-implemented in five service modules (notification_service, notification_targets, notification_rule_service, export_service, import_service, integration_sync_service) — near-identical bodies differing only in which exceptions they caught. Extracted to `app/core/converters.py` as `to_uuid` / `utcnow` / `parse_dt`; each module now imports the shared implementation (aliased back to its private `_uuid`/`_now`/`_parse_dt` name so no call site changes). Behaviour is preserved exactly; the now-unused `datetime`/`timezone` imports were dropped. Suite green (1822).

- **Backend structure (audit C1): domain exception hierarchy + handler.** The service layer had only ~4 domain exceptions and 148 broad `except Exception` blocks; unknown DB errors were too often surfaced as `HTTPException(400, detail=str(e))`. Added `app/core/errors.py` — `DomainError` (base, 500) + `NotFoundError` (404) / `AuthorizationError` (403) / `ValidationError` (400) / `ConflictError` (409) / `ConcurrencyError` (409) — each carrying a safe, client-facing `detail` and a `status_code`. `main.py` registers a single `DomainError` handler that maps each to its HTTP status (logged at INFO as an expected client error, no correlation-id/stack leak). Migrated the canonical access-check helpers (`endpoints/utils.py` `check_patient/examination/medication/immunization/event/allergy/observation_access`) to raise these instead of `HTTPException` (same 404/403/400 contract via the handler), and updated `clinical_event_service` to catch `DomainError` — a first step toward the audit's C2 layer-inversion fix (services will catch domain exceptions, not `HTTPException`). `check_observation_access` now uses the new B3 `patient_id` column (with `subject` fallback). 3 regression tests (`test_audit_c1_domain_errors.py`) cover the hierarchy status codes, the handler mapping, and that the access helpers raise the right domain exception.

- **Data architecture (audit B3): typed `patient_id` FK on Observation + DiagnosticReport.** The patient lived only inside the FHIR `subject` JSONB (`{"reference":"Patient/<uuid>"}`) on `fhir_observations` and `fhir_diagnostic_reports` — forfeiting referential integrity, with no `ON DELETE CASCADE`, and forcing a JSON parse on every per-patient read. `Medication` already had a real `patient_id` FK; this applies the same pattern to the two remaining patient-owned clinical tables. Migration `n5e6f7a8b9c0` adds a maintained `patient_id UUID` column (FK → `fhir_patients.id` `ON DELETE CASCADE`, indexed) to both, backfilled from `subject` only where the referenced patient still exists (dangling `Patient/unknown` / deleted-patient refs stay NULL — the nullable FK permits it). All application write paths now keep `patient_id` in sync with `subject` via a shared `coerce_patient_id` helper (`fhir_service.create_observation`/`create_diagnostic_report`, the OCR pipeline, the import upserters, the telemetry→FHIR backfill worker, and the integration sync sites). `subject` remains the FHIR serialization projection; `patient_id` is the relational source of truth for joins/cascade/scoping. **Bonus bug fix:** the FHIR R4 facade `?patient=` search param now actually filters Observation/DiagnosticReport — `facade/crud._build_resource_filter` keys on `hasattr(model, "patient_id")`, which was a silent no-op before the column existed (the filter returned `None` and was dropped, so `GET /fhir/R4/Observation?patient=<id>` returned every tenant observation). 5 regression tests (`test_audit_b3_patient_id_fk.py`) prove the columns + CASCADE FKs, that both create paths derive `patient_id`, that a patient delete cascades, and the helper handles every reference shape.

- **Data architecture (audit B2): `Observation.document_id` is now a real UUID FK.** It was a free-text `String` that stored a document UUID as text, so deleting a `DocumentModel` left orphan observations with stale references and service code had to compare with `str(obs.document_id) == str(d.id)` because the types never lined up. Migration `m4d5e6f7a8b9` widens the column to `UUID`, nulls malformed/orphan values first (so the upgrade can't fail on a populated DB), and adds `FOREIGN KEY ...
