A new pure-Python `ClinicalEventEngine` (`app/services/clinical_event_engine.py`) derives computed guidance from `(event, type)` with **no DB dependency** — current phase (from onset + phase offsets), upcoming/overdue milestones (absolute or resolved from `event_metadata` via `date_field`), recommended biomarkers (from `BiomarkerEventCorrelation`), and an `is_overdue` flag. Exposed at `GET /clinical-events/{id}/insights`. This is the modular extensibility core: a new journey type = a new JSONB template = new behavior, with no engine code change. 9 pure-Python engine unit tests + 3 real-DB endpoint tests (phase computation, overdue flag, template round-trip).
- **FHIR `EpisodeOfCare` projection — Clinical Events now back two FHIR resources.** A Health-Assistant "health journey" (a 9-month pregnancy, a 2-year dental alignment) is semantically a FHIR `EpisodeOfCare` — *"managing a condition over time, including when the patient is not actively being seen"* — not just a `Condition` (which captures only the problem). The same `ClinicalEvent` row now projects to BOTH: `Condition` via `to_fhir_dict` (the problem) and `EpisodeOfCare` via the new `to_fhir_episode_of_care_dict` (the journey). The two share an id (legal — FHIR ids are per-type) and `EpisodeOfCare.diagnosis[0].condition` references `Condition/{id}` so a client can walk between them. **No new table, no dual-write** — same hybrid-storage pattern. Registered at `/fhir/R4/EpisodeOfCare` with `patient`/`subject`/`status` search (the FHIR status values `active`/`finished`/`onhold`/`planned` translate back to the stored `ClinicalEventStatus` enum via a per-resource `param_filter`). The generic facade dispatcher now honors `ResourceEntry.to_fhir_dict_attr` (previously declared but unused), so one ORM model can back multiple FHIR resources through different projection methods. Reverse converter `fhir_to_episode_of_care_orm` round-trips. Backed by 3 real-DB tests (facade search incl. status translation, round-trip, versioning).
- **`EventAnatomyLink` promoted from dead code to the structured anatomy path.** The `event_anatomy_links` table existed (migration `4f61f50eb0be`) but had no `ClinicalEvent.anatomy_links` relationship, no endpoints, and zero references — anatomy was tracked ad-hoc in `event_metadata.body_part_id` JSONB instead. Phase 3b adds the relationship (cascade delete-orphan), `POST /clinical-events/{id}/link-anatomy` and `DELETE /clinical-events/{id}/unlink-anatomy/{anatomy_id}` endpoints, a `relation_type` discriminator (`primary_site` / `radiates_to` / `referred_to`), an `anatomy_links` field on the event response (with the anatomy name resolved via eager load), and a backfill migration (`f1b2c3d4e5f6`) that promotes every existing `event_metadata.body_part_id` into a real `EventAnatomyLink` row (`relation_type='primary_site'`, `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`). This unifies clinical events with the anatomy atlas already used by the detail page and makes body-site queries first-class.
- **`ClinicalEventOccurrence` model — discrete journey episodes promoted from untyped JSONB to a queryable first-class table.** `ClinicalEvent.occurrences` was a free-form JSONB array (no schema, no per-occurrence integrity, no way to query "all pain episodes with intensity ≥ 8 this quarter" or slice by body site). The new `clinical_event_occurrences` table (migration `f0a1b2c3d4e5`) gives each episode `occurred_at`, `title`, `severity`, `intensity` (1..10), `notes`, an optional `anatomy_id` FK to `anatomy_structures`, and a `metadata` JSONB. New endpoints `POST /clinical-events/{id}/occurrences` and `DELETE /clinical-events/{id}/occurrences/{occurrence_id}` manage them. The legacy `occurrences` JSONB column is retained for one cycle as read-back fallback; migration backfills every existing JSONB entry into a model row, and `to_dict().occurrences` sources from the model when non-empty (falling back to JSONB for rows written through the legacy payload). The occurrence shape is backward-compatible (`date`/`intensity`/`notes` legacy keys preserved) while adding the richer fields. Backed by 3 real-DB tests (CRUD, intensity validation, JSONB read-back).
- **`POST /api/v1/clinical-events/{id}/link-observation` endpoint.** Closes the asymmetry with `link-examination`: observation links were previously only manageable through the create/update full-replace payload. The new endpoint adds a single observation link (with notes) and rejects duplicates, mirroring the examination-link flow. The clinical-event frontend service gains a matching `linkObservationToEvent` call site.
- **Pagination on `GET /api/v1/clinical-events`.** `limit` (default 50, clamped to 200) and `offset` query params replace the unbounded list — previously every list call paid the full deep eager-load chain over all matching events.

### Changed
- **`VersionedMixin` is now active on `ClinicalEvent`.** Each `PUT /clinical-events/{id}` bumps `version` (previously the column was decorative — always 1), and both FHIR projections (`Condition` and `EpisodeOfCare`) emit the real `meta.versionId` instead of a hardcoded `"1"` (it was misusing the row id). This unblocks optimistic locking on the FHIR facade's `If-Match`/`ETag` path for clinical events.
- **Clinical Events: extracted a `ClinicalEventService` as the single mutation chokepoint.** All ~516 LOC of business logic (CRUD, full-replace link sync, soft-delete, lifecycle notifications, the eager-load chain) moved out of the endpoint module into `app/services/clinical_event_service.py`, leaving `clinical_events.py` as a thin HTTP adapter. The canonical eager-load chain (type→category_concept, examination_links, observation_links→biomarker→preferred_unit) is now defined once instead of duplicated in 5 places. `emit_event_notification` lives in the service so the FHIR facade and the import path can route through the same create/update/delete + link-sync + soft-delete + notification semantics as REST (previously each would have had to re-implement them). Backed by 12 real-DB conformance tests (lifecycle, soft-delete, every advertised Condition search param) + 2 Phase-2 tests (link-observation, pagination).

### Fixed
- **Clinical Events: `DELETE` now soft-deletes instead of hard-deleting.** `ClinicalEvent` carries `SoftDeleteMixin`, but `DELETE /api/v1/clinical-events/{id}` called `db.delete(event)` (hard delete) while the FHIR facade (`DELETE /fhir/R4/Condition/{id}`) tombstoned the same row — so deleting via REST permanently removed the row (and CASCADEd its links), destroying the audit trail the facade relies on for `410 Gone`. REST delete now sets `deleted_at`; `list_events` and `check_event_access` filter `deleted_at IS NULL`, so a soft-deleted event 404s from REST too. This unifies the two API surfaces and preserves audit history.
- **5 of 8 advertised FHIR Condition search params silently no-op'd.** `RESOURCE_PARAMS['Condition']` advertised `clinical-status`, `code`, `category`, `verification-status`, and `encounter`, but the generic dispatcher had no real handler for them against `ClinicalEvent` (the projection model): `clinical-status` mapped to a nonexistent `clinical_status` column, `code` ran the JSONB containment path against a `String` column, `category`/`encounter` need joins the dispatcher can't infer, and `verification-status` has no equivalent at all. A FHIR client searching `GET /fhir/R4/Condition?clinical-status=active` got unfiltered results — a conformance violation of the F8 "no advertised param may silently no-op" contract. Fixed: `clinical-status` falls back to the `status` column, `code` honors `String`-column equality (incl. `system|code` form), `category` and `encounter` resolve via per-resource EXISTS-subquery predicates through a new `ResourceEntry.param_filter` extension hook (joins to `clinical_event_types.category_concept` and `event_examination_links`), and `verification-status` is removed from the advertised set. Status/criticality/gender token matching is now case-insensitive via text-cast, fixing an `invalid input value for enum` crash when comparing a PG ENUM column to a lowercase FHIR token. 10 real-DB conformance tests pin every advertised param.
- **Clinical-event lifecycle notifications now fire on resolve and delete, not only on create.** Previously `POST /clinical-events` emitted a `CLINICAL` notification, but status changes (resolving a journey) and deletes were silent. Notifications are now routed through a single `_emit_event_notification` chokepoint (`created`/`updated`/`resolved`/`deleted`), with the resolve transition detected before mutation. Best-effort as before — failures are logged and never abort the parent write.

### Changed
- **Standardized all classification FKs into `concepts.id` on the `<role>_concept_id` naming convention.** The 6 entity tables that classify into the unified taxonomy used 4 different column-name styles — `examinations.category_id` and `clinical_event_types.category_id` hid their target table (read as a reference to a non-existent `categories` table), `biomarker_definitions`/`anatomy_structures` used `class_concept_id`, `doctors` used `specialty_concept_id`, and the relationships were resolved implicitly by SQLAlchemy single-FK guesswork. The two ambiguous columns are renamed to `category_concept_id` (migration `e1f2a3b4c5d6` renames the column + its FK constraint + its index in place, preserving data), the `category_entity` relationship becomes `category_concept`, and **every** concept relationship is now declared with an explicit `foreign_keys=[...]` so resolution no longer depends on there being a single concept FK per table (fragile the day a second is added). Backup import tolerates the legacy `category_id`/`category_details` JSON keys for one cycle alongside the new `category_concept_id`/`category_concept`. See `dev/plans/concept-fk-naming-convention-2026-07-07.md`.

### Fixed
- **`PUT /api/v1/examinations/{id}` returned a stale `category_concept` after a category change.** The endpoint loaded the exam via `check_examination_access` first (eagerly loading `category_concept` as `None`), then mutated `category_concept_id`, then reloaded — but the reload returned the same identity-map instance, and `selectinload` skipped the already-"loaded" relationship, so the response serialized `category_concept: null` (and the `category` name alias) even though the FK was correctly persisted. Fixed by adding `.execution_options(populate_existing=True)` to the post-commit reload so SQLAlchemy overwrites the stale relationship with fresh data.
- **`POST /api/v1/examinations` 500 on response serialization.** After the concept-FK rename, `ExaminationResponse.category_concept` was typed `Optional[Dict[str, Any]]`, but the endpoint returns the ORM `ExaminationModel` whose `.category_concept` is a `Concept` instance — Pydantic cannot coerce a populated ORM object into a bare `Dict` via `from_attributes` ("Input should be a valid dictionary ... input: <Concept object>"). Fixed by typing the field `Optional[ConceptResponse]` (a Pydantic model with `from_attributes=True`); same fix applied to `ExaminationSummaryResponse` and `ClinicalEventTypeResponse`. `ConceptResponse` is safe because `Concept.kind_tags` uses the eager `lazy="selectin"` strategy, so `kinds` is populated when the parent Concept loads (no async greenlet trap during sync serialization). 2 real-DB regression tests pin the contract (exam with + without a category).
- **`documents.category_concept_id` model/DB drift.** Migration `2b4ee2367046` added `documents.category_concept_id` (column + FK `fk_doc_category_concept`) to the database, but `DocumentModel` never declared it — so the live schema had a classification column the ORM did not know about (document classification still ran through the `entities["document_category"]` JSONB path, leaving `documents` inconsistent with every other classified table). The ORM now declares the column + `category_concept` relationship (DB already had it); the migration also adds the missing index. Full population/migration off the JSONB path is tracked as a follow-up. The same migration backfills the missing indexes on the rest of the concept-FK family that the ORM declared (`index=True`) but no prior migration had created: `anatomy_structures.class_concept_id`, `biomarker_definitions.class_concept_id`, `doctors.specialty_concept_id`, `concepts.parent_id`.

### Added
- **Concept-FK naming-convention + drift-detection regression tests** (`tests/test_concept_fk_naming_convention.py`, 13 cases). Pins the contract that every domain-specific FK into `concepts.id` matches `^[a-z_]+_concept_id$` (with `concept_kind_tags.concept_id` and `concepts.parent_id` as the documented owned-child / self-ref exceptions), that every `relationship("Concept")` resolves to a local concept-FK column (the `foreign_keys=` robustness guarantee), that the legacy `category_id`/`category_entity` attributes are gone, and — via a live-DB `information_schema` diff — that the ORM-declared concept columns and the DB-resident ones agree (catches the `documents.category_concept_id` drift class going forward).

- **Download the instance's seeds as a ZIP (UI + dev unpack helper).** A maintainer can now pull the curated taxonomy/anatomy/catalog off a running instance (including one on a different machine) without SSH: a "Seeds" download button on the **TaxonomyManager** page (`/admin/system/taxonomy`, SYSTEM_ADMIN-only) calls `GET /admin/seeds/export.zip` and saves a ZIP of the 9 seed-format JSON files. The download is read-only — the server never writes its own `data/seeds/`. The maintainer transfers the ZIP to their dev machine and runs `python scripts/unpack_seeds_zip.py <zip>` (backs up existing `data/seeds/*.json` to `.backup-<timestamp>/`, refuses unknown/path-traversal entries, then extracts), then reviews with `git diff data/seeds/`. Frontend `seedService.downloadSeedsZip()` mirrors the existing backup-download pattern.
- **Export an instance's data back into the shipped seeds (`SeedExportService` + CLI).** A curator can now build the canonical taxonomy/anatomy/biomarker/catalog set in a running instance via the UI + AI, then snapshot it into `backend/data/seeds/*.json` to replace the hardcoded seeds. New `app/services/seed_export_service.py` is the strict inverse of `SeedService` — one method per seed file — emitting the slug-keyed format (slug is the stable join key; `coding_system`+`code` carried as identity *evidence*, not the key). The CLI `python scripts/export_seeds.py` writes the files through a safety pipeline (stage → back up existing to `.backup-<timestamp>/` → atomic write), so the result is reviewed via `git diff data/seeds/`. Supports `--dry-run`, `--source global|<tenant-uuid>` (export the global taxonomy, or treat a template tenant as the source), `--out DIR`, `--no-backup`. Output is deterministic (sorted by natural key, fixed field order, only meaningful fields, regenerated metadata) so re-exporting an unchanged DB is a git no-op. 16 real-DB tests: per-file round-trip preservation against the shipped seeds, cross-export determinism, scoped export→re-ingest idempotency, the lossless-field guard, the backup/atomic pipeline, and the CLI surface.
- **Lossless seed read-side: anatomy `class_concept_slug` + biomarker concept-edge endpoints.** The seed ingest now reads `class_concept_slug` on `anatomy_structures.json` (preferred over the legacy ~8-value uppercase `category` enum), so anatomy whose class concept is outside the legacy set (e.g. a niche "lymphatic-structure" class) round-trips instead of silently falling back to "other-anatomy". The concept-edge ingest resolves a `biomarker` endpoint type by `BiomarkerDefinition.slug`, unblocking biomarker-level edges beyond panel membership. Both are backward compatible (legacy-only seed items keep working).
- **Backup export/import now carries the taxonomy + anatomy.** ZIP backups (`ExportType.FULL_BACKUP`) include three new sidecars so tenant-private customizations travel with the backup and survive a restore: `concepts.json` (tenant-scoped concepts + their multi-kind tags), `anatomy.json` (tenant-scoped body-part structures + the relations between them), and `concept_edges.json` (the polymorphic knowledge-graph edges — specialty→organ, biomarker→panel `MEMBER_OF`, AI-approved relationships). Import restores them in dependency order (concepts → anatomy → biomarkers/exams → edges) with UUID id-remapping: FK-bearing rows (examination `category_id`, biomarker `class_concept_id`, anatomy `class_concept_id`, edge endpoints) relink to the target's rows. References to global/seeded concepts that were deliberately not exported resolve by slug fallback against the target's re-seeded taxonomy. Edges with an unresolvable dangling endpoint are skipped with a warning rather than aborting the import. Restores are idempotent (upsert by slug / by natural key) so re-importing the same backup is a no-op. The `gather_anatomy` export is strictly tenant-scoped (`tenant_id == tid`) — it never leaks another tenant's `is_custom` anatomy. 17 new real-DB round-trip tests in `tests/test_export_import_taxonomy.py`.
- **Multi-kind concepts (taxonomy consolidation, part 2).** A concept can now carry multiple domain tags — "Blood Laboratory" is simultaneously an `examination_category`, a `biomarker_class`, and a `document_category` — instead of existing as 3 unrelated rows. The single-valued `concepts.kind` column is replaced by a many-to-many `concept_kind_tags` join table (reusing the existing `conceptkind` PG enum) plus a denormalized `primary_kind` column for cheap single-badge rendering. Migration `9a3f7c2e1b4d` is a pure schema change (create join table + `primary_kind`, backfill both from the legacy `kind`, swap the unique index from `(kind, slug, tenant)` → `(slug, tenant)`, drop `kind`); the 16 legacy duplicate concepts are de-duplicated in the seed data (`concepts.json`: 68 → 54 items), which is the single source of truth — the migration assumes a greenfield/empty concepts table (per the prior `consolidate_categories` note) and carries no hardcoded merge table. The new `concepts_with_kind()` helper replaces every legacy `Concept.kind ==` filter across 10 consumer files (services, AI pipeline, endpoints); `resolve_concept_by_slug` keeps its `kind` param (now an optional join-table filter) so resolvers needed no caller changes; `create_concept` accepts `kinds: List[ConceptKind]` (legacy single `kind` still wrapped for backward compat). Pydantic schema emits `kinds: List[str]` + `primary_kind`; the create endpoint accepts either `kinds: [...]` or legacy `kind`. `biomarker_category_to_concept_slug` drops the now-obsolete `-class` suffix. 6 new multi-kind model tests + updated concept/service/API/seed/taxonomy-tool tests; the dedup also fixed 3 previously-failing seed idempotency tests. Frontend (types, TaxonomyManager, ConceptGraphView) lands next.
- **Biomarker catalog auto-seeding.** `seed_default_catalog()` loads `data/seeds/default_catalog.json` (units + biomarker definitions) at startup via `CatalogImportService`, resolving the empty-catalog issue. Runs AFTER `seed_concepts` so `biomarker_class` concepts exist for `class_concept_id` resolution. **Biomarker panel memberships** (`seed_biomarker_panels()`) creates `MEMBER_OF` edges from biomarkers to panel concepts (e.g. LDL → Lipid Panel) from `data/seeds/biomarker_panels.json`. Both wired into `main.py` startup.
- **FHIR observation category on concept meta_data.** The `_BIOMARKER_CONCEPT_TO_FHIR_CATEGORY` and `_BIO_FALLBACK_FHIR_CATEGORY` hardcoded dicts in `persistence.py` are replaced by `meta_data["fhir_observation_category"]` stored directly on each `biomarker_class` concept in `concepts.json`. The FHIR mapping is now editable via the TaxonomyManager UI and lives with the concept (single source of truth). The `_fhir_observation_category()` function takes the concept object directly.
- **Unified taxonomy — Phase 7 (frontend).** Management UI and reusable components for the concept layer: `TaxonomyManager.tsx` — generic CRUD page with a domain switcher (all 16 ConceptKind values), inline editor with color/icon/alias/coding-system fields, icon picker from the Lucide catalog; `<TaxonomyTypeahead>` — server-backed debounced search component for picking concepts in forms (replaces free-text inputs); `conceptService.ts` — typed API wrapper for all /concepts + /concept-edges endpoints; `types/concept.ts` — full TypeScript types. Route: `/admin/system/taxonomy` (SYSTEM_ADMIN); `/examinations/categories` now renders TaxonomyManager. Sidebar item under Administration. Broken `examinationService` + `clinicalEventService` category functions repointed from the dropped endpoints to `/concepts?kind=examination_category` and `/concepts?kind=event_category`. TypeScript build + ESLint clean.
- **Unified taxonomy — Phase 6 (AI chatbot tool).** New `taxonomy` domain tool module auto-wired into the agentic chatbot via `@register_chat_tool("taxonomy")`: `search_concepts(search_term, kind)` — ranked trigram + alias search over the concept layer; `get_concept_neighborhood(concept_id, relation)` — one-hop graph traversal; `get_entity_concepts(entity_type, entity_id, relation)` — "what panels is this biomarker in?" / "what specialty does this doctor have?". All tools are live-read-only (AI never writes; proposals go through HITL). 4 tool tests including alias matching and error handling.
- **Unified taxonomy — Phase 5 (consolidation).** Drops the 4 old scattered category/group tables (`examination_categories`, `clinical_event_categories`, `biomarker_groups`, `biomarker_group_members`) and consolidates all category vocabulary into the unified `concepts` table. Migration `2b4ee2367046`: adds `class_concept_id` FK to `biomarker_definitions` + `anatomy_structures`, `specialty_concept_id` to `doctors`, `category_concept_id` to `documents`; repoints `examinations.category_id` + `clinical_event_types.category_id` FKs to `concepts.id`; drops old free-text/enum `category`/`specialty` columns; drops old tables. All 17 consumer files updated: `analytics_service` (clinical_groups from concept_edges), AI pipeline (`resolve_category` → concepts, form fillers), endpoints (examinations/clinical_events/biomarkers), schemas, export/import, seed service. Deleted `ExaminationCategory` model + endpoint + schema. 101 tests passing.
- **Unified taxonomy — Phase 4 (seeds).** Curated seed data for the concept layer: ~60 concepts covering 9 domains (specialties, body systems, examination categories, event categories, biomarker classes, biomarker panels, anatomy classes, document categories, ATC medication classes) + ~19 concept↔concept edges (specialty EXAMINES body_system, specialty PERFORMS examination_category, ATC class hierarchies via PART_OF). Idempotent upsert by `(kind, slug)` for concepts and `(src, dst, relation)` for edges; parent_slug resolution for hierarchical concepts. Integrated into startup seeding (`main.py` lifespan). 4 seed idempotency tests.
- **Unified taxonomy — Phase 3 (API endpoints).** REST endpoints for the concept layer: `GET/POST /concepts`, `GET/PUT/DELETE /concepts/{id}`, `GET /concepts/search?q=&kind=`, `GET /concepts/{id}/neighbors` (one-hop graph traversal), `GET/POST/DELETE /concept-edges`. Full RBAC enforcement (SYSTEM_ADMIN for global rows; ADMIN for tenant-scoped; USER read-only), tenancy filtering, and validation. Pydantic v2 schemas (`ConceptCreate/Update/Response`, `ConceptEdgeCreate/Response`, `NeighborResponse`). 11 HTTP integration tests covering CRUD, search, edge creation, neighbor traversal, RBAC (USER 403 on write, USER 200 on read), and validation errors.
- **Unified taxonomy — Phase 2 (service layer + search).** `ConceptService` provides full CRUD for concepts + edges with RBAC enforcement (SYSTEM_ADMIN for global rows; ADMIN for tenant-scoped; USER read-only), tenancy filtering (`or_(tenant_id == tid, tenant_id.is_(None))`), soft-delete-with-retire-if-referenced lifecycle, one-hop neighbor traversal, and entity→concept lookup ("what panels is this biomarker in?"). AI-proposed edges land as `status=PROPOSED` and are invisible to graph queries until approved. `search_concepts()` added to `catalog_search_service` — trigram + ilike + JSONB aliases containment, optionally filtered by `kind`, excludes retired/deleted. 20 real-DB integration tests covering CRUD, RBAC, tenancy isolation, edge validation, neighbor traversal, proposed-edge lifecycle, and ranked search.
- **Unified taxonomy / knowledge-graph foundation (Phase 1).** Introduces two new tables that form the backbone of a consolidated medical vocabulary system: `concepts` (controlled-vocabulary nodes for specialties, examination/event/biomarker/anatomy/document categories, biomarker panels, medication classes, diseases, body systems, etc.) and `concept_edges` (typed polymorphic edges between concepts and/or domain entities — `MEMBER_OF`, `EXAMINES`, `PERFORMS`, `TREATS`, …). This replaces the scattered `examination_categories`, `clinical_event_categories`, `biomarker_groups` tables and free-text `category` columns (consolidation migration follows in a later phase). Six new enums (`ConceptKind`, `ConceptStatus`, `ConceptProvenance`, `EdgeApprovalStatus`, `EdgeEndpointType`, `ConceptRelationType`). `coding_system` is a free string (not enum) to support open-ended terminology systems (LOINC, SNOMED, ATC, ICD-10, CVX, MeSH). Trigram GIN index on `name`+`slug` powers ranked search; JSONB GIN on `aliases` enables containment matching. Unique partial indexes use `COALESCE(tenant_id, sentinel)` to correctly handle global (NULL-tenant) rows. Migration `1a3dd1256035`.

### Fixed
- **Export/import jobs stuck in "Processing" forever (completed_at type bug).** `ExportService.complete_job`/`fail_job` and `ImportService._complete_job`/`_fail_job` passed `datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()` — a **string** — into the `completed_at` column (`TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE`). asyncpg rejects strings (it needs a real `datetime`), so the export/import actually succeeded (the ZIP was written) but the DB update marking the job `COMPLETED` crashed, and the fallback `fail_job` crashed the *same way* — leaving the job stuck in `PROCESSING` permanently and the UI never showed an error. Now passes the `datetime` object directly. 3 new real-DB regression tests cover `complete_job`/`fail_job` (the mocked export tests had skipped these, which is why it slipped through).
- **Biomarker class link (`class_concept_id`) was silently dropped on every backup round-trip.** The export emitted the concept *name* (e.g. `"Blood Laboratory"`) in the legacy `category` field, but the import's `biomarker_category_to_concept_slug` only swaps `_`→`-`, turning that name into `"blood laboratory"` (with spaces) which never matched the real slug `"blood-laboratory"` — so `class_concept_id` resolved to `None`. The export now also emits `class_concept_slug` (the canonical concept slug) and `CatalogImportService` resolves that ahead of the legacy name→slug path. The ontology-catalog-URL import (whose JSON uses the underscore convention `blood_laboratory`) is unaffected.
- **Examination category (`category_id`) was exported but never restored.** The `examinations.json` sidecar carried `category_id` + `category_details`, but `_restore_examinations` ignored both — imported exams always came back uncategorized. It now relinks the category (via the concept id-remap, with slug fallback to the target's re-seeded global taxonomy) and also restores the previously-dropped `organization_id`, `source_integration_id`, `external_id`, and `auto_extract_metadata` fields.

### Changed
- **Examination detail toolbar consolidated into an Actions dropdown.** The previously separate *Upload Results*, *Run AI Analysis*, *Edit*, and *Delete* buttons on the examination detail page are now grouped under a single **Actions** dropdown (`MoreVertical` trigger), decluttering the sticky toolbar. Each item retains its prior behaviour and iconography (Add Results / Take Photo on mobile, Full AI Reconstruction, Fast AI Extraction, Edit Details, Delete); the `ExaminationAIActions` (summarize/findings/analysis) button stays separate, and Save/Cancel still surface inline when global editing is active.
- **Repository tab "Include in AI" toggle now matches the FileCard style.** Both the list-view and grid-view document toggle in the examination Repository tab adopt the same subtle indigo chip used on the new-examination document `FileCard`: a `Sparkles` icon with gradient "AI Extract" / muted "AI Off" label on a translucent indigo/grey background (replacing the solid blue `Cpu` button). Added `aria-pressed` + accessible titles.
- **Category selector in Smart Extraction (single) mode.** The new-examination form now shows a **Category** picker (same `CategorySelector` + inline `AIAssistButton` as manual mode, with "Optional — AI will auto-extract if not set" hint) when Smart Extraction AI is enabled but Bulk Create is off. Previously the category was hardcoded to `Clinical` in smart mode; the create payload now sends the user's choice (or `undefined` so the backend auto-extracts).
- **Docs: seed export workflow + schema cheatsheet.** `docs/SEEDING_AND_DEMOS.md` gains §7 "Exporting an instance back to seeds" (identity model, the three delivery surfaces — UI button / `export_seeds.py` CLI / `unpack_seeds_zip.py` — the cross-machine transfer workflow, source scope, the anatomy-markers caveat). `docs/DEVELOPMENT.md` Seed System section adds the export/unpack scripts. The `seeding` skill gains a "Seed export (inverse)" subsection so future sessions know `SeedExportService` exists. New `backend/data/seeds/README.md` is a per-file field-schema cheatsheet (every seed file's required/optional fields + enum values, verified against the ingest code) plus the edit/export workflows.
- **Docs refresh: install/dev/seed.** INSTALL.md's first-time-seeding section now reflects that the full catalog (anatomy + taxonomy + default biomarker catalog) auto-seeds via `SeedService.seed_all()` on every startup — the standalone `seed_default_catalog.py` / `seed_anatomy.py` CLIs are no longer required for setup. DEVELOPMENT.md documents `scripts/reset-dev-db.sh` (wipe + restart the dev Postgres/Redis volumes) and adds a Seed System section covering `seed_all()`'s declarative stage ordering, the standard `{metadata, items}` envelope, the `{added, updated, skipped, errors}` stats contract, and per-stage re-seed. SEEDING_AND_DEMOS.md gains a §0 Seed Pipeline table + fixes the anatomy section for the `anatomy_structures.json`/`anatomy_relations.json` split (54 nodes + 62 edges; new `seed_all` log shape; manual re-seed via the service method, not the expansion-pack CLI).
- **Unified notification system — Phase 5 (role-based admin Notification Center).** Completes the notification system with an admin/system console. New `GET /notifications/admin/stats` endpoint aggregates delivery metrics (counts by source, category, and per-channel delivery status; cross-tenant for SYSTEM_ADMIN). A new `AdminNotificationCenter` component surfaces stat cards, a broadcast composer (tenant-scoped for ADMIN/MANAGER; system-wide cross-tenant for SYSTEM_ADMIN, gated accordingly), and a live admin feed. It appears as a role-conditional "Admin" tab in the Notification Center, visible only to ADMIN/MANAGER/SYSTEM_ADMIN — giving each role its appropriate scope (system admin sees cross-tenant + can broadcast system-wide; tenant admin sees/manages their tenant; regular users see only their personal inbox). i18n keys added for `en`/`el`.
- **Unified notification system — Phase 4 (source wiring).** The remaining notification sources now flow through the unified `emit()` pipeline. **HITL proposals**: the 6 AI propose-tools (`propose_create_clinical_event`, `propose_add_medication`, etc.) now emit an `AGENT`/`HITL_TASK` notification to the chatting user, so pending AI proposals surface in the notification inbox even after the chat is closed (with an "Open chat" action). **Integrations**: `integration_sync_service.run_sync` emits an `INTEGRATION_EVENT` to the integration owner when new wearable/lab data arrives, and a `SYNC_FAILURE` (warning) to the owner + tenant admins on auth/data errors (rate-limit and skip outcomes stay silent). **System broadcasts**: new `POST /admin/notifications/broadcast` endpoint — `ADMIN`/`MANAGER` broadcast to their tenant, `SYSTEM_ADMIN` may broadcast system-wide or target another tenant. **Clinical events**: creating a clinical event emits a `CLINICAL_EVENT` notification to the care team. The `ToolContext` gained a `user_id` field (threaded from the chat entry points) so HITL notifications can target the chatting user.
- **Unified notification system — Phase 3 (biomarker rules UI + allergy naming fix).** A new biomarker-rules builder lets users create custom biomarker-limit notifications ("get alerted when glucose > 140" or "out of normal range"): a searchable biomarker picker (showing each biomarker's normal range), a condition (operator + threshold or "out of normal range"), multi-recipient targeting (any combination of patients and doctors — a notification can be assigned to multiple recipients, not one-to-one), severity, and a per-rule cooldown to prevent alert storms. Existing rules can be enabled/disabled, edited, deleted, and test-fired. The builder is a new "Biomarker Rules" tab in the Notification Center. Rules are evaluated event-driven on observation create (Phase 1 backend). Separately, the misleadingly-named `/alerts` page (which actually showed allergies) is renamed `ClinicalAlerts` → `AllergyAlerts`, with the sidebar label updated to "Allergy Alerts" — freeing the "alerts" name for the biomarker-alert system. i18n keys added for `en`/`el`.
- **Unified notification system — Phase 2 (real-time delivery + user-scoped inbox).** The notification bell is now real-time and user-scoped: a new `/ws/notifications` WebSocket streams each user's notifications from a per-user Redis channel (`user:{id}:notifications`) authenticated via the `["bearer", token]` Sec-WebSocket-Protocol subprotocol, replacing the previous 30-second patient-scoped poll. The bell now works **without a patient selected** (so system/tenant notifications surface), renders severity dots, action buttons (deep-link to the relevant resource), and category icons for all notification types (reminder/alert/hitl/agent/system/integration/clinical_event), and shows a live/reconnecting indicator. The Notification Center page (`/notifications`) is rebuilt with Inbox / All / Reminders tabs, category + status filters, mark-all-read, and dismiss. The frontend `notificationService` and `notificationStore` are rewritten around the Phase 1 fan-out model (inbox items, optimistic read/dismiss, live-event handler). A new `useNotificationStream` hook manages the WebSocket lifecycle (auto-reconnect with backoff + fallback unread-count poll if the socket can't open). The service worker's obsolete `/notifications/{id}/delivered` PATCH is removed (delivery status is now tracked server-side by the push delivery worker). i18n keys added for `en`/`el`.
- **Unified notification system — Phase 1 backend (fan-out model).** The notification subsystem is rebuilt around a 3-table fan-out architecture: one immutable `Notification` event (with `source`/`category`/`severity`/`type`, nullable `patient_id`/`tenant_id` for system/tenant broadcasts), `NotificationRecipient` (per-user inbox state: unread/read/dismissed), and `NotificationDelivery` (per-recipient per-channel delivery log). A single `notification_service.emit()` entry point now produces every notification — it resolves target specs (`USER`/`PATIENT`/`DOCTOR`/`TENANT`/`SYSTEM`) into concrete user ids, fans out recipients + deliveries, optionally links a FHIR `Communication` for clinical sources, publishes to a per-user Redis channel, and enqueues push delivery. The orphaned `AlertModel` is replaced by `NotificationRule` (operator + value + biomarker + multi-recipient targets), evaluated **event-driven** on observation create (`fhir_service.create_observation` → `notification_rule_service.evaluate_and_fire`) with per-rule cooldown. New endpoints: `/notifications/inbox`, `/unread-count`, `/{id}/read|dismiss`, `/read-all`, `/notifications/admin` (tenant/cross-tenant feed), and `/notification-rules` CRUD + `/test`. The `deliver_notification` worker task now iterates per-recipient deliveries (dead-subscription pruning preserved). The legacy `/alerts` endpoints, `AlertModel`, and the dead `biomarker_update` event trigger are removed. Schema folded into the squashed `0001` migration (no backfill — greenfield). **Frontend (real-time bell, Notification Center, rule builder) lands in Phase 2.**
- **FHIR facade tenant bridge: service-account auth + X-Tenant override (F19, G10).** External systems can now connect to the FHIR facade (`/fhir/R4/*`) with a service-account JWT (minted by admins via `POST /auth/service-account`) instead of a user password. The CapabilityStatement documents both auth modes. `SYSTEM_ADMIN` can scope into any tenant via the `X-Tenant: <uuid>` header. Provenance records the external system identity (`client_id`) as a third agent entry on service-account-initiated writes. This is the stepping-stone before full SMART-on-FHIR (F1) — deferred to Stage 4.
- **Service-account JWT auth for external systems (F19).** New `POST /auth/service-account` endpoint (ADMIN/MANAGER/SYSTEM_ADMIN only) creates a password-less machine account (`is_service_account=True`) and returns a long-lived JWT carrying `is_service_account=True` + `client_id=<instance_name>`. The token works as a Bearer against the FHIR facade (`/fhir/R4/*`) and the REST API. Service accounts are bound to one tenant (the JWT's `tenant_id`). `TokenData` gained `is_service_account` + `client_id` fields. `/auth/login` now rejects service-account emails (403). `UserModel.hashed_password` is now nullable (service accounts have no password). Migration `f19a2b3c4d5e` adds the `is_service_account` column with a partial index. This is the tenant-bridge stepping-stone before full SMART-on-FHIR (F1) — external systems can now connect with a bearer token instead of a user password.
- **Push resilience: per-row 401-race retry, cursor integrity, batch isolation.** Three robustness fixes: (1) Push now retries once after a 401 race (token expired between the `get_live_token` check and the PUT) via `force_refresh` — mirroring the pull path's `_authorized_search` pattern. Previously a 401 mid-batch aborted the entire push. (2) The `last_pushed_at` cursor now only advances past *successfully* pushed rows (tracks the max `updated_at` among created/updated outcomes). If ALL rows fail, the cursor stays unchanged → full retry next cycle. Previously the cursor advanced to `now` unconditionally, so transiently-failed rows were never retried (silent data loss). (3) Per-row error isolation — one bad row counts as `error` and the batch continues; only `insufficient_scope` (H1) aborts the batch early.
- **Outbound push now POSTs a Provenance to the remote server (H3).** Hospitals typically require this for regulatory audit ("Health Assistant pushed this from integration X"). After each successful push (PUT 201/200), `_push_one` POSTs a Provenance with the remote Observation id as the target, the local Device as the agent, and a CREATE activity code. Best-effort: Provenance failure (server doesn't support it, network error) is logged and never aborts the push. The push result carries `provenance_created`/`provenance_failed` counters. New `fhir_create` (POST) primitive added to `sdk/fhir.py` alongside the existing `fhir_conditional_update` (PUT).
- **Outbound push requests write scope when push is enabled (H1).** `DEFAULT_SCOPES` was read-only (`patient/*.read`); a spec-strict SMART server rejects `PUT /Observation` with 403. New `PUSH_SCOPES` adds `patient/*.write`; `begin_oauth` passes `push_enabled` when `sync_direction` is `both` or `push_only`. The config-flow description documents that switching to push requires re-authorizing. 403 `insufficient_scope` is now detected — the push stops and the result carries an actionable "re-authorize with write permissions" warning instead of silently failing every row.
- **Error messages now include parsed FHIR OperationOutcome diagnostics.** `parse_operation_outcome` existed but was never called on any error path — all integration SDK raises used raw `response.text[:300]`, making hospital 422/400 rejections hard to debug. Both `fhir_conditional_update` and `http_request` now extract `OperationOutcome.issue[].diagnostics` (the most useful field — e.g. "code system https://loinc.org not recognized") before falling back to the raw body.
- **Outbound push: multi-component observations (blood pressure) + multi-range referenceRange + note preservation.** `fhir_observation_to_create` previously returned `None` for any observation lacking both `valueQuantity` and `valueString` — silently dropping blood pressure (the most common vital, which uses `component[]` for systolic + diastolic) and panels (BMP, CBC). The early-return now checks for `component[]` — these observations survive and their components are mapped onto the `Observation.component` JSONB column (added in Phase 6). `note[0].text` is mapped to the ORM `comment` field. Additionally, `_extract_reference_range` (renamed from `_convert_reference_range`) now returns the full canonical `referenceRange[]` list instead of flattening only the first range to `{min, max}` — multi-range observations (age-stratified, gender-specific) preserve all ranges with `type`/`appliesTo`/`text`/units intact.
- **OAuth hygiene: atomic state consume, 429 fix, token revocation, DCR guard.** Four robustness fixes in the integration SDK auth layer: (1) `OAuthStateStore.consume` now uses `GETDEL` (Redis ≥ 6.2) for a truly atomic read-and-delete — the old GET+DELETE had a TOCTOU race where duplicate OAuth callbacks could consume the same state. (2) The token-endpoint 429 response is now correctly classified as `IntegrationRateLimitError` (was `IntegrationAuthError` — rate-limited token endpoints would pause the integration instead of retrying). (3) `SmartOAuth.revoke(integration)` calls the SMART `revocation_endpoint` (RFC 7009) on disconnect — `DELETE /instance/{id}` now revokes tokens before deleting, preventing stale tokens on hospital servers. Best-effort: network errors are swallowed. (4) If a SMART server advertises a `registration_endpoint` but DCR returns no `client_id`, the flow now raises an actionable `IntegrationAuthError` instead of silently producing an authorize URL with an empty `client_id`.
- **Integration sync pipeline consolidated into shared `run_sync` helper.** The pull → convert → biomarker-map → telemetry-split → push → log pipeline was previously copy-pasted across 4 call sites (the Celery worker, the manual-sync endpoint, the webhook path, and the bridge provider). It now lives in a single `IntegrationSyncService.run_sync(integration, db, provider, *, source)` method that both the worker and the manual-sync endpoint delegate to. The shared helper also acquires the Redis dedup lock internally — fixing a race condition where the manual-sync endpoint didn't respect the worker's lock (concurrent Sync Now + beat could double-write). The 3-tier error contract (`IntegrationAuthError` → status=ERROR; `IntegrationRateLimitError` → retry; generic → log) is now uniform across both sites. The manual-sync endpoint returns HTTP 409 when a sync is already in progress (lock held), 401 on auth failure, 429 on rate limit, 500 on other errors.
- **`Observation.component` JSONB column added (prereq for H2 push).** The FHIR R4 `Observation.component` (`0..*`) — used by multi-component observations like blood pressure (systolic + diastolic) and panels (BMP, CBC) — is now a first-class JSONB column on the ORM model (migration `i7b8c9d0e1f2`, with a GIN index for future `component-code-value-*` search). The import converter (`fhir_to_observation_orm`), `_upsert_observation` (create + update paths), `to_fhir_dict()`, and `to_dict()` all carry it. The `ObservationCreate`/`Update`/`Response` schemas accept `component: Optional[List[Dict]]`. Without this column, the push path (H2, Phase 7) could not emit `component[]` because push reads `obs.to_fhir_dict()` which projects from ORM columns. **DB migration required** (`alembic upgrade head`).
- **`Observation.interpretation` now stores the canonical FHIR R4 list shape (was a flattened string).** The column type changed `String → JSONB` (migration `i6a7b8c9d0e1`) with a backfill that wraps legacy plain-string rows in `[{"text": value}]`. The import path (`fhir_to_observation_orm`), REST create path (`fhir_service.create_observation`), and OCR persistence path all normalize any input (string, list, or None) to the canonical `0..* CodeableConcept` list via the new `_normalize_interpretation` helper. The round-trip import → ORM → `to_fhir_dict()` now preserves the LOINC/OBSINT coding (previously collapsed to a lossy display string). `to_dict()` (frontend projection) still flattens to a single display string via the existing `_flatten_interpretation` helper, so the frontend contract is unchanged. **DB migration required** (`alembic upgrade head`).
- **`validate_and_filter_observations` no longer mutates the caller's list.** The FHIR write-time gate previously did `observations[:] = valid` (in-place mutation), so callers that held a reference to the original list silently saw a shorter list with no signal that items were removed. It now returns `(valid, dropped_count)` and leaves the input untouched. **Breaking API change** for any out-of-tree caller that relied on the in-place mutation — switch to unpacking the returned tuple.
- **FHIR Bundle import: reference routing + cross-tenant collision warnings.** Two import-correctness fixes: (1) `_apply_remap` no longer misroutes bare `urn:uuid:` references — an `Observation.encounter` given as `urn:uuid:abc` now correctly maps to `Encounter/<new>` (was silently mapped to `Patient/<new>`). A new `FIELD_HINT_TO_TYPE` map covers all reference-bearing fields (`subject`/`patient`→Patient, `performer`/`author`→Practitioner, `partOf`→Organization, `context`/`encounter`→Encounter, `device`→Device, `specimen`→Specimen); ambiguous hints (`sender`/`recipient`) are resolved by a bundle look-ahead (`{id → resourceType}` index built once per bundle). (2) `_resolve_id` no longer silently creates a new row when a bundle id exists in another tenant — the collision is now surfaced as a warning in the ImportJob result (e.g. `"Patient/<id> already exists in tenant <other>; created new with id <new>"`).
- **FHIR Bundle import now records a Provenance per entry (bulk-import audit trail).** Previously bulk imports left no audit trail of who imported what — only the `ImportJob` row itself tracked the importing user, with no per-resource Provenance. Each created/updated/deleted entry now records a Provenance via `record_provenance` (best-effort, never aborts the import). The Provenance carries the entry's resource type + id, the `CREATE`/`UPDATE`/`DELETE` activity code, the importing user as the agent, and an `ImportJob/<id>` reference in `entity_inputs` so bulk-import Provenance is distinguishable from facade-write Provenance. `restore_fhir_bundle` gained `actor_user_id` + `source_job_id` params (threaded from the job-driven import paths).
- **FHIR Bundle import now supports all 15 resource types (was 7).** The import dispatcher previously handled only Patient, Observation, MedicationStatement, AllergyIntolerance, DiagnosticReport, Organization, and Practitioner — silently dropping MedicationRequest, Condition, Encounter, Device, Communication, and Provenance on every bulk import (the `_TO_ORM` converter map already had converters for all 15; only the dispatcher branches were missing). All 15 non-DocumentReference types now import correctly: Condition → ClinicalEvent, Encounter → Examination, Device → DeviceModel, Communication → CommunicationModel, Provenance → ProvenanceModel (immutable — existing rows are not overwritten, counted as an idempotent no-op). MedicationRequest delegates to the same Medication table as MedicationStatement (distinguished by the `intent` discriminator). Genuinely-unsupported types (anything outside the FHIR R4 resources we model, e.g. `Coverage`) now surface a warning instead of being silently dropped.
- **FHIR Bundle import now honors `entry.request.method` + `ifNoneExist` (transaction-integrity fix).** Previously every entry in a posted Bundle was treated as POST (create-new) — a bundle authored as a transaction with `{"request": {"method": "PUT", "url": "Observation/<id>"}}` silently became a brand-new observation with a server-generated UUID, losing round-trip integrity with third-party EHR / SMART transaction Bundles. The import path now routes on the verb: `PUT` updates an existing same-tenant row or creates one **with the URL's id** (not a random uuid); `POST` + `ifNoneExist` performs a conditional create (skipped when a match exists — Patient `identifier` → `mrn` lookup today, unsupported forms log a warning and create rather than silently treat "couldn't match" as "no match"); `DELETE` soft-deletes (idempotent on missing id); `POST` (or no request block) keeps the historical create-new behaviour. **Breaking API change:** `ImportService.restore_fhir_bundle` now returns a `BundleRestoreResult` dataclass (attribute access: `.created` / `.updated` / `.deleted` / `.skipped` / `.errors` / `.warnings` / `.id_remap`) instead of the previous 5-tuple. Internal callers + `scripts/seed_demo.py` updated; any out-of-tree caller unpacking the old 5-tuple must switch to attribute access.
- **FHIR R4 facade: honest versioning + If-Match optimistic locking.** The CapabilityStatement per-resource `versioning` is now honestly `"no-version"` (we don't implement `vread` / `history-instance` / a version-history table). `If-Match` optimistic locking is now implemented: a PUT with `If-Match: W/"3"` against a version-2 row returns HTTP 412 Precondition Failed (RFC 7232). Garbage If-Match values are silently ignored (FHIR lenient on ETag form). The `VersionedMixin.version` column is still bumped on update and exposed in the ETag header. `vread` + `history-instance` remain deferred. Location header on create uses the spec-correct short form `<base>/Type/<id>` (allowed for `versioning="no-version"`; the versioned form is only required when `vread` is implemented).
- **FHIR R4 facade: `Provenance.agent.who` now references real FHIR resource types.** Previously `agent.who.reference` used `User/<id>` and `Integration/<id>` — neither is a FHIR resource, so external clients resolving the reference got 404. The agent block is now async and resolves both actor types via DB lookups: `user_id → Practitioner/<doctor.id>` (via `DoctorModel.user_id`, mirroring the F11 fix) and `integration_id → Device/<device.id>` (via `DeviceModel.owner_integration_id`). When resolution yields nothing (admin/manager with no Doctor row; orphan integration with no Device row), the agent is emitted in display-only form `{"display": "..."}` — spec-compliant and logged as "degraded" so audit-trail gaps are identifiable.
- **FHIR R4 facade: `DocumentReference.author` now resolves to a real Practitioner.** Previously `to_fhir_dict()` emitted `Practitioner/<owner_id>` but `owner_id` is a `ForeignKey` to `users.id` (User id, not Doctor id) — external FHIR clients resolving the reference got 404. Added a nullable `documents.practitioner_id` column (FK to `doctors.id`, `ON DELETE SET NULL`), backfilled from the existing owner→doctor mapping at migration time. `to_fhir_dict()` now emits `Practitioner/<practitioner_id>` when set and **omits** `author` entirely when NULL (rather than emit a wrong reference). The upload path (`document_service_db.upload_document`) and the edited-copy path both resolve the Practitioner id from the owner at upload time via a new `_resolve_practitioner_id` helper. Admin/manager uploads (no Doctor row) get no `author` reference rather than a wrong one.
- **FHIR write-time validation gate now covers every clinical write path.** Previously 4 service-layer write paths bypassed `assert_valid_fhir` (doctor/organization/medication/document services), so invalid FHIR could be persisted via the REST endpoints even though the facade and `fhir_service.*` were gated. All 4 services now call `assert_valid_fhir(obj)` right before `commit()`, mirroring the existing gate pattern: `doctor_service.create_doctor`/`update_doctor` (Practitioner), `organization_service.create_organization`/`update_organization` (Organization), `medication_service.create_catalog_medication`/`update_catalog_medication`/`add_patient_medication`/`update_patient_medication` (Medication + MedicationCatalog), `document_service_db.upload_document` + the edited-copy path (DocumentReference). Closes the audit's FHIR validation gate coverage table — every row now reads ✅.
- **FHIR R4 facade: `_elements` projection honored and `_format=xml` explicitly rejected.** `_elements` (comma-separated list of top-level fields) is now applied as a post-serialization projection in search results, keeping the requested fields plus the always-present `resourceType` / `id` / `meta` per FHIR R4 spec. `_format=xml` (and `application/fhir+xml`, RDF, TTL) is now explicitly rejected with a 400 OperationOutcome — previously silently returned JSON which was misleading. JSON-family formats (`json`, `application/json`, `application/fhir+json`) are accepted case-insensitively. `_include` / `_revinclude` chained search remain deferred (parsed but not yet executed).
- **FHIR R4 facade: Bundle entries now carry `search.mode`** (`"match"` for primary results, `"include"` for `_include` resources). Strict R4 clients expect this on every Bundle entry.
- **FHIR R4 facade: `_summary=count` and `_total` are now honored.** `_summary=count` (or `_summary=true`) returns a Bundle with an empty `entry[]` and the `total` (the main SELECT is skipped — cheap "how many match?" queries). `_total=none` skips the COUNT(*) query entirely AND omits the `total` key from the Bundle (default remains `_total=accurate` for backward compat).
- **FHIR R4 facade: search-param coverage now matches advertisement.** Following the F4 "advertise only what's implemented" principle: the dispatcher now honors the commonly-used subset of search params (previously accepted-but-silently-dropped), and the long-tail unimplemented params are removed from `RESOURCE_PARAMS` so they're no longer advertised in the CapabilityStatement. Newly-implemented: `value-quantity` (numeric comparator with FHIR prefix matrix), `performer`/`sender`/`recipient`/`agent`/`target`/`partof`/`parent`/`author` (JSONB reference containment with bare-UUID type hints), `criticality` (scalar enum), `medication` (delegates to the `code` column), `activity` (Provenance CodeableConcept), `identifier` (universal JSONB `{system,value}` containment), `name`/`family`/`given` (text-cast ILIKE on the JSONB name blob), `gender`/`active` (scalar tokens). Removed (not advertised): `Condition.severity`, `Encounter.class/reason-code/diagnosis/practitioner`, `Device.manufacturer/model`, `Medication.form`, `Provenance.entity`, `DocumentReference.author` (returns when F11 lands).
- **FHIR R4 facade: token / category search now uses JSONB `@>` containment semantics.** Three sub-bugs fixed: (1) `code` search previously inspected only `coding[0]` — multi-coding resources (e.g. an Observation carrying both a LOINC and a SNOMED coding) silently missed. The new helper `_jsonb_codeable_concept_match` builds a `@>` containment predicate so a CodeableConcept column matches the supplied fragment anywhere in its structure. (2) `category` search previously did `model.category.astext == value` against `Observation.category` which is a **list** of CodeableConcepts — the comparison matched nothing. The dispatcher now detects JSONB-list columns and emits a list-wrapped `@>` fragment (so any element matches); scalar enum columns like `AllergyIntolerance.category` keep the simple equality. (3) The `:not` token modifier (e.g. `code:not=1234-5`) is now parsed and negates the match. Other modifiers (`:above`/`:below`/`:in`/`:text`) and chained-reference search remain deferred. The `type` param (DocumentReference/DiagnosticReport) was previously unimplemented and now uses the same `@>` path.
- **FHIR R4 facade: date search now honors FHIR precision semantics.** Previously `_parse_fhir_datetime("2024")` was treated as exact `2024-01-01T00:00:00Z` instead of the whole-year range per the FHIR R4 spec. Date search now uses precision-aware ranges: year (`2024`) → `[2024-01-01, 2025-01-01)`; month (`2024-05`) → `[2024-05-01, 2024-06-01)`; day (`2024-05-15`) → `[2024-05-15, 2024-05-16)`; full datetime → exact instant. The full FHIR prefix matrix (`eq`/`ne`/`gt`/`ge`/`lt`/`le`/`sa`/`eb`/`ap`) is interpreted against these ranges (`eq2024` matches any instant in 2024; `gt2024` matches 2025+; etc.). Also fixes a DRY violation: the date branch in `crud._build_resource_filter` (the resource-specific filter builder) now routes through `DateFilter.to_orm_filter` (the same code path `_lastUpdated` uses), so the prefix matrix can no longer drift between the two implementations. Fixed a greedy day-precision branch that was silently truncating the time component of full datetime strings like `2024-05-15T13:30:00Z`.
- **FHIR R4 facade: sort columns now map to real ORM columns and align with filters.** Three corrections: `Condition?_sort=onset-date` now sorts on `onset_date` (previously referenced a non-existent `fhir_onset_datetime` column); `MedicationRequest?authored-on` sort now uses `created_at` to match the same-named filter (previously the filter used `created_at` while sort used `start_date` — they disagreed); and `Patient?_sort=name` now sorts by lowercase family name via a JSONB path expression (`LOWER(COALESCE(name -> 0 ->> 'family', name ->> 'family'))`) that handles both the list-of-HumanName (FHIR canonical) and single-HumanName-dict (legacy) storage shapes — previously it sorted by JSONB blob byte representation, so 'Smith' sorted before 'adams'.
- **FHIR R4 facade: pagination links now work end-to-end.** Previously the search Bundle's `first`/`last`/`previous`/`next` links carried a non-standard `_offset=<n>` query param while the parser only honored `page=N`, so following the `next` link always landed on page 1 (any non-trivial dataset was unreadable via standard pagination). The links now emit spec-standard `page=N` (matching HAPI / Vonk); the parser also accepts `_offset` on input as a tolerant alias so legacy links and clients that send `_offset` keep working.
- **FHIR R4 facade: CapabilityStatement now advertises only what's actually implemented.** Previously it falsely advertised system-wide `batch`, `transaction`, `history-system`, `search-system` interactions, a `/$validate` operation, and per-resource `versioning=versioned` / `updateCreate=true` — none of which the facade implements (POST to `/fhir/R4` is treated as create-one; no `/_search`, no `/_history`, no `vread`, no `history-instance`; PUT to a missing id returns 404). All false claims stripped. Per-resource `versioning` is now honestly `no-version`; `updateCreate` is `False`. This unblocks strict R4 conformance validators (Inferno/Touchstone) that fail servers advertising unimplemented capabilities. (`CapabilityStatement.rest.interaction`, `operation`, per-resource `versioning`.)
- **FHIR R4 facade: `CapabilityStatement.date` is now generated dynamically** at every `/metadata` call instead of being hardcoded.
- **FHIR R4 facade now advertises the correct FHIR version (`4.0.1`).** The CapabilityStatement previously declared `"fhirVersion": "4.3.0"` (R4B) while the path was `/fhir/R4/`, which fails strict R4 validators (Inferno, Touchstone). `FHIR_VERSION` is now `"4.0.1"` to match the path. Validation of the resources we emit continues to use the `fhir.resources` library (its R4B subpackage, since 8.x dropped its R4 subpackage); R4B is a backward-compatible superset of R4 for every field our models project, so the validator accepts exactly the FHIR JSON we produce while we advertise R4 honestly to clients.
- **DB-driven anatomy atlas with admin image management.** The hardcoded frontend atlas is replaced by an `anatomy_figures` table where each row is one view of one figure (e.g. `man-front`, `woman-back`) backed by a **WebP image** on disk under `UPLOAD_DIR/anatomy_figures/`. New `/api/v1/anatomy/figures` endpoints: `GET` (list), `GET /{slug}/image` (serves the WebP via `FileResponse`), and `POST`/`PATCH`/`DELETE` (SYSTEM_ADMIN only, multipart upload). New **Atlas Manager** admin page (`/admin/anatomy-atlas`) to create/edit/delete figures with an **interactive image cropper** — upload a source image, drag to select the view region (real pixel crop via canvas → WebP), live preview, no coordinate math. Adding new views (left side, right side) or figure groups is entirely through the UI.
- **Per-figure marker coordinates.** Organ markers are keyed by figure slug (`display.map.markers["man-front"]`) and normalized 0–1 against the image's pixel dimensions, so each figure owns an independent coordinate space. The PositionEditor and AnatomyExplorer pick a figure (grouped by figure_key → views). Existing markers were migrated (migration `b3d4e5f6a7c8`).
- **Modular Anatomy Graph Ontology.** Replaced the flat `body_parts` table with a directed-graph ontology (`AnatomyStructure` nodes + `AnatomyRelation` edges). 9 categories (SYSTEM, REGION, ORGAN, ORGAN_PART, TISSUE, CELL, SUBSTANCE, JOINT, OTHER) and 7 relation types (PART_OF, BRANCH_OF, DRAINS_INTO, ARTICULATES_WITH, INNERVATED_BY, SUPPLIED_BY, CONTINUOUS_WITH). Optional standard identifiers (SNOMED CT, LOINC, CUSTOM). Base seed of 54 nodes + 67 relationships ships with the application and is seeded automatically on startup.
- **Anatomy Explorer UI.** New `/anatomy` page with a custom 2D SVG body map (front/back views, clickable regions), searchable popup with category icons and SNOMED badges, organ location preview, and an interactive relationship graph (reactflow) showing parents/children/connections. Category filter chips and fullscreen graph modal.
- **Anatomy JSON Import API.** `POST /api/v1/anatomy/import` (SYSTEM_ADMIN) accepts JSON expansion packs with `nodes` and `edges` arrays. Slug-based upsert (never deletes), edge deduplication. Enables specialized deployments to import custom anatomy sub-graphs (e.g., detailed ophthalmology or neuroanatomy packs).
- **AI-Driven Anatomy Graph Generation.** New AI task type `define_anatomy_graph` and chatbot tool `propose_anatomy_graph_generation` allow the AI assistant to generate anatomical sub-graphs on demand via a human-in-the-loop review card.
- **Body Location in Clinical Events.** The Clinical Event form now includes a dedicated body location field (with AnatomySearchPopup + inline OrganPreview) visible for all event types. The Clinical Event detail page shows an organ location visualization section with a link to the Anatomy Explorer.
- **EventAnatomyLink.** M2M table bridging `ClinicalEvent` and `AnatomyStructure` for future graph-based clinical event queries.
- **Anatomy Position Editor.** SYSTEM_ADMIN-only drag-and-drop editor (Positions button on the Anatomy Explorer) for placing organ markers on the body silhouette. Markers auto-save normalized coordinates; front/back view is tagged automatically from drop position. The canonical way to fix or add a structure's map position — no pixel math or JSON editing.
- **Anatomy i18n.** Full `anatomy` translation namespace (EN/EL), including category and relation labels (Organ, Tissue, Part of, Branch of, …) and the explorer/editor UI strings.
- **`scripts/setup_env.py` now generates VAPID keys and prompts for the contact email.** A fresh `python scripts/setup_env.py` run produces a fully-configured Web Push section in `.env` with zero further operator action: a P-256 key pair (`VAPID_PUBLIC_KEY` / `VAPID_PRIVATE_KEY`) is generated using the existing `cryptography` dependency (no Node.js / `npx web-push generate-vapid-keys` needed), and Full Setup mode asks for `VAPID_ADMIN_EMAIL` with a smart default derived from the entered `APP_URL` hostname (`https://health.example.com` → suggests `admin@health.example.com`; `http://localhost:*` → falls back to `admin@example.com`). The user can accept the default (Enter) or override. Keys Only mode still generates the key pair but leaves `VAPID_ADMIN_EMAIL` commented (the config.py placeholder default applies — fine for dev, where missing VAPID keys are tolerated anyway). Closes the loop on the VAPID prod-guard (see *Changed* below): a fresh prod install now goes from `python scripts/setup_env.py` → `docker compose up` with Web Push working end-to-end.

### Changed
- **Patient REST schema now accepts FHIR R4 list cardinality.** `PatientCreate`/`PatientUpdate` fields `name`, `address`, `telecom` changed from `Optional[Dict[str, Any]]` (single object) to `Optional[List[Dict[str, Any]]]` to match FHIR R4 `0..*` cardinality. Posting canonical FHIR JSON like `{"name": [{"family": "Doe", "given": ["John"]}]}` previously returned 422; it now succeeds. Single-dict payloads are correctly rejected (the ORM column still tolerates legacy single-dict rows via `_coerce_*` read-side helpers). `PatientCreate`/`PatientUpdate` are not used by any current endpoint, so no caller breakage.
- **VAPID keys now required in production.** `VAPID_PUBLIC_KEY` / `VAPID_PRIVATE_KEY` env vars must be set when `APP_ENV != "development"`; the app refuses to boot otherwise. The fields were also changed from `os.getenv(...)` (which bypassed pydantic and baked in the value at class-definition time) to plain `Optional[str] = None`, so the existing `SECRET_KEY` / `INTEGRATION_SECRET_KEY` prod-guard pattern now applies to them. In development, missing keys continue to be tolerated (Web Push silently skipped). Operators running `scripts/setup_env.py` don't need to do anything extra — the wizard generates both keys and prompts for `VAPID_ADMIN_EMAIL` automatically (see *Added* above).
- **Lifespan startup is now fail-fatal in production.** Catalog seeding (medications, allergies, clinical event types, body parts, anatomy figures) and integration-registry initialization previously failed silently with a log line — the app would boot half-initialised with no medication/allergy catalog. In production (`APP_ENV != "development"`), these failures now re-raise after logging so the app refuses to boot; development retains the fail-soft behaviour. Stuck-extraction cleanup remains best-effort in both modes.
- **Worker DB engine consolidated to a worker-scoped singleton.** Celery tasks previously created a fresh `AsyncEngine` per invocation; the engine is now a single lazy-init singleton per worker process using `poolclass=NullPool`. Tasks do `db, engine = get_async_session()` → `await db.close()` in `finally`; `engine.dispose()` is never called per task (the engine is disposed on `worker_process_shutdown`). This eliminates the intermittent `RuntimeError: Event loop is closed` / `Future attached to a different loop` crashes on `check_notification_triggers`, `sync_active_integrations`, and other periodic tasks.
- **Anatomy figures switched from SVG to WebP.** SVG viewBox cropping was fundamentally broken (viewport zoom, not a real crop; width/height/viewBox mismatch stretched renders; SVG presentation attributes triggered browser CSS warnings). Replaced with raster WebP images: the crop editor produces a real pixel crop via `<canvas>`, the stored image IS the view, and the marker overlay's viewBox matches the image dimensions by construction — eliminating the entire class of alignment bugs. The four default figures ship as bundled WebP seeds (14–25 KB each, rasterized at 3× from the Wikimedia surface diagrams, CC BY-SA 3.0). Frontend Zustand store (`useAnatomyAtlas`) fetches figure metadata + authenticated image blobs lazily.
- **AnatomyExplorer figure picker.** The ♂/♀ gender toggle and Front/Back view toggle are replaced by a single grouped `<select>` listing all active figures.
- **AI subsystem reorganized under `backend/app/ai/`.** All AI/LLM code (previously scattered across `app/services/ai_*.py`, `app/processors/`, and `app/schemas/ai_*.py`) now lives under a single `app/ai/` package, split by concern: `providers/` (config + factory + enums/registry), `processors/{ocr,nlp}/`, `pipeline/` (extraction orchestration + persistence + ontology), `agents/` (the agentic-chat reasoning loop, HITL helpers, prompts), `tools/` (the chatbot tools split by domain + the integration aggregator), `assistance/` (form-fillers/definitions/icons), and `schemas/`. The three near-duplicate chat reasoning loops (`_chat_stream`, `resume_after_hitl`, `_general_chat`) collapsed into one `run_reasoning_loop(...)` in `agents/chat_agent.py`; AI Celery tasks moved to `workers/ai_tasks.py`. Internal refactor — no user-facing behaviour change and no public API break — but developers should update import paths. Notable mappings: `services/ai_assistance_service` → `ai/assistance/service`, `services/medical_processing_service` → `ai/pipeline/service`, `services/ai_chatbot_tools.ChatbotTools(...).get_tools()` → `ai.tools.get_tools(...)`, `services/integration_tool_aggregator` → `ai/tools/aggregator`, `schemas/ai_{nlp,assistance,config}.py` → `ai/schemas/{nlp,assistance,config}.py`. Branch `refactor/ai-services`.
- **Anatomy Explorer overhaul.** The page now follows app conventions: decoupled `PageHeader` (title/subtitle/icon render in the global header), `PageContainer`, shared `LoadingState`, full i18n, URL deep-linking (`/anatomy/:slug`), debounced server-side search (`?search=`), category-filter dimming on the relationship graph, a landing overview (systems grid + total count), and an "Add custom structure" form (uses the existing `POST`/`PATCH`/`DELETE` endpoints). `bodyPartService` is now a thin adapter over `anatomyService` (single source of truth for `/anatomy`).
- **Anatomy body diagram is now data-driven and figure-independent.** Replaced the hand-coded SVG silhouette with the Wikimedia "surface diagram" assets (male + female, CC BY-SA 3.0 — see `NOTICE`). An atlas registry (`frontend/src/components/anatomy/atlas.ts`) declares figures + per-view crop regions; adding a figure is one asset + one registry line. Organ markers use **normalized 0–1 coordinates** stored per-figure (`display.map.markers.man` / `.woman`) under a new JSONB `display` column (migration `39fffbc136ce`), so positions are resolution-independent and each body is positioned independently. Front/Back toggle crops the viewBox and filters markers; ♂/♀ gender toggle swaps the figure. The base seed ships male markers; female markers are added via the editor.
- **`GET /api/v1/anatomy` supports `?search=`** (ilike on name/slug/standard_code/description) and now orders by name. Added `PATCH`/`DELETE` `/api/v1/anatomy/{id}` for editing/removing structures (global structures require SYSTEM_ADMIN).
- **Unified AI badges.** Every AI surface now uses a single `<AIBadge>` convention: the default renders the gradient **"AI"** label + an **info icon** that opens the transparency popover (active model, provider + country flag, Local/Cloud, privacy notice, medical disclaimer); a custom `label` is shown only where it adds meaning (e.g. "Proposal", "Suggested Unit"). The trigger is now a real `<button>` (keyboard-accessible: Enter/Space toggle, Esc closes + restores focus, `aria-expanded`/`aria-haspopup`), with a new `size="sm"` variant for tight headers. Converged the ad-hoc indicators that previously rolled their own icons/text/tooltips — biomarker "AI Suggested Unit", HITL "AI Proposal" (Card + Modal, formerly a `Bot` icon with no tooltip), the Magic Fill modal header (had no AI marker at all), and the "AI Insights"/"AI Interpretation"/"AI Agent Capabilities" section titles — onto `<AIBadge>`. Standardized AI action-trigger icons to `Sparkles` (the lone `Wand2` outlier in the category manager is gone). Wired the previously-dead `ai_labels.magic_fill_ai`/`smart_extraction_ai` keys and moved the remaining hardcoded AI strings (incl. EN/EL) behind i18n; `ai_chat.hitl.proposal_label` shortened from "AI Proposal" to "Proposal" since the badge now carries the AI signal.

### Fixed
- **Celery periodic tasks crashed intermittently with `RuntimeError: Event loop is closed` / `Future attached to a different loop`.** Root cause: each task's `get_async_session()` created a fresh `AsyncEngine` with its own connection pool, and the `@async_task` decorator created a fresh `asyncio` event loop per task. asyncpg connection protocol transports bound to a previous task's loop resurfaced in subsequent tasks via SQLAlchemy's pool, hitting a closed loop. Fix: the engine is now a worker-scoped singleton using `poolclass=NullPool` so no DB connection is ever reused across loops; engine disposal is wired to Celery's `worker_process_shutdown` signal rather than per-task. Live production outage observed on `check_notification_triggers` (2026-06-27).
- **`relative_score` was never computed for OCR-sourced observations.** Every OCR-sourced observation had `relative_score = NULL`, silently disabling the biomarker engine's scoring feature (`_get_observation_status` step 2 in `analytics_service.py` was dead code for OCR data; everything fell through to the hardcoded `STANDARD_RANGES` dict). `save_observation` (in `app/ai/pipeline/persistence.py`) now computes it using the same formula as the integrations SDK's `ObservationBuilder.build()`: `(value - ref_min) / (ref_max - ref_min)` clamped to `[0.0, 1.0]` when both bounds are present with `max > min`; incomplete range (only one bound) → `0.5`; no range → `NULL`.
- **`normalized_value` had two bugs in the OCR persistence path.** (1) Skip-condition: it was only computed when the biomarker had a preferred unit *different* from the matched raw unit; auto-created biomarkers (no preferred unit) kept raw_value, mixing units across labs in trend history. (2) Wrong direction: `val_float * matched_unit.conversion_multiplier` converts raw → base SI, but the result was labelled as-preferred. Fixed: `normalized_value` is now always expressed in the biomarker's preferred unit (`raw → base → preferred`), falling back to base SI when no preferred unit is set so trends stay consistent across labs.
- **`MedicationCatalog` / `AllergyCatalog` dedup used substring matching.** The uniqueness check `Catalog.name.ilike(name)` treated `_` and `%` as wildcards, so `"Vitamin_B12"` would silently match an existing `"Vitamin-B12"` (underscore matches any single char) and skip the insert. Switched all 5 dedup sites (`ai/pipeline/ontology.py`, `seed_service.py` ×2, `import_service.py` ×2) to `func.lower(Catalog.name) == func.lower(name)` for strict case-insensitive exact match. Catalog *search* features (legitimate substring `ilike('%q%')`) are unchanged.
- **Cumulative extraction was triggered even when all OCR documents produced empty text** (blank pages, OCR failures). The else branch of `_check_trigger_cumulative` fired `cumulative_extraction.delay(...)` "anyway to handle metadata if needed", wasting an LLM call and producing hallucinated or empty impressions. The else branch now marks the exam completed (`extraction_status="completed"`, `impressions=""`) and skips the LLM call entirely.
- **Web Push dead subscriptions accumulated forever.** `webpush_service.send_web_push` swallowed every `WebPushException` including the 410 Gone / 404 Not Found cases that RFC 8030 specifies as "subscription permanently dead", returning `False`. The caller couldn't distinguish transient failure from permanent death, so dead rows in `notification_subscriptions` stayed `is_active=True` and every PUSH cycle re-attempted them. `send_web_push` now raises a new `SubscriptionExpired` exception on 410/404; `deliver_notification`'s PUSH loop catches it and marks the matching `NotificationSubscription.is_active = False`.
- **`doctors.py` list endpoint leaked internal exception text.** The handler was wrapped in a `try/except Exception` that did `print(...)` + `traceback.print_exc()` + re-raised as `HTTPException(500, detail=str(e))`, bypassing the global exception handler. The wrapper is removed; the global handler now logs with a correlation id and returns a sanitized 500.
- **`check_observation_access` raised `AttributeError` → HTTP 500** when an observation's `subject` JSONB dict had no `"reference"` key (`.get()` returned `None`, then `None.split()` raised). Now defensively coerces via `(observation.subject or {}).get("reference", "")` so an absent reference yields `""` and the downstream surfaces a clean 400.
- **Anatomy tests failed on second run** (`UniqueViolationError` on `anatomy_structures.slug`). `anatomy_structures.slug` has a globally-unique constraint (anatomy is an ontology — heart is heart in every tenant), but tests used stable slugs like `"test-heart"` and the suite has no per-test transaction rollback. Rows accumulated across runs in different tenants created by the per-call `system_admin_headers` fixture. Added an autouse module-level fixture that deletes from `anatomy_structures` before each test (CASCADE handles `anatomy_relations` + `event_anatomy_links`). The tables aren't seeded by migrations — the only data in them during tests IS test data — so truncating is safe.
- **"Create New" dropdown hidden behind the sidebar.** The CreateMenu popup (New Examination / New Medication / etc.) is rendered via a portal at `document.body`, but its `z-index` (200) was lower than the sidebar container's (`z-[950]` in `Layout.tsx`). Since the layout root doesn't establish its own stacking context, the sidebar painted over the portaled dropdown. Bumped the dropdown to `z-[1000]` so it now correctly floats above the navigation sidebar.
- **Anatomy SVG assets failed to open in XML editors** with "XML declaration allowed only at the start of the document" and undeclared namespace-prefix errors. The `<?xml ?>` declaration was moved above the license comment, and orphaned Inkscape/RDF metadata blocks (using stripped `sodipodi:`/`rdf:`/`cc:`/`dc:` prefixes) were removed. Both files now validate as well-formed XML with zero errors.

### Fixed
- **Notification periodic task crashed with "Future attached to a different loop".** `check_notification_triggers` delegated to `NotificationManager.process_due_triggers()`, which opened its own session via the global pooled app engine (`AsyncSessionLocal`, `pool_pre_ping=True`). In a Celery prefork worker that engine's asyncpg connections are bound to the master's (already-closed) event loop, so the pool's pre-ping checkout raised `RuntimeError: Future ... attached to a different loop` and teardown raised `RuntimeError: Event loop is closed` — scheduled/recurring medication reminders intermittently failed to fire. The task now owns a worker-scoped `NullPool` session (via `get_async_session()`, the same pattern as `sync_active_integrations`) and injects it into `process_due_triggers(session=...)` / `fire_notification(session=...)`. A failed trigger now rolls back the shared session so the remaining triggers in the cycle still process. Request-path callers are unchanged (they fall back to the app engine).

## [0.3.0-rc.6] - 2026-06-26

### Added
- **Customizable bind addresses for deployment.** Gitea ``deploy.yml`` now supports ``BACKEND_BIND``, ``FRONTEND_BIND``, and ``FLOWER_BIND`` via Gitea Repo Secrets (defaulting to ``127.0.0.1`` for local-only security). This allows multi-VM architectures where a reverse proxy on a different VM connects to the application services over a private interface.
